_Thought for 1m 42s_

## Agent 4 / D — Prime/AFE fixed-coefficient observability

### Verdict

The prime/AFE route does **not** currently yield an unconditional proof of

\[
\int_{I_\rho}|q''_{\rm can}(m)|^2\,dm \ge Q^{-B}|I_\rho|.
\]

The best clean output is a **conditional reduction**:

\[
\boxed{
\text{short-interval source observability}
\;\Longleftarrow\;
\text{finite-jet fixed-coefficient nonrecurrence for the actual zeta AFE polynomial.}
}
\]

Standard localized large-sieve, Montgomery–Vaughan, explicit-formula energy, and uncertainty-principle arguments all hit the same obstruction: on intervals of scale

\[
|I_\rho|\asymp Q^{-1},
\]

the prime frequencies are not orthogonal enough to force a lower bound. The problem becomes a finite Taylor-jet cancellation problem for the fixed one-parameter prime-log flow. This matches the coordinator’s framing: Agent 4’s task is to treat \(P_2\) as an actual fixed-coefficient zeta Dirichlet polynomial and test whether it can be forced away from \(-B_2-D_2\) on \(I_\rho\). 

---

# 1. Conditional setup

Assume Agent 1 has canonicalized the source curvature as

\[
q''_{\rm can}(m)
=
B_2(m)+P_2(m)+D_2(m)+E_2(m),
\]

where

\[
P_2(m)
=
\Re\sum_{n\le X}
a_n e^{-im\log n},
\]

with

\[
a_n
=
b_n(\log n)^2n^{-1/2}W(n/T)
\]

up to harmless sign conventions from differentiating \(n^{-1/2-im}\). I write

\[
F(m):=B_2(m)+D_2(m)+P_2(m),
\]

so that

\[
q''_{\rm can}=F+E_2.
\]

If the canonical error satisfies

\[
\int_{I_\rho}|E_2(m)|^2\,dm
\le
\frac12 Q^{-B}|I_\rho|,
\]

then it suffices to prove

\[
\int_{I_\rho}|F(m)|^2\,dm
\ge
2Q^{-B}|I_\rho|.
\]

Thus Agent 4’s core target is

\[
\boxed{
\int_{I_\rho}
|B_2(m)+D_2(m)+P_2(m)|^2\,dm
\ge
Q^{-B}|I_\rho|.
}
\]

This is exactly the prime-side form of the missing source-curvature observability theorem. The shared background also correctly notes that the full nonlinear residual is too hard directly; \(q''\)-energy is the least nonlinear positive target. 

---

# 2. Localized large-sieve / Montgomery–Vaughan test

Let

\[
I_\rho=[m_0-\Delta,m_0+\Delta],
\qquad
\Delta\asymp Q^{-1},
\]

and initially ignore \(B_2+D_2\). For a complex Dirichlet polynomial

\[
P(m)=\sum_{n\le X}a_n e^{-im\lambda_n},
\qquad
\lambda_n=\log n,
\]

one has the exact local identity

\[
\int_{m_0-\Delta}^{m_0+\Delta}|P(m)|^2\,dm
=
\sum_{n,k\le X}
a_n\overline{a_k}
e^{-im_0(\lambda_n-\lambda_k)}
K_\Delta(\lambda_n-\lambda_k),
\]

where

\[
K_\Delta(u)
=
\int_{-\Delta}^{\Delta}e^{-itu}\,dt
=
\frac{2\sin(\Delta u)}{u}.
\]

For large-sieve or Montgomery–Vaughan style lower bounds, one would want this Gram matrix to be coercive. But at the microscopic scale \(\Delta\asymp Q^{-1}\), this fails.

If the relevant frequencies satisfy roughly

\[
0\le \lambda_n\lesssim Q,
\]

then

\[
\Delta\lambda_n=O(1).
\]

So the interval is at or below the local resolution scale. The kernel is not close to diagonal; it is closer to a low-rank moment kernel:

\[
K_\Delta(\lambda_n-\lambda_k)
=
2\Delta
\left[
1
-
\frac{\Delta^2(\lambda_n-\lambda_k)^2}{6}
+\cdots
\right].
\]

Thus the local \(L^2\) norm is governed by finitely many moments

\[
\sum_n a_n e^{-im_0\lambda_n}\lambda_n^r,
\]

not by an orthogonal prime-frequency energy.

### Consequence

Localized large sieve can at best say:

\[
\int_{I_\rho}|P|^2
\quad\text{is controlled by a finite moment Gram matrix.}
\]

It does **not** give a uniform lower bound for

\[
B_2+D_2+P_2
\]

on a single microscopic interval. It becomes equivalent to showing that the fixed zeta coefficients cannot cancel the background/dual target through enough low-order moments.

So the large-sieve/Montgomery–Vaughan branch reduces to finite-jet nonrecurrence.

---

# 3. Explicit-formula energy test

The explicit formula can represent source-side objects linearly:

\[
q''_{\rm can}
=
B_2
+
P_2
+
D_2
+
E_2.
\]

Squaring gives

\[
\int_I |q''_{\rm can}|^2
=
\int_I |B_2+D_2|^2
+
2\Re\int_I (B_2+D_2)\overline{P_2}
+
\int_I |P_2|^2
+
\text{errors}.
\]

The final term expands into bilinear prime sums:

\[
\int_I |P_2|^2
=
\sum_{n,k}
a_n\overline{a_k}
e^{-im_0\log(n/k)}
K_\Delta(\log(n/k)).
\]

This is positive as a whole, but it does not dominate the cross term

\[
2\Re\int_I (B_2+D_2)\overline{P_2}.
\]

The source-collapse scenario is precisely

\[
P_2(m)\approx -B_2(m)-D_2(m)
\]

throughout \(I_\rho\). In that case the explicit formula identity becomes a cancellation identity, not a coercive lower bound.

### Failure point

The explicit formula gives representation, not coercivity. To make it coercive, one would need a theorem of the following form:

\[
\boxed{
P_2
\text{ cannot approximate }
-B_2-D_2
\text{ on }I_\rho
\text{ to polynomial accuracy.}
}
\]

That is not a standard explicit-formula consequence. It is exactly the fixed-coefficient non-approximation theorem we are missing.

This agrees with the draft’s current no-go ledger: prime-side coercivity for the full residual has not been identified, and tensorizing the explicit formula produces oscillatory multi-prime sums rather than a sign-definite obstruction. 

---

# 4. Uncertainty-principle test

A tempting thought is:

> If \(P_2\) is built from many prime frequencies, perhaps it cannot be too small on a whole interval of length \(Q^{-1}\).

But the relevant bandwidth is approximately

\[
\Lambda\sim Q,
\]

and the interval length is

\[
\Delta\sim Q^{-1}.
\]

Hence

\[
\Lambda\Delta\sim 1.
\]

This is exactly the scale at which a band-limited function can have significant local flattening without violating uncertainty principles. A single interval of Nyquist length is not enough. Logvinenko–Sereda type principles require smallness on a relatively dense set, not on one admissible packet interval.

So uncertainty principles do not rule out

\[
\sup_{m\in I_\rho}|q''_{\rm can}(m)|\le Q^{-C}.
\]

They again reduce to finite-jet control at the center.

---

# 5. Finite-jet reduction: the useful positive result

This is the productive part.

Let

\[
I_\rho=[m_0-\Delta,m_0+\Delta],
\qquad
\Delta\asymp Q^{-1},
\]

and define scaled jets

\[
J_r(F;m_0)
:=
\Delta^r F^{(r)}(m_0).
\]

Assume \(F\) has Bernstein-type control on a slightly larger interval:

\[
|F^{(r)}(m)|
\le
M_0 Q^r r!
\]

or the corresponding AFE analytic continuation/Cauchy bound.

Then finite Taylor theory gives:

\[
F(m_0+u)
=
\sum_{r=0}^{R}
\frac{F^{(r)}(m_0)}{r!}u^r
+
\text{tail}.
\]

Equivalently,

\[
F(m_0+\Delta x)
=
\sum_{r=0}^{R}
\frac{J_r(F;m_0)}{r!}x^r
+
\text{tail},
\qquad |x|\le 1.
\]

A standard polynomial coefficient lower bound gives:

\[
\int_{-1}^{1}
\left|
\sum_{r=0}^{R}c_rx^r
\right|^2dx
\ge
\exp(-C R\log R)\max_{0\le r\le R}|c_r|^2.
\]

Therefore, if

\[
\max_{0\le r\le R}
|J_r(F;m_0)|
\ge
Q^{-B_0},
\]

and the Taylor tail is smaller than half this size on \([-1,1]\), then

\[
\int_{I_\rho}|F(m)|^2\,dm
\ge
Q^{-B_1}|I_\rho|
\]

provided

\[
R\asymp \frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q}
\]

or \(R=O(\log Q)\) with constants adjusted.

This matches the shared background’s finite-jet formulation: if interval estimates fail directly, the correct substitute is a growing finite-jet nonrecurrence target for \((q''_{\rm can})^{(r)}(m_0)\). 

---

# 6. Best theorem candidate

The prime-side theorem should not be stated as a generic Dirichlet-polynomial estimate. It should be stated as a fixed-coefficient zeta nonrecurrence theorem.

## Candidate theorem: fixed-coefficient AFE jet nonrecurrence

Let

\[
F(m)=B_2(m)+D_2(m)+
\Re\sum_{n\le X}
a_n e^{-im\log n},
\]

where \(a_n\) are the actual AFE/zeta coefficients in the canonical source-curvature representation. Let

\[
I_\rho=[m_0-\Delta,m_0+\Delta],
\qquad
\Delta\asymp Q^{-1}.
\]

There exist constants \(B,C>0\) and

\[
R(Q)=
\left\lceil
C\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q}
\right\rceil
\]

such that, for every admissible off-line packet center \(m_0\),

\[
\boxed{
\max_{0\le r\le R(Q)}
\left|
\Delta^r
\frac{d^r}{dm^r}
\left[
B_2(m)+D_2(m)+
\Re\sum_{n\le X}a_ne^{-im\log n}
\right]_{m=m_0}
\right|
\ge
Q^{-B}.
}
\]

Then, assuming the canonical error satisfies

\[
\int_{I_\rho}|E_2|^2\ll Q^{-B'}|I_\rho|
\]

with \(B'\) sufficiently large, one obtains

\[
\boxed{
\int_{I_\rho}
|q''_{\rm can}(m)|^2\,dm
\ge
Q^{-B''}|I_\rho|.
}
\]

This is the clean Agent 4 reduction.

---

# 7. Why this theorem is genuinely arithmetic

The theorem says the one-parameter prime-log orbit

\[
m\mapsto
(e^{-im\log n})_{n\le X}
\]

cannot approach the finite-codimension tube defined by

\[
\Delta^rF^{(r)}(m_0)\approx 0,
\qquad
0\le r\le R(Q),
\]

together with the side constraints imposed by \(B_2,D_2\), smoothing, the dual sum, and the canonical normalization.

This is stronger than ordinary equidistribution. In fact, heuristic recurrence argues in the opposite direction: a finite-codimension tube of tolerance \(Q^{-C}\) and codimension \(K\sim R+3\) should be hit on a scale roughly

\[
Q^{CK}.
\]

For

\[
R=O(\log Q)
\]

this gives

\[
\exp(O((\log Q)^2)),
\]

which is much smaller than a height scale like \(e^Q\). The shared background explicitly flags this recurrence danger and warns that generic Diophantine optimism is insufficient. 

So the theorem cannot be justified by saying “prime phases are independent” or “Euler products are positive.” It needs a real fixed-coefficient obstruction, likely tied to one of:

\[
\text{actual AFE coefficient rigidity},
\]

\[
\text{off-line packet admissibility restricting }m_0,
\]

\[
\text{zero/prime compatibility beyond finite phase recurrence},
\]

\[
\text{global explicit-formula imbalance},
\]

or

\[
\text{a new arithmetic incidence theorem.}
\]

---

# 8. Failure modes of the standard approaches

## 8.1 Generic Dirichlet-polynomial approximation defeats the method

If one treats

\[
P_2(m)=\sum a_ne^{-im\log n}
\]

as an arbitrary trigonometric polynomial with adjustable coefficients, then the desired lower bound is false. One can arrange finite-jet cancellation of

\[
B_2+D_2
\]

through order \(R\) using a Vandermonde/moment system.

Therefore, the theorem must use the **fixed actual coefficients** \(a_n\), not merely the frequency set \(\{\log n\}\).

## 8.2 Phase-relaxed fixed-amplitude models do not block cancellation

Even if amplitudes are fixed and only phases vary, the low-order moment targets can lie inside a feasible zonotope. The background notes that fixed-prime and AFE-style surrogate models have repeatedly produced Regime B behavior: \(q''\)-type quantities nearly vanish while \(q_0\), Gram positivity, and \(\Gamma_G\) remain live. 

Thus amplitude feasibility is not the blocker. The blocker, if one exists, must be the actual one-parameter recurrence structure

\[
m\log p \pmod{2\pi},
\]

plus whatever special restrictions come from admissible off-line packet centers.

## 8.3 Single-interval uncertainty is too weak

Because

\[
\Lambda\Delta\sim 1,
\]

a single packet interval is not large enough to force a lower bound by bandwidth alone.

## 8.4 Explicit-formula positivity is absent

The explicit formula is linear in \(q_0,q'',q^{(4)}\)-type data. The source-weighted RH residual is nonlinear. Squaring creates oscillatory cross-prime terms, not a known positive form. This is already part of the draft’s no-go ledger. 

---

# 9. Recommended theorem package for the paper

The paper should introduce the following as a conditional bridge, not as established fact.

```latex
\begin{hypothesis}[Fixed-coefficient AFE source-jet nonrecurrence]
\label{hyp:afe-source-jet-nonrecurrence}
Let
\[
q''_{\rm can}(m)
=
B_2(m)+D_2(m)+P_2(m)+E_2(m),
\]
be the canonical actual-zeta source-curvature representation, with
\[
P_2(m)=
\Re\sum_{n\le X}
a_n e^{-im\log n}
\]
using the fixed AFE/zeta coefficients in this normalization.  Let
\[
I_\rho=[m_0-\Delta,m_0+\Delta],
\qquad
\Delta\asymp Q^{-1},
\]
be an admissible reduced off-line packet interval.  There exist constants
\(B,C>0\), with
\[
R(Q)=\left\lceil C\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q}\right\rceil,
\]
such that
\[
\max_{0\le r\le R(Q)}
\left|
\Delta^r
\frac{d^r}{dm^r}
\left(B_2(m)+D_2(m)+P_2(m)\right)_{m=m_0}
\right|
\ge Q^{-B}.
\]
\end{hypothesis}
```

Then add the bridge proposition:

```latex
\begin{proposition}[Finite-jet nonrecurrence implies source-curvature observability]
\label{prop:finite-jet-nonrecurrence-implies-source-observability}
Assume Hypothesis~\ref{hyp:afe-source-jet-nonrecurrence}.  Assume moreover
that \(B_2+D_2+P_2\) satisfies the usual Bernstein--Cauchy bounds on a fixed
complex enlargement of \(I_\rho\), and that the canonical error satisfies
\[
\int_{I_\rho}|E_2(m)|^2\,dm
\le Q^{-M}|I_\rho|
\]
with \(M\) sufficiently large.  Then there is \(B'>0\) such that
\[
\int_{I_\rho}|q''_{\rm can}(m)|^2\,dm
\ge Q^{-B'}|I_\rho|.
\]
\end{proposition}
```

Proof sketch to include:

```latex
\begin{proof}[Proof sketch]
Put \(F=B_2+D_2+P_2\) and write \(m=m_0+\Delta x\), \(|x|\le1\).  Taylor expand
\[
F(m_0+\Delta x)
=
\sum_{r=0}^{R}
\frac{\Delta^rF^{(r)}(m_0)}{r!}x^r
+
\mathcal E_R(x).
\]
By the Bernstein--Cauchy bounds and the choice
\(R\asymp \log Q/\log\log Q\), the tail is \(O(Q^{-M_1})\) after increasing
constants.  A coefficient lower bound for polynomials gives
\[
\int_{-1}^{1}
\left|
\sum_{r=0}^{R}c_rx^r
\right|^2dx
\ge
\exp(-C R\log R)\max_r |c_r|^2.
\]
Using the fixed-coefficient jet nonrecurrence hypothesis and
\(\exp(-C R\log R)\ge Q^{-C'}\), we get
\[
\int_{I_\rho}|F(m)|^2\,dm\ge Q^{-B''}|I_\rho|.
\]
The \(E_2\) term is absorbed by Cauchy--Schwarz and the assumed error bound.
\end{proof}
```

---

# 10. Agent 4 decision

The best available Agent 4 output is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Prime/AFE observability is reducible to fixed-coefficient finite-jet nonrecurrence.}
}
\]

But I do **not** see a standard theorem that proves the needed nonrecurrence.

The exact missing prime-side input is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{The actual AFE Dirichlet polynomial for }q''_{\rm can}
\text{ cannot approximate }-B_2-D_2
\text{ through }R(Q)\text{ scaled jets at any admissible }m_0.
}
\]

Until that is proved, the prime/AFE route remains plausible but unclosed.

My recommendation to the coordinator:

1. Keep the \(L^2\) source-curvature theorem as the main arithmetic gate.
2. Record the finite-jet reduction as a useful conditional bridge.
3. Do not claim localized large-sieve/Montgomery–Vaughan/exact-formula energy currently proves the gate.
4. Push next on one of two sharper subproblems:

\[
\text{AFE fixed-coefficient nonrecurrence at admissible off-line centers}
\]

or

\[
\text{a global explicit-formula imbalance tying source-flatness to impossible zero/prime data.}
\]

The current Agent 4 branch is therefore **not dead**, but it has been narrowed to a very specific, nonstandard arithmetic theorem.

I’m going to sharpen the earlier Agent 4 reduction around the only potentially new restriction: \(m_0\) is not just an arbitrary time if it is the center of a hypothetical off-line packet. The question is whether that admissibility adds enough equations to defeat prime-log recurrence.

_Thought for 1m 1s_

## Agent 4 / D — Fixed-coefficient finite-jet nonrecurrence, sharpened

### Executive verdict

The admissible off-line packet condition **does add constraints on \(m_0\)**, but not enough, by itself, to defeat the finite-jet recurrence heuristic.

The sharpened conclusion is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Prime/AFE observability must be strengthened to a center-conditioned nonrecurrence theorem.}
}
\]

The target should no longer be merely

\[
\max_{0\le r\le R}
\left|
\Delta^rF^{(r)}(m_0)
\right|
\ge Q^{-B}.
\]

It should be:

\[
\boxed{
\text{If }m_0\text{ is the ordinate/center of an admissible hypothetical off-line packet,}
\text{ then the AFE source jets cannot all be small.}
}
\]

However, after testing the admissibility constraints, I do **not** see a proof from standard prime-side tools. The zero/packet condition adds finitely many equations, but the prime-log recurrence model still plausibly has enough room to satisfy them together with source-flatness. This is exactly the sharpened Agent 4 gate requested in the coordinator instruction. 

---

# 1. Setup

Work with the canonical actual-zeta source curvature

\[
q''_{\can}(m)=q''_\zeta(m)=\Phi_\zeta'''(m),
\]

and write the prime/AFE-side approximation as

\[
q''_{\can}(m)
=
F(m)+E_2(m),
\]

where

\[
F(m)=B_2(m)+D_2(m)+P_2(m),
\]

and

\[
P_2(m)
=
\Re\sum_{n\le X} a_n e^{-im\log n}.
\]

Here \(a_n\) are the **fixed actual zeta/AFE coefficients**, not adjustable coefficients.

For

\[
I_\rho=[m_0-\Delta,m_0+\Delta],
\qquad
\Delta\asymp Q^{-1},
\]

the finite-jet target is

\[
\max_{0\le r\le R(Q)}
\left|
\Delta^r F^{(r)}(m_0)
\right|
\ge Q^{-B},
\qquad
R(Q)\asymp \frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q}.
\]

The jets are explicitly

\[
\Delta^rF^{(r)}(m_0)
=
\Delta^r(B_2+D_2)^{(r)}(m_0)
+
\Re\sum_{n\le X}
a_n(-i\Delta\log n)^r e^{-im_0\log n}.
\]

Thus source-flatness through order \(R\) is a finite system of approximate moment equations:

\[
\Re\sum_{n\le X}
a_n(-i\Delta\log n)^r e^{-im_0\log n}
\approx
-\Delta^r(B_2+D_2)^{(r)}(m_0),
\qquad
0\le r\le R.
\]

The key question is whether the extra fact

\[
m_0=\text{center/ordinate of an admissible off-line packet}
\]

makes this system impossible.

---

# 2. Is \(m_0\) arbitrary?

No. In the contradiction setup, \(m_0\) is tied to a hypothetical off-line zero or off-line zero packet.

A minimal model is:

\[
\rho=\frac12+\alpha+im_0,
\qquad
\alpha\ne0,
\]

with the functional-equation quartet also present:

\[
\rho,\quad
1-\rho,\quad
\overline{\rho},\quad
1-\overline{\rho}.
\]

So \(m_0\) is not an arbitrary phase time. It satisfies the off-line zero equation

\[
\xi\!\left(\frac12+\alpha+im_0\right)=0.
\]

On the AFE side this is another fixed-coefficient exponential relation:

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)
:=
C_\alpha(m_0)
+
\sum_{n\le X_\alpha}
u_n(\alpha,m_0)e^{-im_0\log n}
+
\chi_\alpha(m_0)
\sum_{n\le Y_\alpha}
v_n(\alpha,m_0)e^{+im_0\log n}
+
\operatorname{err}
=
0.
\]

This gives two real equations:

\[
\Re Z_\alpha(m_0)=0,
\qquad
\Im Z_\alpha(m_0)=0.
\]

If \(\alpha\) is also unknown, then \((m_0,\alpha)\) gives one additional continuous parameter, but the zero condition remains two real constraints.

So the admissible packet center adds roughly **two real equations**, plus open inequalities such as simplicity, core gap, Gram positivity, and admissible scale.

Those inequalities are not coercive against recurrence; they define an open region.

---

# 3. Does the off-line packet hypothesis impose simultaneous constraints on \(F,F',\ldots\)?

Only weakly.

The off-line zero equation imposes

\[
\xi\!\left(\frac12+\alpha+im_0\right)=0.
\]

If the zero is simple, then

\[
\xi'\!\left(\frac12+\alpha+im_0\right)\ne0,
\]

which is an **open nonvanishing condition**, not an additional vanishing equation.

The source-flatness target imposes

\[
\Delta^rF^{(r)}(m_0)\approx0,
\qquad
0\le r\le R.
\]

These are different AFE moment functionals evaluated on the same prime-log phase vector

\[
\left(e^{-im_0\log n}\right)_{n\le X}.
\]

So the combined system is approximately:

\[
\begin{cases}
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0,\\
\Delta^rF^{(r)}(m_0)\approx0,\qquad 0\le r\le R,\\
\text{packet admissibility inequalities.}
\end{cases}
\]

Counting real equations:

\[
2+(R+1)
\]

up to harmless splitting of real and imaginary parts depending on the precise real normalization of \(F\).

Since

\[
R\asymp \frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q},
\]

this is still finite codimension

\[
K\asymp R+3.
\]

There is no visible algebraic overdetermination.

---

# 4. Does zero/prime compatibility give more equations than recurrence can satisfy?

At present, no.

The same prime phases enter both the off-line zero equation and the \(q''_{\can}\)-jet equations. This gives a coupled system, but not an obviously inconsistent one.

A useful finite-dimensional model is this. Select primes \(p_1,\ldots,p_M\), freeze the slow \(m\)-dependence of the AFE coefficients, and consider the torus variables

\[
\theta_j=m_0\log p_j \pmod{2\pi}.
\]

The combined map has the schematic form

\[
\Theta=(\theta_1,\ldots,\theta_M)
\mapsto
\left(
\Re Z_\alpha,\Im Z_\alpha,
J_0,J_1,\ldots,J_R
\right),
\]

where

\[
J_r=\Delta^rF^{(r)}(m_0).
\]

For \(M\gg R\), the Jacobian of this map is generically full rank because the weights involve distinct powers of \(\log p_j\):

\[
(\Delta\log p_j)^r,
\qquad
0\le r\le R.
\]

Thus, in the phase-relaxed model, the simultaneous equations cut out a codimension-\(R+3\) submanifold rather than an empty set.

Returning to the actual one-parameter orbit,

\[
m\mapsto
(m\log p_1,\ldots,m\log p_M)\pmod{2\pi},
\]

Kronecker-type recurrence heuristics still suggest that such a finite-codimension tube can be approached on a scale roughly

\[
\varepsilon^{-K},
\qquad
K\asymp R+3.
\]

For polynomial tolerance \(\varepsilon=Q^{-C}\), this gives recurrence cost

\[
Q^{C(R+3)}
=
\exp\!\left(
O\!\left(\frac{(\log Q)^2}{\log\log Q}\right)
\right),
\]

or at worst

\[
\exp(O((\log Q)^2))
\]

if \(R=O(\log Q)\).

This is still much smaller than a natural height scale \(T=e^Q\). So phase recurrence is not obviously defeated by adding the off-line zero equation.

This is the crucial negative conclusion.

---

# 5. Does the dual term \(D_2\) or \(\chi\)-factor break recurrence?

Not in the current formulation.

The dual AFE term has the form

\[
D_2(m)
\sim
\Re\left[
\chi(m)
\sum_{n\le Y}
\tilde a_n e^{+im\log n}
\right]
\]

plus derivatives of \(\chi\). Differentiating produces terms involving

\[
(\log n)^r,
\qquad
\theta_\chi^{(j)}(m),
\]

and smooth gamma-factor contributions.

On an interval of length

\[
\Delta\asymp Q^{-1},
\]

the \(\chi\)-factor and gamma derivatives are smooth deterministic background terms. They shift the jet targets:

\[
J_r=0
\quad\Longleftrightarrow\quad
P_{2,r}(m_0)
\approx
-\bigl(B_2+D_2\bigr)_r(m_0).
\]

They do not add a sign, monotonicity, or positivity constraint that prevents cancellation.

The dual term also uses the same phase flow, with frequencies \(-\log n\) rather than \(+\log n\). That doubles the visible trigonometric structure but does not make the system coercive.

So \(D_2\) and \(\chi\) complicate the recurrence target but do not break it.

---

# 6. Sharper theorem candidate

The correct Agent 4 theorem is not the earlier unconditional nonrecurrence statement. It should explicitly condition on the off-line packet equation.

## Candidate hypothesis: center-conditioned AFE source-jet nonrecurrence

```latex
\begin{hypothesis}[Center-conditioned AFE source-jet nonrecurrence]
\label{hyp:center-conditioned-afe-source-jet-nonrecurrence}
Let
\[
q''_{\can}(m)=B_2(m)+D_2(m)+P_2(m)+E_2(m)
\]
be the canonical actual-zeta source-curvature representation, where
\[
P_2(m)=\Re\sum_{n\le X}a_ne^{-im\log n}
\]
uses the fixed AFE/zeta coefficients.  Let
\[
I_\rho=[m_0-\Delta,m_0+\Delta],
\qquad
\Delta\asymp Q^{-1},
\]
be an admissible reduced packet interval associated to a hypothetical off-line
zero or off-line packet.  Equivalently, \(m_0\) satisfies the corresponding
off-line AFE zero equation
\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\]
for some admissible transverse displacement \(\alpha\), together with the
usual packet-admissibility inequalities.

Then there exist constants \(B,C>0\), with
\[
R(Q)=\left\lceil C\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q}\right\rceil,
\]
such that
\[
\max_{0\le r\le R(Q)}
\left|
\Delta^r
\frac{d^r}{dm^r}
\left(B_2(m)+D_2(m)+P_2(m)\right)_{m=m_0}
\right|
\ge Q^{-B}.
\]
\end{hypothesis}
```

This is stronger and more accurate than the previous version because it does not ask for nonrecurrence at every \(m_0\). It asks only at \(m_0\)’s that are admissible off-line packet centers.

But this is still a new arithmetic theorem. It is not supplied by standard AFE estimates.

---

# 7. Equivalent “no simultaneous recurrence” formulation

A more operational version is:

```latex
\begin{hypothesis}[No simultaneous off-line-zero/source-flat recurrence]
\label{hyp:no-simultaneous-zero-source-flat-recurrence}
There are constants \(B,C>0\) such that no admissible pair \((\alpha,m_0)\)
can satisfy simultaneously
\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\]
and
\[
\left|
\Delta^r
\frac{d^r}{dm^r}
\left(B_2+D_2+P_2\right)(m_0)
\right|
\le Q^{-B}
\qquad
(0\le r\le R(Q)),
\]
where
\[
R(Q)=\left\lceil C\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q}\right\rceil.
\]
\end{hypothesis}
```

This is probably the cleanest way to state the missing prime-side arithmetic input.

It says: the same fixed zeta phases cannot simultaneously create an off-line zero and flatten the canonical source curvature through the required finite jet depth.

---

# 8. Why this is not currently proved

The obstruction is that the combined conditions still look like finite-codimension recurrence conditions.

The combined constraints are:

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0,
\]

plus

\[
J_r(m_0)=0,
\qquad
0\le r\le R.
\]

This is approximately \(R+3\) real conditions. The prime phase flow has enormous effective dimension when viewed through primes up to the AFE length. No known theorem says that the actual orbit

\[
m\mapsto
(e^{-im\log p})_{p\le X}
\]

avoids the resulting tube at all admissible off-line packet centers.

In particular:

1. **The zero equation is only two real equations.**  
   It is not enough to overdetermine \(R+1\) source-flat jet equations.

2. **Packet admissibility mostly gives inequalities.**  
   Simplicity, core gap, Gram positivity, and same-scale localization are open conditions. They do not block recurrence.

3. **The \(\chi\)-factor shifts targets but does not force positivity.**  
   It changes the moment equations but does not produce a coercive lower bound.

4. **Generic finite-dimensional phase models allow simultaneous solutions.**  
   With enough frequencies, the Jacobian of the map from prime phases to zero/source jets is generically full rank.

5. **Actual one-parameter recurrence remains plausible at the required depth.**  
   The expected recurrence cost for \(R\sim\log Q/\log\log Q\) is sub-\(e^Q\), so scale alone does not save the argument.

---

# 9. What would be needed to close Agent 4

A closing theorem must exploit something beyond generic prime-phase recurrence. Plausible extra inputs would be:

### 9.1 A true fixed-coefficient obstruction

One would need to show that the actual coefficients \(a_n\), not just the frequencies \(\log n\), prevent the combined zero/source-flat target.

Schematic form:

\[
\operatorname{dist}
\left(
\bigl(Z_\alpha(m),J_0(m),\ldots,J_R(m)\bigr),
0
\right)
\ge Q^{-B}
\]

for all admissible \((\alpha,m)\).

### 9.2 A zero-prime compatibility theorem

One could try to prove that if

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0,
\]

then the same explicit formula forces

\[
\max_{0\le r\le R}|J_r(m_0)|\ge Q^{-B}.
\]

This would directly use the off-line zero equation.

But I do not see such a theorem from the ordinary AFE. It would require a new rigidity principle connecting an off-critical zero to critical-line phase curvature.

### 9.3 A global-in-\(m\) obstruction

A local recurrence theorem may be false or unreachable. A global theorem might say that too many or too strong local source-flat packets would violate an explicit-formula energy identity. That is closer to Agent 5’s territory.

### 9.4 A positivity structure hidden in \(D_2+\chi\)

If the dual/gamma terms secretly force a sign-definite contribution in the source-curvature jets at off-line centers, that could break recurrence. I see no such structure yet.

---

# 10. Refined decision

Agent 4’s branch remains mathematically meaningful, but it should be documented as follows:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Prime/AFE observability reduces to a center-conditioned fixed-coefficient finite-jet nonrecurrence theorem.}
}
\]

The admissible off-line center condition strengthens the theorem’s statement, but does **not** presently provide a proof. Recurrence remains plausible because the off-line zero equation adds only finitely many constraints, while the prime-log phase flow still has enough effective degrees of freedom at the relevant finite jet depth.

So the sharpened status is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{No standard prime-side tool closes Gate 1.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{The exact missing theorem is no simultaneous off-line-zero/source-flat recurrence.}
}
\]

I would recommend the paper record this as a conditional arithmetic gate, not as a proven lemma.

_Thought for 22s_

## Agent 4 / D — Center-conditioned finite-jet nonrecurrence

### Verdict

The off-line packet condition **does not presently defeat prime-log recurrence**. It improves the formulation of the Gate 1 arithmetic input, but it does not prove it.

The correct missing theorem is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{No simultaneous off-line-zero/source-flat finite-jet recurrence.}
}
\]

That is stronger than generic finite-jet nonrecurrence because \(m_0\) is not arbitrary: it must be the ordinate or center of an admissible hypothetical off-line packet. But the off-line zero equation contributes only finitely many real constraints, while the source-flat condition is still a finite-codimension target for the same prime-log phase flow. I do not see a standard large-sieve, AFE, \(\chi\)-factor, or explicit-formula coercivity argument that closes this gate. This matches the attached Agent 4/D instruction, which asks specifically whether \(Z_\alpha(m_0)=0\) adds enough constraints to defeat recurrence. 

---

# 1. Canonical setup

Use the repaired convention:

\[
q''_{\can}(m)=q_\zeta''(m)=\Phi_\zeta'''(m).
\]

The prime/AFE representation has the form

\[
q''_{\can}(m)
=
B_2(m)+P_2(m)+D_2(m)+E_2(m),
\]

where

\[
P_2(m)
=
\Re\sum_{n\le X}a_ne^{-im\log n}
\]

has **fixed actual zeta/AFE coefficients**. Define

\[
F(m):=B_2(m)+D_2(m)+P_2(m).
\]

Gate 1 asks for

\[
\int_{I_\rho}|q''_{\can}(m)|^2\,dm
\ge Q^{-B}|I_\rho|.
\]

Ignoring the controlled error \(E_2\), source-flatness on

\[
I_\rho=[m_0-\Delta,m_0+\Delta],
\qquad
\Delta\asymp Q^{-1},
\]

requires finite-jet smallness

\[
\Delta^rF^{(r)}(m_0)\approx0,
\qquad
0\le r\le R(Q),
\]

with

\[
R(Q)\asymp \frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q}.
\]

Explicitly,

\[
\Delta^rF^{(r)}(m_0)
=
\Delta^r(B_2+D_2)^{(r)}(m_0)
+
\Re\sum_{n\le X}
a_n(-i\Delta\log n)^r e^{-im_0\log n}.
\]

So the arithmetic problem is a fixed-coefficient moment-recurrence problem for the prime-log orbit.

---

# 2. What the off-line zero equation contributes

A hypothetical off-line zero has the form

\[
\rho=\frac12+\alpha+im_0,
\qquad
\alpha\ne0.
\]

In AFE notation, this gives a complex equation

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0.
\]

Equivalently, two real equations:

\[
\Re Z_\alpha(m_0)=0,
\qquad
\Im Z_\alpha(m_0)=0.
\]

If \(\alpha\) is treated as an unknown, then \((\alpha,m_0)\) gives two real scalar variables, so the zero equation is not obviously overdetermining. In the prime-phase torus model, it simply adds two scalar constraints to the same phase vector.

The source-flat jets add roughly

\[
R(Q)+1
\]

additional real constraints:

\[
\Delta^rF^{(r)}(m_0)\approx0,
\qquad
0\le r\le R(Q).
\]

Thus the simultaneous target has codimension roughly

\[
K\asymp R(Q)+3.
\]

This is finite and modest compared with the number of prime frequencies visible in the AFE.

---

# 3. Are packet admissibility conditions genuine equations?

Mostly no.

The usual admissibility requirements are of the form:

\[
\text{simple zero},
\]

\[
\text{core gap},
\]

\[
\text{quartet symmetry},
\]

\[
\text{Gram positivity},
\]

\[
\text{same-scale localization},
\]

\[
\text{good-patch regularity}.
\]

Quartet symmetry is structural, coming from the functional equation and conjugation. It does not add an independent scalar equation after the off-line zero is chosen.

Simplicity is

\[
\xi'(\rho)\ne0,
\]

an open nonvanishing condition.

Core gap and Gram positivity are inequalities.

Same-scale localization is a scale restriction, not a vanishing equation.

Good-patch regularity is an analytic bound.

Therefore the admissibility package mostly carves out an open or semi-open region. It does not add enough scalar equalities to make the recurrence target visibly impossible.

---

# 4. Do the same prime phases control zero formation and source-flatness?

Yes. This is the key coupling.

The off-line zero equation has an AFE schematic form

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)
=
C_\alpha(m_0)
+
\sum_{n\le X_\alpha}
u_n(\alpha,m_0)e^{-im_0\log n}
+
\chi_\alpha(m_0)
\sum_{n\le Y_\alpha}
v_n(\alpha,m_0)e^{+im_0\log n}
+
\operatorname{err}.
\]

The source-flat equations are

\[
\Delta^rF^{(r)}(m_0)
=
\Delta^r(B_2+D_2)^{(r)}(m_0)
+
\Re\sum_{n\le X}
a_n(-i\Delta\log n)^r e^{-im_0\log n}
\approx0.
\]

Both are functions of the same one-parameter phase flow

\[
m_0\mapsto
(e^{-im_0\log n})_{n\le X}.
\]

That creates coupling, but not currently a contradiction.

A phase-relaxed model makes this clear. Let

\[
\theta_p=m_0\log p\pmod{2\pi},
\]

and consider the map

\[
\Theta=(\theta_p)_{p\le X}
\mapsto
\left(
\Re Z_\alpha,
\Im Z_\alpha,
J_0,\ldots,J_R
\right),
\]

where

\[
J_r=\Delta^rF^{(r)}(m_0).
\]

The Jacobian in the \(J_r\) components contains weights like

\[
(\Delta\log p)^r.
\]

For enough primes, this resembles a Vandermonde/moment matrix and is generically full rank. Thus, in the phase-relaxed model, simultaneous zero/source-flat solutions should form a positive-dimensional set rather than be empty.

Returning to the actual one-parameter orbit, the recurrence cost for a codimension-\(K\) target at polynomial tolerance \(\varepsilon=Q^{-C}\) is heuristically

\[
\varepsilon^{-K}=Q^{CK}.
\]

With

\[
K\asymp R(Q)+3
\asymp
\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q},
\]

this is

\[
\exp\!\left(
O\!\left(\frac{(\log Q)^2}{\log\log Q}\right)
\right).
\]

That is not prohibitively large relative to natural zeta height scales. So the recurrence heuristic remains plausible.

---

# 5. Does \(D_2\), \(\chi\), or the gamma factor create coercivity?

I do not see such a mechanism.

The dual term has the schematic form

\[
D_2(m)
\sim
\Re\left[
\chi(m)
\sum_{n\le Y}\tilde a_ne^{+im\log n}
\right]
\]

plus differentiated \(\chi\)- and gamma-factor contributions.

Differentiating produces combinations of

\[
(\log n)^r,
\qquad
\chi^{(j)}(m),
\qquad
\theta^{(j)}(m),
\]

but these are deterministic target shifts and smooth coefficient changes. They transform the source-flat equations into

\[
P_2^{(r)}(m_0)
\approx
-\left(B_2+D_2\right)^{(r)}(m_0).
\]

They do not create a sign-definite term, monotonicity principle, or positivity constraint that blocks cancellation.

The \(\chi\)-factor couples the two AFE sides, but still through the same phase flow. It complicates the finite system; it does not obviously overdetermine it.

---

# 6. Precise missing theorem

The right paper-level hypothesis should be stated as follows.

```latex
\begin{hypothesis}[No simultaneous off-line-zero/source-flat recurrence]
\label{hyp:no-simultaneous-offline-zero-source-flat-recurrence}
Let
\[
q''_{\can}(m)=B_2(m)+D_2(m)+P_2(m)+E_2(m)
\]
be the canonical actual-zeta source-curvature representation, with
\[
P_2(m)=\Re\sum_{n\le X}a_ne^{-im\log n}
\]
using the fixed actual zeta/AFE coefficients.  Let
\[
I_\rho=[m_0-\Delta,m_0+\Delta],
\qquad
\Delta\asymp Q^{-1},
\]
be an admissible reduced packet interval associated to a hypothetical
off-line zero
\[
\rho=\frac12+\alpha+im_0,
\qquad
\alpha\ne0.
\]
Equivalently, \((\alpha,m_0)\) satisfies the corresponding AFE zero equation
\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\]
together with the packet-admissibility inequalities.

Then there exist constants \(B,C>0\), with
\[
R(Q)=\left\lceil C\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q}\right\rceil,
\]
such that
\[
\max_{0\le r\le R(Q)}
\left|
\Delta^r
\frac{d^r}{dm^r}
\left(B_2(m)+D_2(m)+P_2(m)\right)_{m=m_0}
\right|
\ge Q^{-B}.
\]
\end{hypothesis}
```

This is sharper than a generic statement because it only asks for nonrecurrence at centers satisfying the off-line zero equation.

---

# 7. Conditional implication to Gate 1

One can then record the finite-jet bridge.

```latex
\begin{proposition}[Center-conditioned finite-jet nonrecurrence implies Gate 1]
\label{prop:center-conditioned-nonrecurrence-implies-gate-one}
Assume Hypothesis~\ref{hyp:no-simultaneous-offline-zero-source-flat-recurrence}.
Assume also that \(B_2+D_2+P_2\) satisfies the required polynomial
Bernstein--Cauchy bounds on a fixed enlargement of \(I_\rho\), and that
\[
\int_{I_\rho}|E_2(m)|^2\,dm\le Q^{-M}|I_\rho|
\]
for \(M\) sufficiently large.  Then there exists \(B'>0\) such that
\[
\int_{I_\rho}|q''_{\can}(m)|^2\,dm
\ge Q^{-B'}|I_\rho|.
\]
\end{proposition}
```

Proof sketch:

\[
F(m_0+\Delta x)
=
\sum_{r=0}^{R}
\frac{\Delta^rF^{(r)}(m_0)}{r!}x^r
+
\mathcal E_R(x).
\]

A polynomial coefficient lower bound gives

\[
\int_{-1}^{1}
\left|
\sum_{r=0}^{R}c_rx^r
\right|^2dx
\ge
\exp(-CR\log R)\max_{0\le r\le R}|c_r|^2.
\]

Since

\[
R\asymp\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q},
\]

one has

\[
\exp(-CR\log R)\ge Q^{-C'}.
\]

The finite-jet nonrecurrence lower bound then gives

\[
\int_{I_\rho}|F(m)|^2\,dm
\ge Q^{-B''}|I_\rho|.
\]

The \(E_2\) term is absorbed by the assumed error estimate.

---

# 8. Why this is not currently proved

The proof obstruction is structural:

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\]

adds two real equations. The source-flat condition adds \(R+1\) finite-jet equations. The packet conditions are mostly inequalities. The combined system is finite-codimension, not visibly inconsistent.

The actual prime-log orbit

\[
m\mapsto(e^{-im\log p})_{p\le X}
\]

may plausibly recur near such a finite-codimension target at polynomial jet tolerance. No standard theorem currently gives avoidance of that target.

So the status is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{The off-line center condition sharpens the arithmetic gate but does not close it.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate 1 still requires a new fixed-coefficient, center-conditioned nonrecurrence theorem.}
}
\]

---

# 9. Recommendation to coordinator

For the paper, Agent 4’s contribution should be recorded as a **conditional reduction**, not a proof.

Use this language:

```latex
The prime/AFE route reduces Gate~1 to a center-conditioned fixed-coefficient
finite-jet nonrecurrence theorem.  The off-line zero equation \(Z_\alpha(m_0)=0\)
does add constraints on the center \(m_0\), but at present these are only
finitely many scalar constraints and do not by themselves defeat prime-log
recurrence.  The packet-admissibility conditions are mostly open inequalities.
No standard localized large-sieve, Montgomery--Vaughan, AFE, \(\chi\)-factor,
or explicit-formula energy estimate currently proves the required
nonrecurrence.
```

The next mathematical work on Agent 4’s branch should therefore be narrowly focused on:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Can }Z_\alpha(m_0)=0\text{ force at least one source-curvature jet to be polynomially large?}
}
\]

Equivalently:

\[
\boxed{
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\max_{0\le r\le R}
|\Delta^rF^{(r)}(m_0)|
\ge Q^{-B}.
}
\]

At present, I would classify this as a difficult, nonstandard arithmetic theorem, not a consequence of existing prime/AFE technology.

_Thought for 1m 33s_

## Agent 4 / D — Derivative complexity through order six

### Verdict

The draft has enough **ingredients** to make the derivative-complexity bound plausible, but it does **not yet prove** the full Gate-2 analytic package in the form needed:

\[
\sup_{I_\rho^\ast}|q^{(r)}|\le Q^{C_r},
\qquad 0\le r\le6.
\]

This should be added as a **missing good-patch hypothesis** or promoted to a proposition after explicitly proving the higher-order tail and regularization bounds.

This matches the current architecture status: Gate 2 now requires a new good-patch analytic package, including polynomial derivative complexity, source-mass thickening, Remez/Bernstein propagation, and ODE base-locus rigidity. 

---

# 1. Component audit

## 1. Core packet

**Status: likely OK, but should be stated.**

For a finite admissible core packet, each one-zero or one-quartet kernel is rational with denominator bounded below on the microscopic tube. If the admissible tube has width \(\asymp Q^{-1}\), then for each fixed \(0\le r\le6\),

\[
|q_{\core}^{(r)}|\ll Q^{C_r}.
\]

What is missing is a clean sentence saying that every core denominator remains \(\gg Q^{-2}\) on \(I_\rho^\ast\), and that the number of core packets is polynomially bounded.

## 2. Far tail

**Status: almost OK, but currently only explicitly closed at low order.**

The draft’s tail curvature machinery controls second derivatives. For Gate 2, we need the same shell argument through order six:

\[
|T_{\far}^{(r)}|
\ll
\sum_{\rho\notin\mathcal L}\Delta_\rho^{-(r+2)},
\qquad
0\le r\le6.
\]

The shell-counting pattern should give

\[
\sum_{\rho\notin\mathcal L}\Delta_\rho^{-(r+2)}
\ll
Q R^{-(r+1)}
\]

for \(0\le r\le6\). This is polynomial and in fact small for large \(R\). But the draft should explicitly record the finite-order version, not only the curvature case.

## 3. Gamma/background

**Status: OK.**

The gamma/background terms are explicit and smooth at the relevant height. For \(Q\asymp\log |m|\), all derivatives through order six are polynomially bounded, generally much smaller than the core/tail worst case.

No serious failure here.

## 4. AFE error

**Status: missing if the AFE representation is used.**

For the zero-side derivative-complexity proof, AFE error is not needed. But if the paper uses

\[
q''_{\can}=B_2+P_2+D_2+E_2
\]

as the canonical representation, then to bound \(q^{(6)}\) one needs differentiated control of \(E_2\) through four additional \(m\)-derivatives:

\[
\sup_{I_\rho^\ast}
\left|
\partial_m^jE_2(m)
\right|
\le Q^{C_j},
\qquad 0\le j\le4.
\]

The repair patch correctly defines \(q''_{\can}\) and separates it from \(q''_{\source,R}\), but the differentiated \(E_2\)-budget is not yet closed. 

## 5. Zero regularization

**Status: missing as a global statement, avoidable via core/tail decomposition.**

A fully regularized zero-side formula

\[
q''_{\can}(m)
=
B_2(m)+\sum_\rho^{\rm reg}K_2(m;\rho)
\]

needs derivative-safe regularization through the relevant orders. The easier route is to avoid relying on the global regularized sum and instead use:

\[
q_\zeta
=
B_\zeta+q_{\core}+T_{\far}
\]

on the good patch, with explicit finite-core and finite-order tail estimates.

---

# 2. Exact LaTeX insertion

**Location:** Insert immediately after `Remark~\ref{rem:ode-form-source-anisotropy-reintegration}` or immediately before the next source-observability/prime-side discussion.

```latex
\begin{hypothesis}[Gate--2 derivative-complexity good patch]
\label{hyp:gate-two-derivative-complexity-good-patch}
Let \(I_\rho\) be an admissible reduced packet interval and let
\(I_\rho^\ast\) be a fixed polynomial enlargement, contained in the same
good-patch tube.  Write
\[
q=q_\zeta,
\qquad
q''_{\can}=q_\zeta''.
\]
There exist constants \(C_r\), \(0\le r\le6\), such that
\[
\sup_{m\in I_\rho^\ast}|q_\zeta^{(r)}(m)|
\le Q^{C_r},
\qquad
0\le r\le6.
\]

Equivalently, the canonical full phase derivative has polynomial finite
complexity through the order needed for
\[
u=q''_{\can},
\qquad
\Gamma_G=u-6q+2q^3,
\qquad
\Gamma_{G,2}=2q(q')^2-\frac16\Gamma_G''.
\]

A sufficient zero-side package is the following:
\begin{enumerate}
\item the distinguished core contains only polynomially many zero packets, and
all core denominators remain \(\gg Q^{-2}\) on the tube over \(I_\rho^\ast\);

\item for every \(0\le r\le6\), the omitted-zero tail satisfies
\[
\sup_{I_\rho^\ast}|T_{\far}^{(r)}|
\ll
\sum_{\rho\notin\mathcal L}\Delta_\rho^{-(r+2)}
\ll Q^{C_r};
\]

\item the background/gamma contribution satisfies
\[
\sup_{I_\rho^\ast}|B_\zeta^{(r)}|\le Q^{C_r},
\qquad 0\le r\le6;
\]

\item if the prime/AFE representation
\[
q''_{\can}=B_2+P_2+D_2+E_2
\]
is used instead of the zero-side decomposition, then the differentiated error
term satisfies
\[
\sup_{I_\rho^\ast}|\partial_m^jE_2(m)|\le Q^{C_j},
\qquad 0\le j\le4.
\]
\end{enumerate}
\end{hypothesis}
```

---

# 3. Optional proposition if the draft wants to promote it

If the authors want this as a proposition rather than a hypothesis, the following is the clean version.

```latex
\begin{proposition}[Finite-order derivative complexity from core--tail control]
\label{prop:finite-order-derivative-complexity-core-tail}
Assume the zero-side good-patch package in
Hypothesis~\ref{hyp:gate-two-derivative-complexity-good-patch}, excluding only
the conclusion.  Then
\[
\sup_{m\in I_\rho^\ast}|q_\zeta^{(r)}(m)|
\le Q^{C_r},
\qquad
0\le r\le6.
\]
Consequently
\[
u=q''_{\can},
\qquad
\Gamma_G=u-6q+2q^3,
\qquad
\Gamma_{G,2}=2q(q')^2-\frac16\Gamma_G''
\]
also have polynomial finite complexity on \(I_\rho^\ast\), in the sense that
all derivatives explicitly occurring in the Gate--2 ODE/Remez argument are
bounded by powers of \(Q\).
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Write on the good patch
\[
q_\zeta=B_\zeta+q_{\core}+T_{\far}.
\]
The background term is explicit, so its derivatives through order six are
polynomially bounded in \(Q\).  Each core zero-packet contribution is a rational
kernel whose denominator is bounded below by \(\gg Q^{-2}\) on the tube over
\(I_\rho^\ast\).  Since the number of core packets is polynomially bounded,
differentiating each kernel at most six times gives
\[
\sup_{I_\rho^\ast}|q_{\core}^{(r)}|\le Q^{C_r},
\qquad 0\le r\le6.
\]
For the far tail, differentiating a one-zero kernel \(r\) times gives
\[
|f_\rho^{(r)}(m)|\ll_r \Delta_\rho^{-(r+2)}
\]
on \(I_\rho^\ast\).  Hence
\[
\sup_{I_\rho^\ast}|T_{\far}^{(r)}|
\ll_r
\sum_{\rho\notin\mathcal L}\Delta_\rho^{-(r+2)}
\ll Q^{C_r}
\]
by the finite-order shell bound.  Summing the three contributions gives the
claim for \(q_\zeta^{(r)}\), \(0\le r\le6\).  The displayed bounds for
\(u,\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2}\), and \(\Gamma_G''\) follow algebraically from
their definitions and the identity
\[
\Gamma_{G,2}=2q(q')^2-\frac16\Gamma_G''.
\]
\end{proof}
```

---

# 4. Final classification

This is not a deep arithmetic obstruction. It is a **bookkeeping/good-patch lemma**.

The precise failure is not the core packet, far tail, or gamma/background individually. The failure is that the draft does not yet package them into a single canonical statement for the full phase:

\[
q_\zeta
\quad\text{through}\quad
q_\zeta^{(6)}
\]

on the enlarged Gate-2 interval \(I_\rho^\ast\).

So my recommendation is to add the hypothesis now, and later promote it to a proposition once the finite-order shell estimate and differentiated \(E_2\)-budget are written explicitly.

## Agent 4 / D — Remez/Bernstein propagation under minimal smoothness

### Verdict

The propagation step is **valid under order-six derivative complexity**, with one clarification:

\[
\int_J(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)\,dm\le Q^{-M}|J|
\]

does imply, on a polynomially large subinterval \(J'\subset J\),

\[
|\Gamma_G|+|\Gamma_{G,2}|+|\Gamma_G''|
\le Q^{-M/C},
\]

provided the following are available:

\[
|J|\ge Q^{-L},
\]

\[
\sup_J |q_\zeta^{(r)}|\le Q^{C_r},
\qquad 0\le r\le 6.
\]

No \(q^{(7)}\) or \(q^{(8)}\) bound is needed. Order six is enough because \(\Gamma_G^{(4)}\) is the highest derivative required to control \(\Gamma_G''\) by finite differences, and \(\Gamma_G^{(4)}\) uses \(q_\zeta^{(6)}\). This supports the attached Gate-2 proof architecture, where derivative complexity through order six is the key missing good-patch package. 

---

# 1. Notation

Write

\[
u=q''_{\can},
\]

\[
G:=\Gamma_G=u-6q+2q^3,
\]

\[
K:=\Gamma_{G,2}=2q(q')^2-\frac16G''.
\]

Assume on an interval \(J\),

\[
\int_J(G^2+K^2)\,dm\le Q^{-M}|J|.
\]

Let

\[
|J|=\ell,
\qquad
\ell\ge Q^{-L}.
\]

Assume derivative complexity through order six:

\[
\sup_J |q^{(r)}|\le Q^{C_r},
\qquad 0\le r\le6.
\]

Then algebraically,

\[
\sup_J |G'|\le Q^{D_1},
\]

\[
\sup_J |G^{(4)}|\le Q^{D_4},
\]

\[
\sup_J |K'|\le Q^{D_K},
\]

for constants \(D_1,D_4,D_K\) depending only on the finite derivative-complexity exponents \(C_0,\ldots,C_6\).

Why:

\[
G'=q^{(3)}-6q'+6q^2q',
\]

so \(q^{(3)}\) suffices.

\[
G^{(4)}
\]

uses \(q^{(6)}\) and lower products of \(q,q',\ldots,q^{(4)}\).

Also

\[
K'=2(q')^3+4qq'q''-\frac16G''',
\]

and \(G'''\) uses \(q^{(5)}\). Thus \(q^{(6)}\) is more than enough.

---

# 2. Real-variable propagation lemma

Here is the clean propagation statement.

### Lemma

Let \(J\) be an interval of length \(\ell\ge Q^{-L}\). Let \(G,K\in C^4(J)\times C^1(J)\) satisfy

\[
\int_J(G^2+K^2)\,dm\le Q^{-M}\ell,
\]

\[
\|G'\|_{L^\infty(J)}\le Q^{D_1},
\qquad
\|G^{(4)}\|_{L^\infty(J)}\le Q^{D_4},
\qquad
\|K'\|_{L^\infty(J)}\le Q^{D_K}.
\]

Then, for \(M\) sufficiently large relative to \(D_1,D_4,D_K,L\), the middle half

\[
J'=\left\{m\in J:\operatorname{dist}(m,\partial J)\ge \frac{\ell}{4}\right\}
\]

satisfies

\[
\sup_{J'}\left(|G|+|K|+|G''|\right)
\le Q^{-M/C}
\]

for some constant \(C\) depending only on \(D_1,D_4,D_K,L\).

---

# 3. Proof

## Step 1 — \(L^2\)-small plus Lipschitz implies \(L^\infty\)-small

Let \(f\in C^1(J)\), with

\[
\int_J f^2\le \eta^2\ell,
\qquad
\|f'\|_\infty\le L_f.
\]

If

\[
S:=\|f\|_\infty,
\]

then at a point \(x_0\) with \(|f(x_0)|=S\), we have

\[
|f(x)|\ge \frac S2
\]

on an interval of radius at least

\[
r=\min\left(\frac{\ell}{2},\frac{S}{2L_f}\right).
\]

Therefore

\[
\eta^2\ell
\ge
\int_J f^2
\ge
\frac{S^2}{4}r.
\]

This gives

\[
S\ll
\eta
+
(L_f\eta^2\ell)^{1/3}.
\]

Apply this to \(G\) and \(K\), with

\[
\eta=Q^{-M/2}.
\]

Since

\[
L_f\le Q^D,
\qquad
\ell\le Q^{O(1)},\qquad
\ell\ge Q^{-L},
\]

we get

\[
\|G\|_{L^\infty(J)}
+
\|K\|_{L^\infty(J)}
\le
Q^{-cM+C_0}
\]

for some \(c>0\). After increasing constants,

\[
\|G\|_{L^\infty(J)}
+
\|K\|_{L^\infty(J)}
\le
Q^{-M/C_1}.
\]

This already gives smallness of \(\Gamma_G\) and \(\Gamma_{G,2}\) on all of \(J\).

---

## Step 2 — Small \(G\) plus bounded \(G^{(4)}\) implies small \(G''\) inside \(J\)

Let

\[
\delta:=\|G\|_{L^\infty(J)}.
\]

For \(x\in J'\), use the central second-difference formula:

\[
G''(x)
=
\frac{G(x+h)-2G(x)+G(x-h)}{h^2}
+
O\left(\|G^{(4)}\|_\infty h^2\right),
\]

valid whenever \(0<h\le \ell/4\).

Hence

\[
|G''(x)|
\le
\frac{4\delta}{h^2}
+
C Q^{D_4}h^2.
\]

Choose

\[
h=\left(\delta Q^{-D_4}\right)^{1/4}.
\]

For \(M\) large enough, the previous step gives \(\delta\) so small that

\[
h\le \ell/4.
\]

Then

\[
|G''(x)|
\ll
Q^{D_4/2}\delta^{1/2}.
\]

Since

\[
\delta\le Q^{-M/C_1},
\]

we obtain

\[
\sup_{J'}|G''|
\le
Q^{-M/C_2}
\]

after enlarging \(C_2\).

Thus

\[
\sup_{J'}\left(|G|+|K|+|G''|\right)
\le Q^{-M/C}
\]

for a fixed constant \(C\).

---

# 4. Is order six really enough?

Yes.

The required derivative controls are:

\[
G'\quad\text{for }L^2\to L^\infty\text{ propagation of }G,
\]

\[
K'\quad\text{for }L^2\to L^\infty\text{ propagation of }K,
\]

\[
G^{(4)}\quad\text{for }G\to G''\text{ propagation}.
\]

Now

\[
G=q''-6q+2q^3.
\]

Therefore:

\[
G'\text{ uses }q^{(3)},
\]

\[
G^{(4)}\text{ uses }q^{(6)},
\]

and

\[
K'=2(q')^3+4qq'q''-\frac16G'''
\]

uses \(q^{(5)}\).

So the highest required derivative is \(q^{(6)}\). There is no hidden need for \(q^{(7)}\) or \(q^{(8)}\).

A slightly sharper Landau-Kolmogorov interpolation could probably reduce the formal requirement to order five, because \(G''\) can be interpolated between \(G\) and \(G'''\). But order six is cleaner, elementary, and already aligned with the current Gate-2 package.

---

# 5. Size and location of \(J'\)

The propagation can take \(J'\) to be the **middle half** of \(J\), provided \(M\) is large enough relative to the derivative-complexity exponents and \(|J|\ge Q^{-L}\).

If one wants a statement uniform for all \(M\), use a polynomially large subinterval instead:

\[
|J'|\ge Q^{-C}|J|.
\]

But in the Gate-2 contradiction argument, \(M\) is chosen large at the start. Therefore the middle-half version is acceptable and simpler.

---

# 6. Counterexample checks

## 6.1 Without derivative complexity

The propagation is false.

Take

\[
G(x)=\varepsilon\sin(Nx),
\qquad
K(x)=0.
\]

Then

\[
\int_JG^2\asymp \varepsilon^2|J|,
\]

but

\[
G''(x)=-\varepsilon N^2\sin(Nx).
\]

For \(N\gg\varepsilon^{-1/2}\), \(G''\) is large despite \(G\) being \(L^2\)-small. Thus derivative complexity is essential.

## 6.2 With only \(C^1\) or \(C^2\) control

Still false or insufficient.

Small \(L^2\)-norm and bounded first derivative give small \(G\), but do not control \(G''\). Bounded \(G''\) only gives an upper bound, not smallness. One needs interpolation between small \(G\) and a higher derivative bound.

## 6.3 With \(C^4\) control of \(G\)

Sufficient.

The finite-difference argument above uses \(G^{(4)}\). Since \(G^{(4)}\) is controlled by \(q^{(6)}\), this confirms the order-six package.

---

# 7. Clean theorem for the Gate-2 package

The propagation component should be stated as:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Small }L^2\text{ anisotropy energy plus order-six derivative complexity}
\Rightarrow
\text{pointwise small }(\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2},\Gamma_G'')
\text{ on a subinterval.}
}
\]

More explicitly:

\[
\int_J(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)\,dm
\le Q^{-M}|J|
\]

and

\[
\sup_J|q^{(r)}|\le Q^{C_r},
\qquad 0\le r\le6,
\]

imply that for some

\[
J'\subset J,
\qquad
|J'|\ge c|J|
\]

or at worst

\[
|J'|\ge Q^{-C}|J|,
\]

one has

\[
\sup_{J'}
\left(
|\Gamma_G|+|\Gamma_{G,2}|+|\Gamma_G''|
\right)
\le Q^{-M/C}.
\]

This component is therefore sound. The remaining burden is to prove the derivative-complexity package and then verify the ODE base-locus rigidity lemma against the propagated bounds.

## Agent 4 / D — Far-tail dyadic shell bound

### Verdict

The far-tail estimate closes **conditionally**, but only after making one normalization distinction explicit.

For the Gate-2 derivative-complexity package, the object to control is the full phase-derivative tail in

\[
q_\zeta=B_\zeta+q_{\core}+T_{\far}.
\]

Thus the relevant estimate is

\[
\sup_{I_\rho^\ast}|T_{\far}^{(r)}|
\le Q^{C_r},
\qquad 0\le r\le6.
\]

For a one-zero kernel contributing to \(q_\zeta\), the correct derivative scale is

\[
|K_\nu^{(r)}(m)|\ll_r \Delta_\nu(m)^{-(r+1)}.
\]

The previously quoted \(\Delta^{-(r+2)}\) scale corresponds to one derivative higher, i.e. a \(q_\zeta'\)-level tail. For the \(q''_{\can}=q_\zeta''\) tail, it is \(\Delta^{-(r+3)}\). The current prompt explicitly asks us to determine this normalization because the Gate-2 package now rests on derivative complexity through order six for \(q_\zeta\). 

---

# 1. Kernel derivative exponent

A typical off-line quartet or one-sided packet contribution to the phase derivative has the model form

\[
K_\nu(m)
\asymp
\frac{c_\nu}{(m-\gamma_\nu)^2+c_\nu^2},
\]

up to harmless signs and quartet symmetrization. Define

\[
\Delta_\nu(m)
=
\sqrt{(m-\gamma_\nu)^2+c_\nu^2}.
\]

Then

\[
|K_\nu(m)|\ll \Delta_\nu(m)^{-1}.
\]

Each \(m\)-derivative costs one more power of \(\Delta_\nu^{-1}\), so

\[
\boxed{
|K_\nu^{(r)}(m)|
\ll_r
\Delta_\nu(m)^{-(r+1)}.
}
\]

Therefore:

\[
q_\zeta\text{-level:}\qquad
|K_\nu^{(r)}|\ll_r \Delta^{-(r+1)}.
\]

\[
q_\zeta'\text{-level:}\qquad
|\partial_m^r K_\nu'|
\ll_r \Delta^{-(r+2)}.
\]

\[
q''_{\can}=q_\zeta''\text{-level:}\qquad
|\partial_m^r K_\nu''|
\ll_r \Delta^{-(r+3)}.
\]

For Gate 2, because the sufficient clean package is

\[
\sup_{I_\rho^\ast}|q_\zeta^{(r)}|\le Q^{C_r},
\qquad 0\le r\le6,
\]

we need the **\(q_\zeta\)-level** estimate through \(r=6\):

\[
|K_\nu^{(r)}|\ll_r \Delta_\nu^{-(r+1)}.
\]

---

# 2. Dyadic shell decomposition

Let

\[
R:=\inf_{\nu\notin\mathcal L}\Delta_\nu(I_\rho^\ast),
\]

and assume the near-zero inclusion condition

\[
R\ge Q^{-C_R}.
\]

Decompose omitted zeros into shells

\[
\mathcal S_j
=
\left\{
\nu\notin\mathcal L:
2^jR\le \Delta_\nu(I_\rho^\ast)<2^{j+1}R
\right\}.
\]

Assume the local shell-counting estimate

\[
\boxed{
\#\mathcal S(Y)
:=
\#\{\nu:Y\le\Delta_\nu(I_\rho^\ast)<2Y\}
\ll
Y\log T+Q^{C_0}
}
\]

for \(Y\ge R\), at least up to the range where the local Hadamard/tail decomposition is being used. This is exactly the type of shell input identified as necessary in the latest synthesis. 

Then for \(r\ge1\),

\[
\begin{aligned}
\sup_{I_\rho^\ast}|T_{\far}^{(r)}|
&\ll_r
\sum_{j\ge0}
\#\mathcal S_j\,(2^jR)^{-(r+1)}
\\
&\ll_r
\sum_{j\ge0}
\left(2^jR\log T+Q^{C_0}\right)
(2^jR)^{-(r+1)}
\\
&=
\log T
\sum_{j\ge0}(2^jR)^{-r}
+
Q^{C_0}
\sum_{j\ge0}(2^jR)^{-(r+1)}.
\end{aligned}
\]

For \(r\ge1\), both sums converge geometrically:

\[
\sum_{j\ge0}(2^jR)^{-r}
\ll R^{-r},
\]

\[
\sum_{j\ge0}(2^jR)^{-(r+1)}
\ll R^{-(r+1)}.
\]

Therefore

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{I_\rho^\ast}|T_{\far}^{(r)}|
\ll_r
(\log T)R^{-r}
+
Q^{C_0}R^{-(r+1)},
\qquad 1\le r\le6.
}
\]

If

\[
Q\asymp\log T
\]

and

\[
R\ge Q^{-C_R},
\]

then

\[
\sup_{I_\rho^\ast}|T_{\far}^{(r)}|
\le Q^{C_r},
\qquad 1\le r\le6.
\]

So all **positive derivatives** of the far tail are polynomially controlled.

---

# 3. The \(r=0\) problem

For \(r=0\), the naive absolute sum gives

\[
\sum_{j\ge0}
\#\mathcal S_j\,(2^jR)^{-1}
\ll
\sum_{j\ge0}
\left(\log T+Q^{C_0}(2^jR)^{-1}\right).
\]

The \(Q^{C_0}\)-part converges, but the \(\log T\)-part diverges across infinitely many shells.

Thus:

\[
\boxed{
T_{\far}\text{ itself is not absolutely controlled by the local shell bound alone.}
}
\]

For \(r=0\), one needs one of the following:

1. **Completed-phase/background subtraction**, where the non-absolutely-convergent bulk is absorbed into \(B_\zeta\);

2. **Symmetric regularization of the zero sum**, so the paired far-shell contribution has cancellation;

3. **Finite-height truncation plus explicit background**, with the truncation error differentiated/regularized;

4. A direct good-patch bound for \(T_{\far}\) as part of the decomposition.

This is not a problem for \(r\ge1\), but Gate 2 also wants \(|q|\le Q^C\), so \(r=0\) must be handled by the completed-phase normalization, not by raw absolute summation.

This matches the broader paper status: the zero-side representation must fix all background, tail, source/core, and regularization conventions before it can be used as canonical actual-zeta data. 

---

# 4. Conditional far-tail theorem

A sharp conditional theorem is:

Let

\[
q_\zeta=B_\zeta+q_{\core}+T_{\far}
\]

be the completed, regularized local zero-side decomposition on \(I_\rho^\ast\). Assume:

\[
\inf_{\nu\notin\mathcal L}\Delta_\nu(I_\rho^\ast)
\ge R\ge Q^{-C_R},
\]

and for every dyadic \(Y\ge R\),

\[
\#\{\nu:Y\le\Delta_\nu(I_\rho^\ast)<2Y\}
\ll Y\log T+Q^{C_0}.
\]

Then for \(1\le r\le6\),

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{I_\rho^\ast}|T_{\far}^{(r)}|
\ll_r
(\log T)R^{-r}
+
Q^{C_0}R^{-(r+1)}
\le Q^{C_r}.
}
\]

For \(r=0\), the same conclusion holds provided \(T_{\far}\) is interpreted as a **completed/regularized tail after subtracting the background bulk**, or provided an independent good-patch bound

\[
\sup_{I_\rho^\ast}|T_{\far}|\le Q^{C_0'}
\]

is included.

---

# 5. What local zero-counting theorem is needed?

The needed theorem is local and dyadic:

\[
\boxed{
N(I_\rho^\ast;Y,2Y)
:=
\#\{\nu:Y\le\Delta_\nu(I_\rho^\ast)<2Y\}
\ll
Y\log T+Q^{C_0}.
}
\]

The additive \(Q^{C_0}\) term is important for very small \(Y\), since \(Y\log T\) may be \(<1\) when \(Y\ll1/\log T\). This estimate is compatible with Riemann–von Mangoldt-type counting, but if the draft only states global counting and not local shell occupancy, it should be recorded as a local-counting input.

Quartet closure only changes constants: each packet has at most boundedly many functional-equation/conjugation partners.

---

# 6. Weakest tail cutoff condition

For \(1\le r\le6\), it is enough that the omitted tail begins at polynomial distance:

\[
\boxed{
R\ge Q^{-C_R}.
}
\]

Then

\[
(\log T)R^{-r}
+
Q^{C_0}R^{-(r+1)}
\]

is polynomial in \(Q\).

For \(r=0\), polynomial cutoff alone is **not enough** unless the zero-side tail is regularized. The raw absolute tail diverges logarithmically over infinitely many shells.

So the weakest complete package is:

\[
R\ge Q^{-C_R}
\]

plus

\[
\text{completed-phase regularization/background subtraction for }T_{\far}.
\]

---

# 7. Failure mode

If a zero is left in the tail with sub-polynomial distance

\[
\Delta_\nu(I_\rho^\ast)<Q^{-C}
\]

for arbitrarily large \(C\), then even the \(q_\zeta\)-level derivative estimate fails:

\[
|K_\nu^{(6)}|
\gg
\Delta_\nu^{-7},
\]

which is super-polynomial. For \(q''_{\can}\)-level derivatives, the failure is even worse:

\[
|\partial_m^r K_\nu''|
\gg
\Delta_\nu^{-(r+3)}.
\]

Therefore the core/tail split must include every zero or packet within polynomial distance of \(I_\rho^\ast\). The latest synthesis already identifies this as the key risk: a single near zero misclassified into the tail destroys derivative complexity. 

---

# Final conclusion

For Agent 4’s branch:

\[
\boxed{
\text{The far-tail derivative estimate closes for }1\le r\le6
\text{ under polynomial tail cutoff and dyadic local zero-counting.}
}
\]

The only caveat is \(r=0\): raw absolute convergence fails, so \(T_{\far}\) must be understood as a completed/regularized tail with the divergent bulk absorbed into \(B_\zeta\), or else \(\sup |T_{\far}|\le Q^C\) must be assumed separately.

Thus the far-tail part of derivative complexity is not a deep obstruction. The required conditions are:

\[
R\ge Q^{-C_R},
\]

\[
\#\{\nu:Y\le\Delta_\nu<2Y\}
\ll Y\log T+Q^{C_0},
\]

and a completed-phase regularization for the \(r=0\) tail.

## Assistant (2026-04-26 13:46:51)

I’ll analyze the singular/near-packet regime separately from the smooth good-patch proof. The point is to see whether very small denominators automatically force Gate 2, or whether they create a separate cancellation problem.

## Agent 4 / D — Alternative proof of Gate 2 without core denominator separation

### Verdict

Denominator separation is **not logically necessary** for Gate 2, but it is necessary for the current **smooth good-patch proof**.

If a core packet has

\[
\Delta_\nu(I_\rho^\ast)\ll Q^{-C}
\]

for every fixed \(C\), then the order-six derivative-complexity package fails. However, this does **not automatically mean Gate 2 fails**. A very near packet typically creates enormous source and anisotropy signals, so Gate 2 should become easier unless there is a highly tuned same-scale cancellation.

Thus the right classification is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate 2 should split into a smooth denominator-separated regime and a singular near-packet regime.}
}
\]

The smooth regime is handled by the existing derivative-complexity/Remez/ODE package. The singular regime needs a separate lower-bound theorem. Without such a theorem, simply imposing denominator separation may exclude shallow off-line packets and is therefore a substantive assumption, not just harmless bookkeeping. The attached instruction asks exactly whether a near packet automatically gives Gate 2 or whether cancellation can still defeat it. The answer is: **automatic unless same-scale cancellation is allowed; same-scale cancellation remains the danger.** 

---

# 1. Local singular-packet model

Let a packet have transverse depth \(c\) and ordinate center \(\gamma\), and write

\[
x=m-\gamma,
\qquad
d(m)=\sqrt{x^2+c^2}.
\]

A typical positive local phase-derivative kernel has the model form

\[
K(m)\asymp \frac{c}{x^2+c^2}.
\]

Near the packet center,

\[
K(0)\asymp c^{-1},
\]

and

\[
K^{(r)}(0)\asymp c^{-(r+1)}.
\]

Thus, if this packet contributes dominantly to \(q=q_\zeta\), then at \(m=\gamma\)

\[
q\asymp c^{-1},
\]

\[
q''\asymp c^{-3},
\]

\[
q^{(4)}\asymp c^{-5},
\]

and in general

\[
q^{(r)}\asymp c^{-(r+1)}.
\]

So derivative complexity through order six fails if

\[
c\ll Q^{-C}
\]

for every fixed \(C\).

But Gate 2 asks for

\[
\int_I |u|^2(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)\,dm,
\qquad
u=q''_{\can}.
\]

If the singular packet is not cancelled, this integral is enormous.

---

# 2. Single dominant packet gives Gate 2 automatically

Use the model

\[
q(x)=\frac{c}{x^2+c^2}.
\]

At \(x=0\),

\[
q(0)=c^{-1},
\]

\[
u(0)=q''(0)=-2c^{-3},
\]

\[
q^{(4)}(0)=24c^{-5}.
\]

Then

\[
\Gamma_G
=
u-6q+2q^3.
\]

At \(x=0\),

\[
\Gamma_G(0)
=
-2c^{-3}-6c^{-1}+2c^{-3}
=
-6c^{-1}.
\]

So even though the leading \(c^{-3}\) terms cancel in \(\Gamma_G\), a large lower-order signal remains:

\[
|\Gamma_G(0)|\asymp c^{-1}.
\]

Also

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}
=
(1-q^2)u-\frac16q^{(4)}.
\]

At \(x=0\),

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}(0)
=
(1-c^{-2})(-2c^{-3})-4c^{-5}
=
-2c^{-3}-2c^{-5}.
\]

So

\[
|\Gamma_{G,2}(0)|\asymp c^{-5}.
\]

Therefore the pointwise Gate-2 integrand near the center has size at least

\[
|u|^2\Gamma_{G,2}^2
\asymp
c^{-6}c^{-10}
=
c^{-16}.
\]

On a subinterval of length \(\asymp c\), this contributes

\[
\int |u|^2\Gamma_{G,2}^2
\gg c^{-15}.
\]

If

\[
c<Q^{-C}
\]

with \(C\) large, then

\[
c^{-15}\gg Q^A
\]

for any fixed \(A\). Thus Gate 2 is not merely true; it is violently true.

### Conclusion

A single near singular packet is not dangerous. It is a large-signal regime.

---

# 3. The dangerous case is cancellation among same-scale packets

The only way a near denominator can fail to give Gate 2 automatically is if the singular contributions cancel in both:

\[
u=q''_{\can},
\]

and

\[
(\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2}).
\]

This requires other packets at comparable scale. If all other packets are farther away by a polynomial factor, they cannot cancel the dominant powers

\[
c^{-3},\quad c^{-5},\quad c^{-7}.
\]

So dangerous cancellation requires a same-scale cluster:

\[
\Delta_{\nu_j}(I_\rho^\ast)\asymp c
\]

with several packets whose contributions tune the finite jet package of \(q\).

This is essentially the same phenomenon as the same-scale packet quadrature no-go:

\[
q''=q^{(4)}=\cdots=q^{(2M)}=0
\]

or, more generally, finite-jet tuning of

\[
u,\quad \Gamma_G,\quad \Gamma_{G,2}.
\]

The singular regime therefore does not create a new analytic obstruction; it recreates the old arithmetic/local-quadrature obstruction at a smaller scale.

---

# 4. Can large packet terms cancel in \(q''_{\can}\) and anisotropy?

Yes, at least formally.

The same-scale positive packet construction already shows that local packet geometry can flatten source derivatives while keeping \(q_0>0\). In a singular same-scale cluster, the same mechanism can be rescaled.

A finite cluster at scale \(c\) can make certain normalized moments vanish:

\[
q''(\gamma),\quad q^{(4)}(\gamma),\quad \ldots
\]

or tune them to prescribed values up to finite order. Since

\[
\Gamma_G=u-6q+2q^3
\]

and

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}=(1-q^2)u-\frac16q^{(4)},
\]

vanishing or smallness of \(\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2}\) imposes finite algebraic constraints on the same local jets.

Therefore, without an anti-quadrature theorem, one cannot assert that singular clusters automatically force Gate 2. One can assert only:

\[
\boxed{
\text{A single dominant near packet, or a non-cancelling near cluster, forces Gate 2.}
}
\]

The remaining bad case is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{a near same-scale cluster that cancels source and anisotropy jets.}
}
\]

---

# 5. A useful two-regime theorem

The right replacement for denominator separation is a two-regime theorem.

## Regime S: smooth denominator-separated regime

Assume

\[
\inf_{\nu\in\mathcal L_R^{\der}}
\inf_{m\in I_\rho^\ast}
\Delta_\nu(m)
\ge Q^{-C_{\sep}}.
\]

Then the derivative-complexity package applies:

\[
\sup_{I_\rho^\ast}|q_\zeta^{(r)}|\le Q^{C_r},
\qquad 0\le r\le6.
\]

Together with Gate 1, source-mass thickening, propagation, and ODE base-locus rigidity, this gives Gate 2:

\[
\int_{I_\rho}|u|^2(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)\,dm
\ge Q^{-A}|I_\rho|.
\]

## Regime N: near-packet regime

Assume there exists a packet \(\nu\) with

\[
\Delta_\nu(I_\rho^\ast)<Q^{-C}
\]

for arbitrarily large \(C\).

Then either:

### N1. Non-cancelling near packet

There is a subinterval \(J\subset I_\rho\) of length comparable to the packet scale \(c\), or with polynomial overlap if the packet center is slightly off interval, such that

\[
|u|\max(|\Gamma_G|,|\Gamma_{G,2}|)
\ge Q^A
\]

for any prescribed fixed \(A\), once \(C\) is large enough.

Then Gate 2 follows immediately.

### N2. Cancelling near cluster

The near-packet singular terms cancel so strongly that

\[
u,\quad \Gamma_G,\quad \Gamma_{G,2}
\]

are all polynomially small on the relevant part of \(I_\rho\).

Then the proof has not gained anything from singularity. This is a rescaled same-scale quadrature problem and must be handled by arithmetic or anti-quadrature input.

Thus the near-packet theorem should be:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Either near-packet non-cancellation gives Gate 2, or one has a same-scale finite-jet cancellation certificate.}
}
\]

---

# 6. Is denominator separation genuinely necessary?

For the current smooth proof, yes.

The derivative-complexity step fails without

\[
\Delta_\nu(I_\rho^\ast)\ge Q^{-C}.
\]

In particular,

\[
|q_\zeta^{(6)}|\asymp \Delta^{-7}
\]

is super-polynomial if \(\Delta\) is super-polynomially small.

But for the theorem itself, denominator separation is probably **not necessary**. Near singularities are usually favorable because they produce huge row signals.

So the correct statement is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Denominator separation is a proof-regime assumption, not a theorem-level necessity.}
}
\]

It should not be imposed globally unless the excluded near-packet regime is separately treated.

---

# 7. Does imposing \(c_P\ge Q^{-C_{\sep}}\) smuggle in zero-free-strip information?

Potentially yes.

If the distinguished off-line packet has transverse depth

\[
c_P=|\Re\rho-\tfrac12|
\]

or a comparable denominator parameter, then requiring

\[
c_P\ge Q^{-C_{\sep}}
\]

excludes off-line zeros super-polynomially close to the critical line.

That is a substantive assumption. It resembles a local zero-free-strip condition around the critical line, not merely a coordinate convenience.

Since RH must rule out all off-line zeros, including arbitrarily shallow ones, the proof cannot simply discard

\[
c_P\ll Q^{-C}
\]

unless it proves these are easier or impossible.

Therefore:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Shallow off-line packets require either a separate large-signal proof or a separate arithmetic exclusion.}
}
\]

---

# 8. Final answer to Agent 4’s task

Can Gate 2 be proved without core denominator separation?

### Yes, in non-cancelling singular regimes.

A near packet usually makes

\[
q,\quad q'',\quad q^{(4)},\quad \Gamma_G,\quad \Gamma_{G,2}
\]

large enough to force Gate 2 immediately.

### No, not in full generality from current inputs.

If a same-scale near cluster cancels the singular jets, then derivative complexity is unavailable and automatic largeness may fail. This bad case reduces to the same-scale quadrature obstruction already identified.

### Therefore

The architecture should use a two-regime split:

\[
\boxed{
\text{smooth denominator-separated Gate 2}
}
\]

plus

\[
\boxed{
\text{singular near-packet non-cancellation or anti-quadrature theorem.}
}
\]

Without the second branch, denominator separation is a serious unclosed assumption, not a harmless analytic patch.
