## Assistant (2026-04-26 13:51:13)

I’ll work in rescaled singular coordinates. The decisive question is whether the \(c^{-3}\) and \(c^{-5}\) singular powers create a new obstruction, or whether they factor out and leave the same finite positive-quadrature problem.

_Thought for 35s_

## Agent 4 / D — Same-scale singular anti-quadrature

### Verdict

In the singular same-scale regime, the large powers of \(c^{-1}\) **factor out** after rescaling. This means singularity alone does not create a new arithmetic obstruction. The relevant finite-jet equations become scale-invariant.

However, there is an important distinction:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Source flattening in the singular regime is still locally possible.}
}
\]

That is the same quadrature obstruction as before, now rescaled.

But:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Conditional on Gate 1 source mass, simultaneous Gate 2 anisotropy cancellation is locally obstructed at leading singular order.}
}
\]

So the singular regime does **not** create a new Gate 2 obstruction beyond the old Gate 1 source-flatness/quadrature problem. This supports the current synthesis: continue with a smooth/singular split, but do not silently impose denominator separation globally. 

---

# 1. Rescaling the singular same-scale cluster

Let the near cluster have common scale

\[
\Delta_{\nu_j}\asymp c,
\qquad
c\ll Q^{-C}
\]

for every fixed \(C\). Write

\[
m=\gamma_0+cx,
\]

and model each positive packet by

\[
K_{\nu_j}(m)
=
\frac{c d_j}{(m-\gamma_j)^2+c^2d_j^2},
\qquad
\gamma_j=\gamma_0+ca_j.
\]

Then

\[
K_{\nu_j}(m)
=
c^{-1}
\frac{d_j}{(x-a_j)^2+d_j^2}.
\]

Thus the near-cluster profile has the form

\[
q_{\near}(m)=c^{-1}Q(x),
\]

where

\[
Q(x)=
\sum_j w_j
\frac{d_j}{(x-a_j)^2+d_j^2}
\]

with positive weights in the positive-packet model.

Because

\[
\frac{d}{dm}=c^{-1}\frac{d}{dx},
\]

we get

\[
q_{\near}^{(r)}(m)=c^{-1-r}Q^{(r)}(x).
\]

In particular,

\[
q_{\near}=c^{-1}Q,
\]

\[
u_{\near}=q_{\near}''=c^{-3}Q'',
\]

\[
q_{\near}^{(4)}=c^{-5}Q^{(4)}.
\]

So the singular powers are explicit and homogeneous.

---

# 2. Rescaled anisotropy equations

Recall

\[
\Gamma_G=u-6q+2q^3,
\]

and

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}=(1-q^2)u-\frac16q^{(4)}.
\]

Substituting

\[
q=c^{-1}Q,
\qquad
u=c^{-3}Q'',
\qquad
q^{(4)}=c^{-5}Q^{(4)},
\]

gives

\[
\Gamma_G
=
c^{-3}
\left(
Q''+2Q^3-6c^2Q
\right).
\]

Thus the leading singular Gram-anisotropy equation is

\[
\boxed{
F_1(Q):=Q''+2Q^3.
}
\]

Similarly,

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}
=
(1-c^{-2}Q^2)c^{-3}Q''
-\frac16c^{-5}Q^{(4)}.
\]

So

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}
=
c^{-5}
\left(
-Q^2Q''-\frac16Q^{(4)}
+c^2Q''
\right).
\]

The leading singular second-anisotropy equation is

\[
\boxed{
F_2(Q):=-Q^2Q''-\frac16Q^{(4)}.
}
\]

Gate 2’s integrand has leading size

\[
|u|^2(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)
\sim
c^{-6}
\left(
c^{-6}Q''^{\,2}F_1(Q)^2
+
c^{-10}Q''^{\,2}F_2(Q)^2
\right).
\]

Since \(dm=c\,dx\), the local singular contribution is

\[
\int |u|^2(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)\,dm
\sim
c^{-11}\int Q''^{\,2}F_1(Q)^2\,dx
+
c^{-15}\int Q''^{\,2}F_2(Q)^2\,dx.
\]

Therefore, unless the normalized functions \(Q'',F_1,F_2\) are tuned small, the Gate 2 integral is enormous.

---

# 3. Positive same-scale quadrature can still flatten the source

The known same-scale positive packet quadrature survives rescaling.

A continuous positive same-scale distribution can make

\[
Q(x)\equiv \text{constant}
\]

on the local normalized interval, or can match this through any finite jet order by finite quadrature.

Then

\[
Q''=Q^{(4)}=\cdots=0.
\]

Consequently,

\[
u_{\near}=c^{-3}Q''=0
\]

at the matched jet level.

This is exactly the old source-flatness obstruction, now at singular scale.

So local positive geometry still cannot prove Gate 1. It can still create source-flatness by finite quadrature.

### Important distinction

This source-flattening does **not** produce a new Gate 2 counterexample under Gate 1. It kills \(u\) itself. Therefore it threatens Gate 1, not the Gate 1 \(\Rightarrow\) Gate 2 transfer.

---

# 4. Conditional on source mass, simultaneous anisotropy cancellation is locally obstructed

Suppose instead that Gate 1 has source mass at the singular scale, so \(Q''\) is not negligible on a normalized set.

To make Gate 2 fail despite \(Q''\)-mass, one would need

\[
F_1(Q)\approx0,
\qquad
F_2(Q)\approx0
\]

where \(Q''\) is large.

The exact leading equations are

\[
Q''+2Q^3=0,
\]

and

\[
-Q^2Q''-\frac16Q^{(4)}=0.
\]

From the first equation,

\[
Q''=-2Q^3.
\]

Differentiate twice:

\[
Q'''=-6Q^2Q',
\]

and

\[
Q^{(4)}
=
-12Q(Q')^2-6Q^2Q''.
\]

Using

\[
Q''=-2Q^3,
\]

this becomes

\[
Q^{(4)}
=
-12Q(Q')^2+12Q^5.
\]

Substitute into \(F_2=0\):

\[
0
=
-Q^2(-2Q^3)
-\frac16\left(-12Q(Q')^2+12Q^5\right).
\]

Thus

\[
0
=
2Q^5+2Q(Q')^2-2Q^5
=
2Q(Q')^2.
\]

Since the positive-packet profile satisfies

\[
Q>0,
\]

we get

\[
Q'=0.
\]

Then

\[
Q''=0.
\]

But the first equation also requires

\[
Q''=-2Q^3.
\]

Hence

\[
Q=0,
\]

contradicting positivity.

Therefore there is no nontrivial positive smooth profile satisfying

\[
F_1(Q)=F_2(Q)=0
\]

on an interval.

### Consequence

The normalized singular base locus

\[
Q''\ne0,
\qquad
F_1(Q)=0,
\qquad
F_2(Q)=0
\]

is locally empty for positive profiles.

So once source mass is present, singular same-scale anisotropy cancellation is harder than the nonsingular case, not easier.

---

# 5. Does quartet symmetry help or obstruct cancellation?

Quartet symmetry does not materially change the scale analysis.

After rescaling, quartet closure modifies the admissible packet family by imposing symmetric partners and perhaps changing the exact positive kernel profile. But the leading singular form remains a finite positive superposition of same-scale rational kernels.

Thus:

- quartet symmetry does **not** obstruct source flattening by finite positive quadrature;
- quartet symmetry does **not** rescue a simultaneous \(F_1=F_2=0\) base-locus once source mass is present;
- quartet symmetry mainly changes constants and admissible parameter families.

So the singular branch remains governed by the same finite positive quadrature geometry at Gate 1, plus the leading ODE incompatibility at Gate 2.

---

# 6. Does singular scaling make cancellation harder, easier, or invariant?

It depends on which cancellation.

## Source cancellation

For source flattening,

\[
u=c^{-3}Q'',
\]

so the singular power \(c^{-3}\) factors out. One needs

\[
Q''\approx0.
\]

This is scale-invariant. Singular scaling does **not** make source cancellation harder.

Therefore the Gate 1 anti-quadrature problem is unchanged.

## Anisotropy cancellation under source mass

For Gate 2 cancellation, the relevant leading equations are

\[
F_1(Q)=Q''+2Q^3\approx0,
\]

\[
F_2(Q)=-Q^2Q''-\frac16Q^{(4)}\approx0.
\]

These are also scale-invariant after factoring out \(c^{-3}\) and \(c^{-5}\), but they are structurally incompatible with positive nonzero source mass.

Thus singular scaling does not itself solve the problem, but it reveals a stronger leading-order obstruction to Gate 2 failure.

---

# 7. Exact anti-quadrature theorem needed

The singular regime needs an arithmetic theorem only for **source flattening**, not for a new Gate 2 anisotropy cancellation, at least at leading order.

The required theorem is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Actual zeta zeros cannot realize a positive same-scale cluster whose normalized profile }Q
\text{ satisfies }Q''\approx0
\text{ on the relevant normalized interval.}
}
\]

More generally, if source flatness across an interval requires finite-jet cancellation through order \(R\), the theorem should exclude:

\[
Q^{(2)}(x_0),\,
Q^{(3)}(x_0),\,
\ldots,\,
Q^{(R+2)}(x_0)
\approx0
\]

for the actual zeta near-cluster profile, with the appropriate same-scale packet restrictions.

This is essentially the same Gate 1 anti-quadrature theorem already identified. It is not a new Gate 2 theorem.

If Gate 1 is assumed true, then the singular same-scale cluster cannot be source-flat enough; once \(Q''\)-mass is present, the leading \(F_1,F_2\) incompatibility blocks simultaneous anisotropy cancellation.

---

# 8. Final classification

The singular same-scale branch should be classified as follows:

## Case A — Non-source-flat singular cluster

\[
Q''\text{ has polynomial normalized mass.}
\]

Then the large singular factors force Gate 2 unless

\[
F_1(Q),F_2(Q)
\]

are simultaneously tiny on the \(Q''\)-mass. Local ODE algebra shows this is impossible for a positive profile except with additional degeneracy forcing \(Q=0\). Thus Gate 2 is locally secure.

## Case B — Source-flat singular cluster

\[
Q''\approx0
\]

through the finite order needed on the interval.

Then Gate 1 itself is threatened. This is the old same-scale quadrature obstruction in rescaled variables.

## Case C — Signed or non-positive correction terms at singular scale

If same-scale correction terms with effective negative weights are allowed, then the positivity argument weakens. In that case the local ODE contradiction above may fail, and one would need a signed anti-cancellation theorem. But for the positive zero-packet geometry used in the same-scale quadrature model, positivity is enough.

---

# Final answer

Singular same-scale cancellation does **not** create a fundamentally new Gate 2 obstruction.

After rescaling

\[
m=\gamma+cx,
\qquad
q_{\near}=c^{-1}Q(x),
\]

the large powers of \(c^{-1}\) factor out. Source cancellation becomes the old scale-invariant condition

\[
Q''\approx0,
\]

which is locally possible by positive same-scale quadrature and remains an arithmetic Gate 1 obstruction.

But if Gate 1 supplies \(Q''\)-mass, then Gate 2 cancellation would require the leading equations

\[
Q''+2Q^3\approx0,
\qquad
-Q^2Q''-\frac16Q^{(4)}\approx0.
\]

The exact equations are incompatible for positive nonzero \(Q\), since they imply

\[
2Q(Q')^2=0,
\]

hence \(Q'=0\), hence \(Q''=0\), hence \(Q=0\).

Thus:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Singular Gate 2 reduces to Gate 1 anti-quadrature, not to a new obstruction.}
}
\]

The remaining arithmetic theorem is still the same one: actual zeta must forbid the relevant same-scale source-flattening quadrature pattern.

## Assistant (2026-04-26 13:56:52)

## Agent 4 / D — Numerical test design for Gate 1 across ordinary and singular scales

### Verdict

A useful numerical program should not try to “verify RH.” It should test the specific Gate 1 obstruction:

\[
E_I
=
|I|^{-1}\int_I |q''_{\can}(m)|^2\,dm
\]

on packet-scale intervals, and compare actual-zeta behavior against deliberately adversarial same-scale quadrature controls.

The current architecture has reduced the hard part to Gate 1 actual-zeta source-curvature observability. Smooth Gate 2 is now local analysis, while singular Gate 2 reduces back to Gate 1 anti-quadrature after rescaling. The latest coordinator note explicitly frames the next target as actual-zeta source-curvature observability in both ordinary and singular scales. 

---

# 1. Canonical numerical object

The object to measure is

\[
q''_{\can}(m)=q_\zeta''(m)=\Phi_\zeta'''(m).
\]

Numerically, compute it in two independent ways.

## A. Zero-side representation

Use a regularized zero-side formula

\[
q''_{\can}(m)
=
B_2(m)+\sum_{\rho}^{\rm reg}K_2(m;\rho).
\]

Here:

- \(B_2(m)\) is the differentiated gamma/background/completion contribution;
- \(K_2(m;\rho)\) is the second \(m\)-derivative of the local phase-derivative kernel attached to a zero or quartet;
- the sum must use a fixed regularization convention, otherwise the far-tail/background split contaminates \(q''_{\can}\).

For an off-line packet model with transverse depth \(c\) and ordinate \(\gamma\), the local positive model is

\[
K(m)=\frac{c}{(m-\gamma)^2+c^2},
\]

so

\[
K''(m)
=
\frac{2c(3(m-\gamma)^2-c^2)}
{\bigl((m-\gamma)^2+c^2\bigr)^3}.
\]

This is the prototype contribution to \(q''_{\can}\).

## B. Prime/AFE representation

Use

\[
q''_{\can}(m)
=
B_2(m)+P_2(m)+D_2(m)+E_2(m),
\]

where

\[
P_2(m)
=
\Re\sum_{n\le X}
a_n e^{-im\log n}
\]

with fixed actual-zeta/AFE coefficients, including the \((\log n)^2\)-type weights coming from two \(m\)-derivatives. \(D_2\) is the dual term, and \(E_2\) is the differentiated truncation/smoothing error.

The AFE computation is mainly a consistency and recurrence test. The zero-side computation is the cleaner way to scan around zero packets if verified zeros are available.

---

# 2. Required data

## For the zero-side scan

Need:

1. Verified zeros \(\rho=\beta+i\gamma\), including enough zeros beyond the scan window to regularize the tail.
2. A convention for quartet grouping:
   \[
   \rho,\quad 1-\rho,\quad \bar\rho,\quad 1-\bar\rho.
   \]
3. The gamma/background term \(B_2(m)\).
4. Tail cutoff \(Y_{\max}\) and a bound for the omitted regularized tail.
5. Interval scale convention:
   \[
   I=[m_0-c_I/Q,m_0+c_I/Q]
   \]
   in the ordinary scan, and
   \[
   I=[\gamma-c_xc,\gamma+c_xc]
   \]
   in synthetic singular scans.

## For the prime/AFE scan

Need:

1. Height \(T\) and \(m\)-window.
2. AFE length \(X\sim \sqrt{T/2\pi}\), or the paper’s smoothing-specific length.
3. Coefficients \(a_n\), with differentiated weights.
4. Smoothing function \(W(n/T)\).
5. Dual term \(D_2\), including \(\chi\)- or \(\theta\)-derivatives.
6. Error model for \(E_2\) after two \(m\)-derivatives.

---

# 3. Diagnostics

For every interval \(I\), compute

\[
S_I=\sup_{m\in I}|q''_{\can}(m)|,
\]

\[
E_I=|I|^{-1}\int_I|q''_{\can}(m)|^2\,dm,
\]

and

\[
B_I^{\rm eff}
=
-\frac{\log E_I}{\log Q}.
\]

Interpretation:

- \(B_I^{\rm eff}=O(1)>0\): polynomial flatness; potentially compatible with Gate 1 if bounded.
- \(B_I^{\rm eff}\to+\infty\): super-polynomial source flatness; serious threat.
- \(B_I^{\rm eff}<0\): source curvature is growing with \(Q\); Gate 1 is numerically healthy.

Also compute finite-jet diagnostics at the interval center:

\[
J_r(I)
=
\Delta^r\frac{d^r}{dm^r}q''_{\can}(m_0),
\qquad 0\le r\le R,
\]

where

\[
\Delta=|I|/2.
\]

A source-flat interval should show simultaneous smallness of \(J_r\) for \(r\le R\), not just \(J_0\).

---

# 4. Experiment 1 — Ordinary \(Q^{-1}\)-scale actual-zeta scan

### Purpose

Test whether actual zeta shows source-flat intervals at the ordinary packet scale.

### Intervals

Use

\[
I_j=[m_j-c_I/Q_j,m_j+c_I/Q_j],
\]

with

\[
Q_j\asymp \log m_j
\]

or the paper’s local \(Q\)-definition.

Choose \(m_j\) from:

1. Gram points;
2. midpoints between consecutive critical zeros;
3. neighborhoods of unusually small gaps;
4. random points in a height band;
5. if off-line surrogate packets are being tested, centers attached to inserted hypothetical packets.

### Computation

For each \(I_j\):

1. Compute \(q''_{\can}\) using zero-side regularized sums.
2. Repeat using AFE for a subset as a consistency check.
3. Numerically integrate with adaptive quadrature or high-order Gauss-Legendre sampling.
4. Record \(S_I,E_I,B_I^{\rm eff}\).
5. Record low finite jets \(J_0,\ldots,J_R\).

### Expected support for Gate 1

Gate 1 is supported if, across many intervals and increasing heights,

\[
E_I\ge Q^{-B_0}
\]

for a stable moderate \(B_0\), with no trend toward

\[
B_I^{\rm eff}\to+\infty.
\]

### Threat

Gate 1 is threatened if intervals appear with

\[
E_I\ll Q^{-B}
\]

for growing \(B\), especially if finite jets \(J_0,\ldots,J_R\) are simultaneously small.

---

# 5. Experiment 2 — Singular/shallow-scale synthetic packet scan

### Purpose

Test the singular branch:

\[
m=\gamma+cx,
\qquad
q_{\near}=c^{-1}Q(x).
\]

This is not actual zeta; it is a controlled model to check the predicted dichotomy:

\[
\text{dominance}\Rightarrow \text{huge Gate 2 signal},
\]

\[
\text{cancellation}\Rightarrow \text{source-flat quadrature}.
\]

### Synthetic model

Build

\[
q(m)=\sum_j w_j\frac{c_j}{(m-\gamma_j)^2+c_j^2}+q_{\mathrm{bg}}(m).
\]

For same-scale singular packets, set

\[
\gamma_j=\gamma_0+ca_j,
\qquad
c_j=cd_j.
\]

Then

\[
q(m)=c^{-1}Q(x)+q_{\mathrm{bg}}(m).
\]

Scan \(c\) over:

\[
10^{-2},10^{-4},10^{-8},10^{-16}
\]

or symbolic rescaled values.

### Measurements

Compute:

\[
u=q'',
\]

\[
\Gamma_G=u-6q+2q^3,
\]

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}=(1-q^2)u-\frac16q^{(4)}.
\]

Record:

\[
E_I=|I|^{-1}\int_I|u|^2,
\]

and

\[
V_I=|I|^{-1}\int_I|u|^2(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2).
\]

### Expected result

For a single dominant packet:

\[
E_I\asymp c^{-6},
\]

and

\[
V_I\asymp c^{-16}
\]

at density level, or integrated over length \(c\),

\[
\int_I |u|^2(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)\,dm
\asymp c^{-15}.
\]

So singular dominance should be numerically obvious.

If source flattening is imposed by quadrature, \(E_I\) should collapse. That confirms the branch reduces to Gate 1.

---

# 6. Experiment 3 — Same-scale quadrature negative control

### Purpose

Verify the numerical pipeline detects a known adversary.

Use a positive same-scale packet distribution designed to flatten \(q''\).

A continuous model is a same-radius distribution

\[
x=d\cos\theta,
\qquad
c=d\sin\theta,
\]

with positive density chosen so that the aggregate profile is constant near the center.

Numerically approximate it by finite quadrature:

\[
q_{\quad}(m)
=
\sum_{j=1}^N w_j
\frac{c_j}{(m-x_j)^2+c_j^2}.
\]

Choose weights \(w_j>0\) to match finite jet conditions:

\[
q_{\quad}^{(2)}(0)=q_{\quad}^{(3)}(0)=\cdots=q_{\quad}^{(R+2)}(0)=0
\]

or minimize

\[
\sum_{r=0}^{R}
\left|
d^{r+2}q_{\quad}^{(r+2)}(0)
\right|^2.
\]

Then scan

\[
I=[-c_I d,c_I d].
\]

### Expected result

The negative control should produce:

\[
E_I\ll 1
\]

and large positive

\[
B_I^{\rm eff}.
\]

If the code fails to see this, the numerical method is not sensitive enough to detect the adversary.

---

# 7. Distinguishing actual zeta from surrogates

Use four comparison classes:

## A. Actual-zero scan

Uses verified zeta zeros and real \(B_2\)/regularization.

If no source-flat intervals appear, this supports Gate 1.

## B. Random same-density zero surrogate

Use zero ordinates with the same local density but randomized packet angles/depths.

If random surrogates do not flatten either, the evidence is weak: flattening may simply be rare.

## C. Adversarial same-scale quadrature

Explicitly constructed to flatten.

If this flattens but actual zeta does not, this supports the claim that actual arithmetic forbids the adversary.

## D. Fixed-prime/AFE phase surrogate

Keep AFE amplitudes and frequencies, but vary phases or sample over \(m\).

If this surrogate finds source-flat finite-jet recurrences while actual zeta does not, then the off-line-center/actual-zero compatibility is doing work.

If actual zeta behaves like the surrogate and source-flat intervals appear, Gate 1 is threatened.

---

# 8. Practical pseudocode

```text
for each height band [T, T+H]:
    Q = log(T)
    load verified zeros in expanded window [T-Htail, T+H+Htail]
    precompute background B2(m)
    for each candidate center m0:
        I = [m0 - cI/Q, m0 + cI/Q]
        sample m_k in I
        q2_k_zero = B2(m_k) + regularized_sum_K2(m_k, zeros)
        E_I = mean(|q2_k_zero|^2)
        S_I = max(|q2_k_zero|)
        B_eff = -log(E_I)/log(Q)
        compute scaled finite jets J_r at m0
        store diagnostics

for synthetic singular scale c:
    build q(m)=sum_j w_j c_j/((m-gamma_j)^2+c_j^2)
    compute q'', q^(4), Gamma_G, Gamma_G2
    compute E_I and V_I on I=[gamma-cx*c, gamma+cx*c]

for quadrature negative control:
    solve positive or constrained least-squares weights w_j
    enforce q^(2),...,q^(R+2) small at 0
    compute E_I and compare to actual-zeta scans
```

---

# 9. Numerical outcomes and interpretation

## Supports Gate 1

- Actual-zeta scans show
  \[
  B_I^{\rm eff}
  \]
  bounded above by a moderate constant.
- No interval shows simultaneous finite-jet flattening.
- Adversarial quadrature controls do flatten, proving the test has sensitivity.
- AFE and zero-side computations agree within the error budget.

## Threatens Gate 1

- Actual-zeta intervals show increasing
  \[
  B_I^{\rm eff}
  \]
  with height.
- Several consecutive scaled jets satisfy
  \[
  |J_r|\ll Q^{-B}
  \]
  for growing \(B\).
- Behavior resembles same-scale quadrature controls.

## Falsifies the current rank-two route numerically

Not a formal falsification, but a serious route-level failure would be:

\[
E_I\ll Q^{-B}|I|
\]

for arbitrarily large effective \(B\), together with live anisotropy or evidence that Gate 2 cannot be recovered by singular dominance.

That would indicate actual zeta permits source-flat intervals and the rank-two norm architecture is non-closing without a source-robust row or global trace theorem.

---

# 10. Final recommendation

The numerical program should run in this order:

1. **Negative control first:** confirm same-scale quadrature can make \(E_I\) collapse.
2. **Synthetic singular scan:** confirm dominance gives huge Gate 2 and cancellation collapses back to Gate 1.
3. **Low/medium-height actual-zero scan:** measure \(E_I,B_I^{\rm eff}\).
4. **AFE cross-check:** verify the same \(q''_{\can}\) behavior with fixed coefficients.
5. **Phase surrogate comparison:** test whether finite-jet recurrence appears in models but not actual zeta.

This design directly tests the current bottleneck:

\[
\boxed{
\int_{I_\rho}|q''_{\can}(m)|^2\,dm
\ge Q^{-B}|I_\rho|.
}
\]

It also distinguishes three possibilities:

\[
\text{actual zeta has arithmetic anti-quadrature},
\]

\[
\text{source-flatness is generic but hidden at tested heights},
\]

or

\[
\text{the rank-two route needs a source-robust/global replacement.}
\]

## Agent 4 / D — Numerical Gate 1 stress test

### Verdict

The numerical program should now target exactly one quantity:

\[
E_I=|I|^{-1}\int_I |q''_{\can}(m)|^2\,dm,
\qquad
q''_{\can}=q_\zeta''=\Phi_\zeta'''.
\]

The purpose is to determine whether actual zeta behaves like the same-scale quadrature adversary. The current strategy has reduced the proof architecture primarily to Gate 1; smooth Gate 2 is local analysis, and singular Gate 2 reduces back to Gate 1 anti-quadrature. 

---

# 1. Numerical object: zero-side version

Use the canonical zero-side representation

\[
q''_{\can}(m)
=
B_2(m)+\sum_\rho^{\rm reg}K_2(m;\rho).
\]

Here:

\[
B_2(m)
\]

is the completed gamma/background contribution, and

\[
K_2(m;\rho)
\]

is the second derivative of the packet kernel contribution to \(q_\zeta\).

For a local off-line packet model

\[
K(m;\gamma,c)=\frac{c}{(m-\gamma)^2+c^2},
\]

one has

\[
K_2(m;\gamma,c)
=
\frac{2c\left(3(m-\gamma)^2-c^2\right)}
{\left((m-\gamma)^2+c^2\right)^3}.
\]

The actual implementation must use the paper’s completed/regularized quartet convention, because the raw zero-side tail is not absolutely summable at the \(q_\zeta\)-level. The test should therefore record separately:

\[
q''_{\can,\mathrm{core}},
\qquad
q''_{\can,\mathrm{tail}},
\qquad
B_2.
\]

A healthy scan should be insensitive to moderate changes in tail cutoff after regularization.

---

# 2. Numerical object: prime/AFE version

Independently compute

\[
q''_{\can}(m)
=
B_2(m)+P_2(m)+D_2(m)+E_2(m),
\]

with

\[
P_2(m)
=
\Re\sum_{n\le X}a_n e^{-im\log n}.
\]

The coefficients \(a_n\) are fixed actual-zeta/AFE coefficients including the differentiated \((\log n)^2\)-weights. The dual term \(D_2\) must include the differentiated \(\chi\)- or theta-factor contribution.

This version tests whether the fixed-prime phase model can exhibit source-flat recurrence. It should be used as a cross-check, not as the sole numerical source, because the differentiated AFE error \(E_2\) must be controlled carefully.

---

# 3. Ordinary \(Q^{-1}\)-scale actual-zeta scan

For height \(T\), set

\[
Q\asymp \log T
\]

or the paper’s local \(Q\). For centers \(m_0\), define

\[
I(m_0)=
[m_0-c_I/Q,\ m_0+c_I/Q].
\]

Use several classes of centers:

\[
\text{Gram points},
\]

\[
\text{critical-zero ordinates},
\]

\[
\text{midpoints between adjacent critical zeros},
\]

\[
\text{unusually small or large gap neighborhoods},
\]

\[
\text{random points in }[T,T+H].
\]

For each interval compute:

\[
S_I=\sup_{m\in I}|q''_{\can}(m)|,
\]

\[
E_I=|I|^{-1}\int_I |q''_{\can}(m)|^2\,dm,
\]

\[
B_I^{\rm eff}=-\frac{\log E_I}{\log Q}.
\]

Also compute scaled finite jets:

\[
J_r(I)=
\Delta^r
\partial_m^r q''_{\can}(m_0),
\qquad
0\le r\le R(Q),
\]

where

\[
\Delta=|I|/2,
\qquad
R(Q)\asymp \frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q}
\]

or a practical low-order proxy such as \(R=6,8,10,12\).

### Gate 1-supporting outcome

Gate 1 is numerically supported if:

\[
E_I\ge Q^{-B_0}
\]

for a stable moderate \(B_0\), and \(B_I^{\rm eff}\) does not grow with height.

### Gate 1-threatening outcome

Gate 1 is threatened if there are intervals with:

\[
B_I^{\rm eff}\to+\infty
\]

or with simultaneous finite-jet suppression

\[
|J_r(I)|\ll Q^{-B}
\qquad
0\le r\le R(Q)
\]

for increasing effective \(B\).

---

# 4. Singular/shallow-scale synthetic scan

This test is not actual zeta. It validates the singular-regime logic.

Use

\[
m=\gamma+cx,
\qquad
c\ll1,
\]

and build

\[
q_{\near}(m)=
\sum_{j=1}^N
w_j\frac{c_j}{(m-\gamma_j)^2+c_j^2},
\]

with same-scale packets

\[
\gamma_j=\gamma+ca_j,
\qquad
c_j=cd_j.
\]

Then

\[
q_{\near}(m)=c^{-1}Q(x),
\]

\[
q_{\near}''(m)=c^{-3}Q''(x),
\]

\[
q_{\near}^{(4)}(m)=c^{-5}Q^{(4)}(x).
\]

Compute

\[
u=q'',
\]

\[
\Gamma_G=u-6q+2q^3,
\]

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}=(1-q^2)u-\frac16q^{(4)}.
\]

Then compute:

\[
E_I=|I|^{-1}\int_I |u|^2\,dm,
\]

\[
V_I=|I|^{-1}\int_I |u|^2(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)\,dm.
\]

For a single dominant packet, one should observe approximately:

\[
u\sim c^{-3},
\qquad
\Gamma_{G,2}\sim c^{-5},
\]

hence

\[
|u|^2|\Gamma_{G,2}|^2\sim c^{-16}.
\]

On a length-\(c\) interval, the integrated Gate 2 mass scales like

\[
c^{-15}.
\]

This confirms that singular packets are not dangerous unless source curvature is cancelled.

---

# 5. Same-scale quadrature negative control

This is the most important control. It proves the numerical pipeline can detect the known adversary.

Construct

\[
q_{\quad}(m)
=
\sum_{j=1}^N
w_j
\frac{c_j}{(m-x_j)^2+c_j^2},
\qquad
w_j>0,
\]

with same-scale coordinates

\[
x_j=d\cos\theta_j,
\qquad
c_j=d\sin\theta_j.
\]

Choose \(w_j,\theta_j\) to minimize or solve:

\[
q_{\quad}^{(2)}(0)=0,
\]

\[
q_{\quad}^{(3)}(0)=0,
\]

\[
\cdots
\]

\[
q_{\quad}^{(R+2)}(0)=0.
\]

Equivalently, in normalized coordinates,

\[
Q''(0)=Q^{(3)}(0)=\cdots=Q^{(R+2)}(0)=0.
\]

Then scan

\[
I=[-c_Xd,c_Xd].
\]

The expected result is:

\[
E_I\ll 1,
\]

and

\[
B_I^{\rm eff}\gg1.
\]

If this negative control fails to produce visible flatness, the numerical procedure is not sensitive enough to test Gate 1.

---

# 6. How to distinguish actual zeta from surrogates

Run four side-by-side classes.

### A. Actual zero-side scan

Use verified zero data plus the completed background/regularized tail.

This is the primary evidence.

### B. Random same-density zero surrogate

Keep the same local density but randomize packet locations/depths within admissible constraints.

If both actual and random data avoid flatness, the evidence is weaker. If actual avoids flatness but adversarial controls flatten, that is stronger.

### C. Explicit quadrature adversary

Force finite-jet source flatness by design.

This should flatten. If actual zeta does not, the distinction is meaningful.

### D. Fixed-prime/AFE phase surrogate

Use actual AFE amplitudes and frequencies but sample phase behavior aggressively.

If the surrogate finds source-flat recurrence while actual zeta does not, the off-line-center/zero-prime compatibility is likely carrying arithmetic content.

---

# 7. Practical pseudocode

```text
for each height band [T, T+H]:
    Q = log(T)
    load verified zeros in [T-H_tail, T+H+H_tail]
    build regularized zero-side q_can_second(m)
    build optional AFE q_can_second_AFE(m)

    candidate_centers = Gram points
                      + zero ordinates
                      + zero-gap midpoints
                      + small-gap neighborhoods
                      + random points

    for m0 in candidate_centers:
        I = [m0 - cI/Q, m0 + cI/Q]
        sample nodes m_k in I
        values = q_can_second(m_k)
        E_I = mean(abs(values)^2)
        S_I = max(abs(values))
        B_eff = -log(E_I)/log(Q)

        compute scaled jets J_r at m0
        store {T, m0, E_I, S_I, B_eff, J_r}

run singular synthetic tests:
    for c in [1e-2, 1e-4, 1e-8, 1e-16]:
        build one-packet and multi-packet q(m)
        compute u, Gamma_G, Gamma_G2
        compute E_I and V_I

run quadrature negative controls:
    choose same-scale packet nodes
    solve constrained least squares for positive weights
    enforce Q''(0), ..., Q^(R+2)(0) small
    compute E_I and B_eff
```

---

# 8. Interpretation table

| Outcome | Interpretation |
|---|---|
| Actual \(E_I\) stays polynomially healthy | Supports Gate 1 |
| Actual \(B_I^{\rm eff}\) grows with height | Threatens Gate 1 |
| Actual finite jets \(J_0,\ldots,J_R\) are jointly tiny | Strong Gate 1 warning |
| Quadrature control flattens but actual zeta does not | Supports anti-quadrature hypothesis |
| AFE surrogate flattens but actual zero-side does not | Center/zero-prime compatibility may be essential |
| Actual zeta resembles quadrature control | Rank-two route likely non-closing without source-robust/global replacement |

---

# 9. Final recommendation

Run the tests in this order:

1. **Quadrature negative control** to validate sensitivity.
2. **Singular synthetic scan** to confirm dominance vs. cancellation behavior.
3. **Ordinary actual-zero scan** over several height bands.
4. **AFE cross-check** on selected intervals.
5. **Phase surrogate comparison** to test finite-jet recurrence behavior.

The decisive diagnostic is not a single small value of \(q''_{\can}\). The serious warning sign is interval-level or finite-jet source flatness:

\[
E_I\ll Q^{-B}
\]

with increasing effective \(B\), or

\[
\Delta^r\partial_m^r q''_{\can}(m_0)\approx0
\qquad
0\le r\le R(Q).
\]

That is the numerical signature of the same-scale source-flattening obstruction now central to the proof attempt.

## Agent 4 / D — Numerical protocol with explicit pass/fail criteria

### Verdict

The numerical work should be framed as a **Gate 1 stress test**, not as evidence for RH directly. The target diagnostic is:

\[
E_I=|I|^{-1}\int_I |q''_{\can}(m)|^2\,dm,
\qquad
B_I^{\rm eff}=-\frac{\log E_I}{\log Q}.
\]

The goal is to determine whether actual zeta exhibits the same kind of interval/finite-jet source flattening that the same-scale quadrature adversary can produce. The latest coordinator summary correctly states that Gate 1 is now the decisive theorem and that the numerical protocol should compare actual zeta against quadrature and AFE/phase surrogates. 

---

# 1. Zero-side computation of \(q''_{\can}\)

Use the canonical object:

\[
q''_{\can}(m)=q_\zeta''(m)=\Phi_\zeta'''(m).
\]

The zero-side numerical representation should be:

\[
q''_{\can}(m)
=
B_2(m)+\sum_{\rho}^{\rm reg}K_2(m;\rho).
\]

For a local packet model with ordinate \(\gamma\) and transverse depth \(c\),

\[
K(m;\gamma,c)=\frac{c}{(m-\gamma)^2+c^2},
\]

so

\[
K_2(m;\gamma,c)
=
\frac{2c\left(3(m-\gamma)^2-c^2\right)}
{\left((m-\gamma)^2+c^2\right)^3}.
\]

For actual zeta, the implementation must use the paper’s regularized/completed quartet convention, not a raw divergent zero sum. Numerically, track:

\[
B_2(m),
\qquad
K_{2,\core}(m),
\qquad
K_{2,\tail}^{\rm reg}(m),
\qquad
q''_{\can}(m).
\]

### Error checks

For each height band and interval:

1. Vary the zero-tail cutoff.
2. Vary quadrature density.
3. Compare regularized zero-side output against AFE output on a subset.
4. Confirm that \(E_I\) is stable under cutoff enlargement.

A Gate 1 warning is not credible if it disappears under tail cutoff or quadrature refinement.

---

# 2. Prime/AFE computation of \(q''_{\can}\)

Use:

\[
q''_{\can}(m)=B_2(m)+P_2(m)+D_2(m)+E_2(m),
\]

with

\[
P_2(m)=\Re\sum_{n\le X}a_ne^{-im\log n}.
\]

The coefficients \(a_n\) must be the fixed actual-zeta/AFE coefficients, including differentiated \((\log n)^2\)-weights and smoothing. \(D_2\) must include the differentiated dual term and \(\chi\)- or theta-factor derivatives.

The AFE version is mainly a cross-check and a recurrence diagnostic. It should not be used alone unless \(E_2\) is controlled after the required derivatives.

---

# 3. Actual-zeta ordinary-scale scan

For each height band \([T,T+H]\), set:

\[
Q=\log T
\]

or the paper’s exact local \(Q\). Use intervals

\[
I(m_0)=[m_0-c_I/Q,\ m_0+c_I/Q].
\]

Sample centers \(m_0\) from:

\[
\text{Gram points},
\]

\[
\text{critical-zero ordinates},
\]

\[
\text{midpoints between adjacent critical zeros},
\]

\[
\text{small-gap and large-gap neighborhoods},
\]

\[
\text{random points in the band}.
\]

For each interval compute:

\[
S_I=\sup_I |q''_{\can}|,
\]

\[
E_I=|I|^{-1}\int_I |q''_{\can}|^2\,dm,
\]

\[
B_I^{\rm eff}=-\frac{\log E_I}{\log Q}.
\]

Also compute scaled jets:

\[
J_r(I)=\Delta^r\partial_m^r q''_{\can}(m_0),
\qquad
0\le r\le R_{\rm test},
\]

where

\[
\Delta=|I|/2.
\]

Use practical values such as:

\[
R_{\rm test}=6,8,10,12
\]

and, where feasible,

\[
R(Q)\asymp \frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q}.
\]

---

# 4. Adversarial same-scale quadrature negative control

This control is mandatory.

Build:

\[
q_{\quad}(m)=
\sum_{j=1}^{N}w_j
\frac{c_j}{(m-x_j)^2+c_j^2},
\qquad
w_j>0,
\]

with same-scale coordinates:

\[
x_j=d\cos\theta_j,
\qquad
c_j=d\sin\theta_j.
\]

Choose \(w_j,\theta_j\) so that in normalized coordinates:

\[
Q''(0)\approx0,
\quad
Q^{(3)}(0)\approx0,
\quad
\ldots,
\quad
Q^{(R+2)}(0)\approx0.
\]

Equivalently, solve or minimize the moment system:

\[
\sum_j w_j\sin(k\theta_j)\approx0,
\qquad
3\le k\le R+3.
\]

Then measure \(E_I\) on:

\[
I=[-c_Xd,\ c_Xd].
\]

### Expected result

The negative control should produce:

\[
E_I\ll1,
\qquad
B_I^{\rm eff}\gg1.
\]

If the negative control does not flatten, the numerical method is not sensitive enough to test Gate 1.

---

# 5. Singular synthetic packet tests

Use:

\[
m=\gamma+cx,
\qquad
c\ll1.
\]

Construct:

\[
q_{\near}(m)
=
\sum_jw_j
\frac{c_j}{(m-\gamma_j)^2+c_j^2},
\]

with:

\[
\gamma_j=\gamma+ca_j,
\qquad
c_j=cd_j.
\]

Then:

\[
q_{\near}=c^{-1}Q(x),
\]

\[
q_{\near}''=c^{-3}Q''(x),
\]

\[
q_{\near}^{(4)}=c^{-5}Q^{(4)}(x).
\]

Compute:

\[
u=q'',
\]

\[
\Gamma_G=u-6q+2q^3,
\]

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}=(1-q^2)u-\frac16q^{(4)}.
\]

Measure:

\[
E_I=|I|^{-1}\int_I|u|^2\,dm,
\]

and:

\[
V_I=|I|^{-1}\int_I|u|^2(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)\,dm.
\]

### Expected outcomes

For a single dominant shallow packet:

\[
u\sim c^{-3},
\qquad
\Gamma_{G,2}\sim c^{-5},
\]

so:

\[
|u|^2|\Gamma_{G,2}|^2\sim c^{-16}.
\]

Thus \(V_I\) should be huge. If singular source flattening is imposed by quadrature, \(E_I\) should collapse instead. This confirms that singular Gate 2 reduces to Gate 1 anti-quadrature.

---

# 6. Required data and numerical settings

### Zero data

Use verified zeros in a window substantially larger than the scan band:

\[
[T-H_{\tail},\ T+H+H_{\tail}].
\]

Tail sensitivity must be measured by increasing \(H_{\tail}\).

### Sampling density

For ordinary intervals:

\[
|I|\asymp Q^{-1}.
\]

Use at least 50–200 quadrature nodes per interval initially, then increase adaptively for intervals with unusually low \(E_I\).

For singular synthetic intervals:

\[
|I|\asymp c.
\]

Use normalized \(x\)-nodes, not absolute \(m\)-nodes, to avoid losing resolution.

### Quadrature

Use Gauss–Legendre or Clenshaw–Curtis quadrature on each interval. For suspected flat intervals, double the quadrature order and confirm stability.

### Cross-checks

For selected intervals:

\[
q''_{\can,\zero}(m)
\quad\text{vs.}\quad
q''_{\can,\AFE}(m).
\]

Record the discrepancy:

\[
\mathrm{Err}_I
=
|I|^{-1}\int_I
|q''_{\can,\zero}-q''_{\can,\AFE}|^2\,dm.
\]

Require:

\[
\mathrm{Err}_I\ll E_I
\]

before treating a small \(E_I\) as meaningful.

---

# 7. Pass/fail criteria

## Supports Gate 1

Gate 1 is numerically supported if:

\[
B_I^{\rm eff}
\]

remains bounded by a moderate constant across height bands, center classes, and increasing \(Q\), and no interval shows simultaneous finite-jet flattening:

\[
|J_r(I)|\ll Q^{-B}
\quad
(0\le r\le R_{\rm test})
\]

with growing effective \(B\).

A strong support pattern is:

1. actual-zeta scans have healthy \(E_I\);
2. quadrature controls flatten strongly;
3. AFE and zero-side computations agree;
4. fixed-prime/phase surrogates flatten more often than actual zeta.

## Threatens Gate 1

Gate 1 is threatened if actual-zeta intervals show:

\[
B_I^{\rm eff}
\]

increasing with height, or if there are repeated intervals with:

\[
E_I\ll Q^{-B}
\]

for growing effective \(B\).

The strongest warning is simultaneous finite-jet suppression:

\[
|J_r(I)|\ll Q^{-B}
\qquad
0\le r\le R_{\rm test}.
\]

## Numerically suggests rank-two route is non-closing

The route looks non-closing if actual zeta behaves like the quadrature control:

\[
E_I\approx0
\]

at polynomial or super-polynomial strength on packet-scale intervals, especially if anisotropy remains live or if Gate 2 cannot be recovered by singular dominance.

---

# 8. Interpretation table

| Observation | Interpretation |
|---|---|
| Actual \(E_I\) healthy; quadrature control flat | Supports actual-zeta anti-quadrature |
| Actual \(E_I\) flat only at isolated points, not intervals | Not a Gate 1 failure |
| Actual interval \(E_I\) decays with height | Gate 1 threatened |
| Actual finite jets jointly small | Serious Gate 1 warning |
| AFE surrogate flattens but actual zeros do not | Actual zero/prime compatibility may be protective |
| Actual zeros and quadrature controls both flatten | Rank-two norm route likely non-closing |
| Singular dominance gives huge \(V_I\) | Confirms singular Gate 2 is harmless absent cancellation |
| Singular quadrature collapses \(E_I\) | Confirms singular obstruction reduces to Gate 1 |

---

# 9. Recommended execution order

1. **Implement quadrature negative control first.**  
   This validates sensitivity.

2. **Run singular synthetic tests.**  
   Confirm the dominance/cancellation dichotomy.

3. **Run ordinary actual-zero scans at low and medium heights.**  
   Collect \(E_I,S_I,B_I^{\rm eff},J_r\).

4. **Cross-check selected intervals by AFE.**  
   Especially intervals with unusually small \(E_I\).

5. **Run fixed-prime/phase surrogate scans.**  
   Determine whether source-flat recurrence appears in models more easily than in actual zeta.

6. **Escalate only suspicious intervals.**  
   Increase zero tail, quadrature order, jet depth, and AFE accuracy.

---

# 10. Final experimental theorem target

The numerical protocol is designed to test this empirical claim:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Actual zeta does not exhibit same-scale finite-jet source-curvature flattening.}
}
\]

A numerical pass does not prove Gate 1, but it distinguishes actual-zeta behavior from the known local quadrature adversary and helps decide whether the rank-two route is worth continuing.

## Agent 4 / D — Gate 1 numerics: implementable experimental specification

### Objective

Numerically stress-test Gate 1:

\[
\int_{I_\rho}|q''_{\can}(m)|^2\,dm
\ge Q^{-B}|I_\rho|,
\qquad
q''_{\can}=q_\zeta''=\Phi_\zeta'''.
\]

The diagnostic is:

\[
E_I=|I|^{-1}\int_I|q''_{\can}(m)|^2\,dm,
\qquad
B_I^{\rm eff}=-\frac{\log E_I}{\log Q}.
\]

The test should detect whether actual zeta behaves like a same-scale source-flattening quadrature adversary. The attached coordinator brief states that Gate 1 is now the central theorem and that numerical work should compare actual zeta against quadrature controls and AFE/fixed-prime surrogates. 

---

# 1. Zero-side computation

Use the canonical zero-side representation:

\[
q''_{\can}(m)
=
B_2(m)+\sum_\rho^{\rm reg}K_2(m;\rho).
\]

For a local packet model,

\[
K(m;\gamma,c)=\frac{c}{(m-\gamma)^2+c^2},
\]

so

\[
K_2(m;\gamma,c)
=
\frac{2c\bigl(3(m-\gamma)^2-c^2\bigr)}
{\bigl((m-\gamma)^2+c^2\bigr)^3}.
\]

Implementation requirements:

1. **Zero data:** verified zeros in an expanded window

\[
[T-H_{\tail},\,T+H+H_{\tail}].
\]

2. **Quartet grouping:** for off-line synthetic or hypothetical tests, group

\[
\rho,\quad 1-\rho,\quad \bar\rho,\quad 1-\bar\rho.
\]

3. **Background term:** compute \(B_2(m)\) from the completed gamma/background contribution in the same normalization as \(q''_{\can}\).

4. **Regularized tail:** do not use a raw divergent zero sum. Use the draft’s completed/regularized tail convention. Numerically store components separately:

\[
B_2(m),\qquad
K_{2,\core}(m),\qquad
K_{2,\tail}^{\rm reg}(m).
\]

5. **Cutoff stability:** repeat with increasing \(H_{\tail}\). A suspiciously small \(E_I\) is meaningful only if it is stable under tail enlargement.

---

# 2. AFE cross-check

Compute independently:

\[
q''_{\can}(m)=B_2(m)+P_2(m)+D_2(m)+E_2(m),
\]

where

\[
P_2(m)=\Re\sum_{n\le X}a_ne^{-im\log n}.
\]

The coefficients \(a_n\) must include the differentiated \((\log n)^2\)-weights, fixed actual-zeta coefficients, and smoothing. \(D_2\) must include the differentiated dual term and \(\chi\)- or \(\theta\)-factor derivatives.

AFE use cases:

- cross-check selected intervals from the zero-side scan;
- detect whether fixed-prime phase surrogates exhibit source-flat recurrence;
- validate that small \(E_I\) is not a zero-side regularization artifact.

Require the discrepancy

\[
\operatorname{Err}_I
=
|I|^{-1}\int_I
|q''_{\can,\zero}(m)-q''_{\can,\AFE}(m)|^2\,dm
\]

to satisfy

\[
\operatorname{Err}_I\ll E_I
\]

before trusting a small \(E_I\).

---

# 3. Interval families to scan

For ordinary-scale scans, set

\[
Q\asymp \log T
\]

or the draft’s precise \(Q\), and use

\[
I(m_0)=[m_0-c_I/Q,\ m_0+c_I/Q].
\]

Scan centers:

1. Gram points.
2. Critical-zero ordinates.
3. Midpoints between adjacent critical zeros.
4. Small-gap neighborhoods.
5. Large-gap neighborhoods.
6. Random points in \([T,T+H]\).
7. Synthetic off-line packet centers.

For each interval compute:

\[
S_I=\sup_I|q''_{\can}|,
\]

\[
E_I=|I|^{-1}\int_I|q''_{\can}|^2\,dm,
\]

\[
B_I^{\rm eff}=-\frac{\log E_I}{\log Q}.
\]

Also compute finite-jet diagnostics:

\[
J_r(I)=\Delta^r\partial_m^r q''_{\can}(m_0),
\qquad
0\le r\le R_{\test},
\]

with

\[
\Delta=|I|/2.
\]

Use practical values

\[
R_{\test}=6,8,10,12,
\]

and, where feasible,

\[
R(Q)\asymp\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q}.
\]

---

# 4. Same-scale quadrature negative control

This must be run before actual-zeta scans.

Construct

\[
q_{\quad}(m)
=
\sum_{j=1}^N
w_j
\frac{c_j}{(m-x_j)^2+c_j^2},
\qquad
w_j>0,
\]

with same-scale coordinates

\[
x_j=d\cos\theta_j,
\qquad
c_j=d\sin\theta_j.
\]

Choose \(w_j,\theta_j\) to make the normalized source jets small:

\[
Q''(0)\approx0,\quad
Q^{(3)}(0)\approx0,\quad
\ldots,\quad
Q^{(R+2)}(0)\approx0.
\]

Equivalently solve or minimize

\[
\sum_jw_j\sin(k\theta_j)\approx0,
\qquad
3\le k\le R+3.
\]

Then scan

\[
I=[-c_Xd,\ c_Xd].
\]

Expected failure signature:

\[
E_I\ll1,
\qquad
B_I^{\rm eff}\gg1,
\]

with simultaneous small finite jets \(J_0,\ldots,J_R\).

If the negative control does not flatten, the numerical pipeline is not sensitive enough.

---

# 5. Singular synthetic dominance/cancellation tests

Use singular scaling:

\[
m=\gamma+cx,
\qquad
c\ll1.
\]

Build

\[
q_{\near}(m)=
\sum_jw_j
\frac{c_j}{(m-\gamma_j)^2+c_j^2},
\]

with

\[
\gamma_j=\gamma+ca_j,
\qquad
c_j=cd_j.
\]

Then

\[
q_{\near}=c^{-1}Q(x),
\]

\[
q_{\near}''=c^{-3}Q''(x),
\]

\[
q_{\near}^{(4)}=c^{-5}Q^{(4)}(x).
\]

Compute

\[
u=q'',
\]

\[
\Gamma_G=u-6q+2q^3,
\]

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}=(1-q^2)u-\frac16q^{(4)}.
\]

Measure:

\[
E_I=|I|^{-1}\int_I|u|^2\,dm,
\]

\[
V_I=|I|^{-1}\int_I
|u|^2(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)\,dm.
\]

Expected dominance signature for one near packet:

\[
u\sim c^{-3},
\qquad
\Gamma_{G,2}\sim c^{-5},
\]

so

\[
|u|^2|\Gamma_{G,2}|^2\sim c^{-16}.
\]

Thus \(V_I\) should be huge.

Expected cancellation signature:

\[
E_I\ll1
\]

after same-scale quadrature tuning. This confirms that singular danger reduces back to Gate 1 source flattening.

---

# 6. Sampling and quadrature details

For ordinary intervals:

\[
|I|\asymp Q^{-1}.
\]

Use 50–200 quadrature nodes initially. For any interval with low \(E_I\), rerun with doubled and quadrupled nodes.

Use Gauss–Legendre or Clenshaw–Curtis quadrature on each interval.

For singular synthetic intervals:

\[
|I|\asymp c.
\]

Always sample in normalized \(x\)-coordinates to avoid resolution loss.

For finite jets, use either:

- analytic derivatives of the packet kernels;
- high-order automatic differentiation;
- spectral differentiation on the interval, cross-checked against direct finite differences.

---

# 7. Concrete thresholds

Define a baseline acceptable exponent \(B_0\), e.g.

\[
B_0=10
\]

for low/medium numerical exploration, then adjust after seeing height scaling.

## Supports Gate 1

Gate 1 is numerically supported if:

\[
B_I^{\rm eff}\le B_0
\]

uniformly across sampled height bands and interval families, with no upward trend as \(Q\) increases.

Stronger support:

- actual-zero scans are healthy;
- quadrature negative controls flatten strongly;
- AFE and zero-side values agree;
- phase surrogates flatten more often than actual zeta.

## Threatens Gate 1

Gate 1 is threatened if:

\[
B_I^{\rm eff}
\]

increases materially with height, or if many intervals satisfy

\[
E_I\ll Q^{-B}
\]

for growing effective \(B\).

Serious warning:

\[
|J_r(I)|\ll Q^{-B}
\qquad
0\le r\le R_{\test}
\]

for multiple consecutive jets.

## Numerically non-closing route signal

The rank-two route looks numerically non-closing if actual zeta resembles the quadrature adversary:

\[
E_I\approx0
\]

at interval scale, with finite-jet flattening and no compensating singular Gate 2 dominance.

---

# 8. Execution order

1. **Same-scale quadrature negative control.**  
   Validate that the code detects the known adversary.

2. **Singular synthetic dominance/cancellation tests.**  
   Validate the smooth/singular dichotomy.

3. **Ordinary actual-zero scans.**  
   Run at several height bands.

4. **AFE cross-checks.**  
   Apply to the most suspicious and most typical intervals.

5. **Fixed-prime/phase surrogates.**  
   Determine whether source-flat recurrence appears in models more readily than in actual zeta.

6. **Escalate suspicious intervals.**  
   Increase tail cutoff, quadrature order, jet depth, and AFE precision.

---

# 9. Final experimental criterion

The numerical experiment tests the empirical claim:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Actual zeta does not exhibit same-scale finite-jet source-curvature flattening.}
}
\]

Numerical support does not prove Gate 1. But a well-designed run can distinguish:

\[
\text{actual-zeta anti-quadrature behavior}
\]

from

\[
\text{generic/surrogate source-flat recurrence}.
\]

That distinction is now the most useful numerical input for deciding whether the rank-two route should continue.

## Agent 4 / D — Gate 1 numerical stress-test specification

### Objective

Build a numerical protocol targeting only Gate 1:

\[
E_I:=|I|^{-1}\int_I |q''_{\can}(m)|^2\,dm,
\qquad
q''_{\can}=q_\zeta''=\Phi_\zeta'''.
\]

The key diagnostic is:

\[
B_I^{\rm eff}:=-\frac{\log E_I}{\log Q}.
\]

The experiment should answer one question: **does actual zeta exhibit same-scale source-curvature flattening resembling the quadrature adversary?** The attached instruction frames Gate 1 as the decisive bottleneck and asks for actual-zeta scans, AFE cross-checks, same-scale quadrature controls, and singular/shallow packet synthetic tests. 

---

# 1. Zero-side computation

Use the canonical zero-side representation:

\[
q''_{\can}(m)=B_2(m)+\sum_{\rho}^{\rm reg}K_2(m;\rho).
\]

For the local packet kernel

\[
K(m;\gamma,c)=\frac{c}{(m-\gamma)^2+c^2},
\]

the source-curvature kernel is:

\[
K_2(m;\gamma,c)
=
\frac{2c\left(3(m-\gamma)^2-c^2\right)}
{\left((m-\gamma)^2+c^2\right)^3}.
\]

The implementation must not use a raw divergent zero sum. It should separate and report:

\[
B_2(m),
\qquad
K_{2,\core}(m),
\qquad
K_{2,\tail}^{\rm reg}(m),
\qquad
q''_{\can}(m).
\]

Required inputs:

1. Verified zeros over an expanded window

\[
[T-H_{\tail},T+H+H_{\tail}].
\]

2. The gamma/background contribution \(B_2\) in the same normalization as \(q''_{\can}\).

3. A fixed regularization convention for the far zero tail.

4. Quartet grouping for any synthetic off-line tests:

\[
\rho,\quad 1-\rho,\quad \bar\rho,\quad 1-\bar\rho.
\]

Main error checks:

\[
E_I(H_{\tail})
\]

should stabilize as \(H_{\tail}\) grows. Any interval with suspiciously small \(E_I\) must be recomputed with larger zero windows, higher quadrature order, and an AFE cross-check.

---

# 2. AFE cross-check

Independently compute:

\[
q''_{\can}(m)=B_2(m)+P_2(m)+D_2(m)+E_2(m),
\]

where

\[
P_2(m)=\Re\sum_{n\le X}a_ne^{-im\log n}.
\]

The coefficients \(a_n\) must include the fixed actual-zeta coefficients, smoothing, and differentiated \((\log n)^2\)-weights. \(D_2\) must include the differentiated dual/\(\chi\)-factor contribution.

For selected intervals, compute:

\[
\operatorname{Err}_I
=
|I|^{-1}\int_I
|q''_{\can,\zero}(m)-q''_{\can,\AFE}(m)|^2\,dm.
\]

A small \(E_I\) is credible only if:

\[
\operatorname{Err}_I\ll E_I.
\]

If \(E_I\) is small but the zero-side and AFE values disagree, classify the interval as numerically unresolved, not as Gate 1-threatening.

---

# 3. Actual-zeta scan intervals

For height \(T\), set:

\[
Q\asymp \log T
\]

or the draft’s local \(Q\). Use intervals:

\[
I(m_0)=\left[m_0-\frac{c_I}{Q},\,m_0+\frac{c_I}{Q}\right].
\]

Scan centers \(m_0\) from:

1. Gram points;
2. zero ordinates;
3. midpoints between consecutive zero ordinates;
4. small-gap neighborhoods;
5. large-gap neighborhoods;
6. random points in the height band;
7. synthetic off-line packet centers.

For each \(I\), compute:

\[
S_I=\sup_{m\in I}|q''_{\can}(m)|,
\]

\[
E_I=|I|^{-1}\int_I|q''_{\can}(m)|^2\,dm,
\]

\[
B_I^{\rm eff}=-\frac{\log E_I}{\log Q}.
\]

Also compute scaled finite jets:

\[
J_r(I)=\Delta^r\partial_m^r q''_{\can}(m_0),
\qquad
0\le r\le R_{\test},
\]

where

\[
\Delta=|I|/2.
\]

Use practical initial values:

\[
R_{\test}=6,8,10,12.
\]

The serious warning sign is not an isolated small \(q''_{\can}(m_0)\), but interval-level or finite-jet flatness:

\[
E_I\ll Q^{-B}
\]

or

\[
|J_r(I)|\ll Q^{-B}
\qquad
0\le r\le R_{\test}.
\]

---

# 4. Same-scale quadrature negative control

This must be run before interpreting actual-zeta data.

Construct:

\[
q_{\quad}(m)=
\sum_{j=1}^{N}w_j
\frac{c_j}{(m-x_j)^2+c_j^2},
\qquad
w_j>0,
\]

with same-scale coordinates:

\[
x_j=d\cos\theta_j,
\qquad
c_j=d\sin\theta_j.
\]

Choose \(w_j,\theta_j\) to make:

\[
Q''(0)\approx0,\quad
Q^{(3)}(0)\approx0,\quad\ldots,\quad
Q^{(R+2)}(0)\approx0.
\]

Equivalently minimize:

\[
\sum_{k=3}^{R+3}
\left|
\sum_jw_j\sin(k\theta_j)
\right|^2
\]

under \(w_j>0\), or use a positive quadrature construction.

Expected negative-control signature:

\[
E_I\ll1,
\qquad
B_I^{\rm eff}\gg1,
\]

with small jets:

\[
J_0,\ldots,J_R\approx0.
\]

If this control does not flatten, the experiment is not sensitive enough to test Gate 1.

---

# 5. Singular/shallow packet synthetic tests

Use:

\[
m=\gamma+cx,
\qquad
c\ll1.
\]

Construct:

\[
q_{\near}(m)=
\sum_jw_j
\frac{c_j}{(m-\gamma_j)^2+c_j^2},
\]

with:

\[
\gamma_j=\gamma+ca_j,
\qquad
c_j=cd_j.
\]

Then:

\[
q_{\near}=c^{-1}Q(x),
\]

\[
q_{\near}''=c^{-3}Q''(x),
\]

\[
q_{\near}^{(4)}=c^{-5}Q^{(4)}(x).
\]

Compute:

\[
u=q'',
\]

\[
\Gamma_G=u-6q+2q^3,
\]

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}=(1-q^2)u-\frac16q^{(4)}.
\]

Measure:

\[
E_I=|I|^{-1}\int_I|u|^2\,dm,
\]

\[
V_I=|I|^{-1}\int_I|u|^2(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)\,dm.
\]

Expected dominance result for one shallow packet:

\[
u\sim c^{-3},
\qquad
\Gamma_{G,2}\sim c^{-5},
\]

so:

\[
|u|^2|\Gamma_{G,2}|^2\sim c^{-16}.
\]

Thus \(V_I\) should be huge. If same-scale quadrature cancels \(Q''\), then \(E_I\) collapses. This confirms that singular danger reduces to Gate 1 source flattening.

---

# 6. Numerical thresholds

Use a baseline exploratory threshold such as:

\[
B_0=10.
\]

### Supports Gate 1

Gate 1 is numerically supported if:

\[
B_I^{\rm eff}\le B_0
\]

uniformly across sampled height bands, center classes, and increasing \(Q\), with no upward trend.

Stronger support requires:

1. same-scale quadrature controls flatten strongly;
2. actual zeta does not flatten;
3. AFE and zero-side computations agree;
4. fixed-prime or phase surrogates flatten more often than actual zeta.

### Threatens Gate 1

Gate 1 is threatened if:

\[
B_I^{\rm eff}
\]

grows with height, or if repeated intervals satisfy:

\[
E_I\ll Q^{-B}
\]

for increasing effective \(B\).

The strongest warning is simultaneous finite-jet suppression:

\[
|J_r(I)|\ll Q^{-B},
\qquad
0\le r\le R_{\test}.
\]

### Numerically non-closing signal

The rank-two route looks numerically non-closing if actual zeta resembles the quadrature adversary:

\[
E_I\approx0
\]

on interval scale, with finite-jet flattening and no singular-dominance recovery.

---

# 7. Execution order

1. Run same-scale quadrature negative controls.
2. Run singular synthetic dominance/cancellation tests.
3. Run ordinary actual-zero scans at several height bands.
4. AFE-cross-check typical and suspicious intervals.
5. Run fixed-prime/phase surrogate scans.
6. Escalate suspicious intervals with larger tails, higher quadrature, higher precision, and deeper finite-jet diagnostics.

Final experimental claim being tested:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Actual zeta does not exhibit same-scale finite-jet source-curvature flattening.}
}
\]

A positive numerical result will not prove Gate 1, but it will tell us whether actual zeta behaves fundamentally differently from the known local quadrature adversary.

## Agent 4 / D — Numerical Gate 1 implementation plan

### Objective

Implement a numerical stress test for Gate 1:

\[
E_I:=|I|^{-1}\int_I |q''_{\can}(m)|^2\,dm,
\qquad
q''_{\can}=q_\zeta''=\Phi_\zeta'''.
\]

The aim is not to test RH directly. It is to detect whether actual zeta permits same-scale finite-jet source flattening. The current shared status is that Gate 1 is essential, no credible bypass is available, and if Gate 1 fails the rank-two norm route becomes non-closing. 

---

# 1. Zero-side computation

Use the canonical representation

\[
q''_{\can}(m)
=
B_2(m)+\sum_{\rho}^{\rm reg}K_2(m;\rho).
\]

For a packet model

\[
K(m;\gamma,c)=\frac{c}{(m-\gamma)^2+c^2},
\]

use

\[
K_2(m;\gamma,c)
=
\frac{2c\left(3(m-\gamma)^2-c^2\right)}
{\left((m-\gamma)^2+c^2\right)^3}.
\]

Implementation must separate:

\[
B_2(m),\qquad
K_{2,\core}(m),\qquad
K_{2,\tail}^{\rm reg}(m),\qquad
q''_{\can}(m).
\]

Required controls:

1. Use verified zeros in an expanded window

\[
[T-H_{\tail},T+H+H_{\tail}].
\]

2. Increase \(H_{\tail}\) until

\[
E_I(H_{\tail})
\]

is stable.

3. Use the completed/regularized zero-tail convention. A raw unregularized zero sum is not acceptable.

4. For any suspicious low-\(E_I\) interval, rerun with:
   - larger tail cutoff;
   - higher quadrature order;
   - higher precision;
   - AFE cross-check.

---

# 2. AFE cross-check

Use

\[
q''_{\can}(m)
=
B_2(m)+P_2(m)+D_2(m)+E_2(m),
\]

where

\[
P_2(m)=\Re\sum_{n\le X}a_ne^{-im\log n}.
\]

The coefficients \(a_n\) must include actual fixed zeta/AFE coefficients, smoothing, and differentiated \((\log n)^2\)-weights. \(D_2\) must include the differentiated dual term and \(\chi\)-factor/theta-factor derivatives.

For selected intervals compute

\[
\operatorname{Err}_I
=
|I|^{-1}
\int_I
\left|
q''_{\can,\zero}(m)-q''_{\can,\AFE}(m)
\right|^2\,dm.
\]

A small \(E_I\) is credible only if

\[
\operatorname{Err}_I\ll E_I.
\]

Otherwise classify the interval as numerically unresolved.

---

# 3. Data and numerical settings

Use several height bands \([T,T+H]\). Set

\[
Q\asymp \log T
\]

unless the draft’s local \(Q\) convention differs.

For each interval

\[
I=[m_0-c_I/Q,\ m_0+c_I/Q],
\]

compute

\[
S_I=\sup_I|q''_{\can}|,
\]

\[
E_I=|I|^{-1}\int_I |q''_{\can}|^2\,dm,
\]

\[
B_I^{\rm eff}=-\frac{\log E_I}{\log Q}.
\]

Also compute scaled finite jets:

\[
J_r(I)=\Delta^r\partial_m^r q''_{\can}(m_0),
\qquad
0\le r\le R_{\test},
\qquad
\Delta=|I|/2.
\]

Initial practical jet depths:

\[
R_{\test}=6,8,10,12.
\]

Quadrature:

- Use Gauss–Legendre or Clenshaw–Curtis quadrature.
- Start with 100–200 nodes per ordinary interval.
- Double and quadruple node counts on suspicious intervals.
- Use normalized \(x\)-coordinates for singular synthetic tests.

Precision:

- Start with at least 80–100 decimal digits if using high derivatives or close packet configurations.
- Increase precision when \(E_I\) is near the warning threshold.

---

# 4. Scan interval families

Run scans centered at:

1. Gram points.
2. Critical-zero ordinates.
3. Midpoints between adjacent zero ordinates.
4. Small-gap neighborhoods.
5. Large-gap neighborhoods.
6. Random points in the height band.
7. Synthetic off-line packet centers.

The small-gap and synthetic centers are important because the adversarial mechanism is local packet flattening, not generic pointwise smallness.

---

# 5. Negative controls

## 5.1 Same-scale finite quadrature

Construct

\[
q_{\quad}(m)=
\sum_{j=1}^{N}
w_j
\frac{c_j}{(m-x_j)^2+c_j^2},
\qquad
w_j>0,
\]

with

\[
x_j=d\cos\theta_j,
\qquad
c_j=d\sin\theta_j.
\]

Choose \(w_j,\theta_j\) to flatten source jets:

\[
Q''(0)\approx0,\quad
Q^{(3)}(0)\approx0,\quad\ldots,\quad
Q^{(R+2)}(0)\approx0.
\]

Equivalent moment target:

\[
\sum_j w_j\sin(k\theta_j)\approx0,
\qquad
3\le k\le R+3.
\]

Expected result:

\[
E_I\ll1,\qquad B_I^{\rm eff}\gg1,
\]

with

\[
J_0,\ldots,J_R\approx0.
\]

If this control does not flatten, the numerical pipeline is not sensitive enough.

## 5.2 Singular shallow-packet dominance

Use

\[
m=\gamma+cx,\qquad c\ll1,
\]

and

\[
q_{\near}(m)=
\sum_jw_j
\frac{c_j}{(m-\gamma_j)^2+c_j^2},
\]

with

\[
\gamma_j=\gamma+ca_j,\qquad c_j=cd_j.
\]

Then

\[
q_{\near}=c^{-1}Q(x),
\qquad
q_{\near}''=c^{-3}Q''(x),
\qquad
q_{\near}^{(4)}=c^{-5}Q^{(4)}(x).
\]

Compute

\[
u=q'',
\]

\[
\Gamma_G=u-6q+2q^3,
\]

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}=(1-q^2)u-\frac16q^{(4)}.
\]

Also compute

\[
V_I=
|I|^{-1}\int_I |u|^2(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)\,dm.
\]

For a single dominant shallow packet, expect

\[
u\sim c^{-3},\qquad \Gamma_{G,2}\sim c^{-5},
\]

so

\[
|u|^2|\Gamma_{G,2}|^2\sim c^{-16}.
\]

Thus \(V_I\) should be huge.

## 5.3 Singular cancellation model

Use the same singular scale but tune a same-scale cluster to make

\[
Q''\approx0
\]

through finite order. Expected result:

\[
E_I\ll1.
\]

This verifies that singular danger reduces to Gate 1 source flattening.

---

# 6. Hard interpretation thresholds

Use an exploratory threshold

\[
B_0=10
\]

at low/medium heights. Adjust only after observing scaling.

## Supports Gate 1

Gate 1 is numerically supported if:

\[
B_I^{\rm eff}\le B_0
\]

across height bands, center families, and increasing \(Q\), with no upward trend.

Stronger support requires:

- quadrature controls flatten strongly;
- actual zeta does not flatten;
- zero-side and AFE computations agree;
- phase/fixed-prime surrogates flatten more often than actual zeta.

## Threatens Gate 1

Gate 1 is threatened if:

\[
B_I^{\rm eff}
\]

grows with height, or if many intervals satisfy

\[
E_I\ll Q^{-B}
\]

for increasing effective \(B\).

A serious warning requires finite-jet suppression:

\[
|J_r(I)|\ll Q^{-B},
\qquad
0\le r\le R_{\test}.
\]

## Route likely non-closing

The rank-two route looks numerically non-closing if actual zeta behaves like the same-scale quadrature adversary:

\[
E_I\approx0
\]

on interval scale, with finite-jet flattening, and no singular dominance recovery.

---

# 7. Execution order

1. Implement same-scale quadrature negative control.
2. Implement singular dominance and singular cancellation tests.
3. Run ordinary actual-zero scans.
4. AFE-cross-check typical and suspicious intervals.
5. Run fixed-prime/phase surrogate scans.
6. Escalate suspicious intervals with larger tails, more quadrature nodes, higher precision, and deeper jet diagnostics.

Final tested claim:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Actual zeta does not exhibit same-scale finite-jet source-curvature flattening.}
}
\]

A positive numerical result will not prove Gate 1, but it will determine whether actual-zeta data behave materially differently from the known quadrature adversary.

## Agent 4 / D — Realistic surrogate search protocol

### Objective

Search for Gate 1 countermodels in increasingly realistic surrogates by minimizing

\[
\mathcal J(m_0,\alpha)
=
|Z_\alpha(m_0)|^2
+
\sum_{r=0}^{R}
\left|
\Delta^r\partial_m^r q''_{\can}(m_0)
\right|^2.
\]

A successful countermodel is not merely a small value of \(q''_{\can}\) at one point. It must show finite-jet source flatness and then actual interval flatness:

\[
\int_I |q''_{\can}(m)|^2\,dm \ll Q^{-B}|I|.
\]

The attached coordinator prompt asks for a staged surrogate search from phase-relaxed models through increasingly realistic AFE/off-line-center constraints. 

---

# 1. Surrogate levels

## Level 0 — Pure phase-relaxed torus

Replace the actual one-parameter orbit by independent phases:

\[
z_p\in S^1.
\]

Model

\[
P_2(z)=\Re\sum_{n\le X} a_n z^{\nu(n)},
\]

where

\[
z^{\nu(n)}=\prod_{p^k\parallel n}z_p^k.
\]

Objective:

\[
\mathcal J_0(z,\alpha)
=
|Z_\alpha(z)|^2
+
\sum_{r=0}^{R}|S_r(z)|^2,
\]

where \(S_r\) is the scaled source-jet functional.

Purpose: determine whether coefficient structure alone forbids simultaneous zero/source-flatness.

Expected result: likely many solutions, because the number of phase variables greatly exceeds the number of equations.

---

## Level 1 — One-parameter fixed-prime flow

Restore

\[
z_p=e^{-im\log p}.
\]

Search over \(m\), but initially omit the dual term and use the main AFE/source polynomial only.

Objective:

\[
\mathcal J_1(m)
=
\sum_{r=0}^{R}
\left|
\Delta^r\partial_m^r P_2(m)
+
T_r(m)
\right|^2,
\]

where \(T_r\) is the background target being cancelled.

Purpose: test whether the actual prime-log orbit hits source-flat tubes at all.

---

## Level 2 — AFE main sum only plus off-line center

Add the approximate off-line zero equation using only the main AFE side:

\[
Z_{\alpha,\main}(m)=0.
\]

Objective:

\[
\mathcal J_2(m,\alpha)
=
|Z_{\alpha,\main}(m)|^2
+
\sum_{r=0}^{R}|S_r(m)|^2.
\]

Purpose: test whether the off-line center condition materially suppresses source-flat recurrence.

---

## Level 3 — AFE main plus dual/\(\chi\)

Use

\[
Z_\alpha(m)
=
Z_{\alpha,\main}(m)+Z_{\alpha,\dual}(m),
\]

with the \(\chi\)-factor, and compute

\[
q''_{\can}
=
B_2+P_2+D_2
\]

without the residual \(E_2\) at first.

Objective:

\[
\mathcal J_3(m,\alpha)
=
|Z_\alpha(m)|^2
+
\sum_{r=0}^{R}
\left|
\Delta^r\partial_m^r(B_2+P_2+D_2)(m)
\right|^2.
\]

Purpose: test whether the functional equation destroys the recurrence found in simpler models.

---

## Level 4 — Full AFE with gamma/background and error budget

Include:

\[
B_2,\quad P_2,\quad D_2,\quad E_2.
\]

Use the objective:

\[
\mathcal J_4(m,\alpha)
=
|Z_\alpha(m)|^2
+
\sum_{r=0}^{R}
\left|
\Delta^r\partial_m^r(B_2+P_2+D_2)(m)
\right|^2
+
\operatorname{Err}_{\AFE}(m,\alpha).
\]

Do not count a candidate as successful unless the AFE error is below the claimed flatness scale.

---

## Level 5 — Zero-side consistency check

For any candidate \((m_0,\alpha)\), build a corresponding zero-side or synthetic packet profile and compute

\[
E_I=|I|^{-1}\int_I |q''_{\can}(m)|^2\,dm.
\]

This is mandatory. A jet-flat candidate is only meaningful if interval flatness follows.

---

# 2. Variables and constraints by level

| Level | Variables | Constraints/objective |
|---|---:|---|
| Phase-relaxed torus | \(z_p\in S^1,\alpha\) | \(Z_\alpha=0,\ S_0=\cdots=S_R=0\) |
| Fixed-prime flow | \(m\) | \(S_0=\cdots=S_R=0\) |
| Main AFE + center | \(m,\alpha\) | \(Z_{\alpha,\main}=0,\ S_r=0\) |
| Full AFE | \(m,\alpha\) | \(Z_\alpha=0,\ S_r=0\), gamma/dual included |
| Validated candidate | \(m,\alpha\), interval \(I\) | \(E_I\ll Q^{-B}\), AFE/zero-side agreement |

Here

\[
S_r(m)
=
\Delta^r
\partial_m^r(B_2+D_2+P_2)(m).
\]

---

# 3. Search methods

## A. Nonlinear least squares over \((m,\alpha)\)

Minimize

\[
\mathcal J(m,\alpha)
\]

with multiple random starts.

Use variables:

\[
m\in[T,T+H],
\qquad
\alpha\in[\alpha_{\min},\alpha_{\max}].
\]

Use log-scaled penalties so that one term cannot dominate:

\[
\widetilde{\mathcal J}
=
\log\left(|Z_\alpha|^2+\varepsilon\right)
+
\sum_{r=0}^{R}
\log\left(|S_r|^2+\varepsilon\right).
\]

## B. Grid + local refinement

Use a coarse grid in \(m\), find low values of

\[
\sum_{r=0}^{R}|S_r(m)|^2,
\]

then optimize \(\alpha\) for \(Z_\alpha(m)\), then refine both.

This reveals whether source-flatness and zero-center conditions align naturally or only after tuning.

## C. Phase-relaxed torus optimization

Parameterize

\[
z_p=e^{i\theta_p}.
\]

Minimize

\[
\mathcal J_0(\theta,\alpha).
\]

If relaxed solutions are easy, compute their distance to the actual orbit:

\[
\theta_p\approx -m\log p \pmod{2\pi}.
\]

This measures whether the actual one-parameter orbit is the real obstruction.

## D. Random phase sampling

Sample independent phases to estimate the small-ball probability:

\[
\mathbb P(\mathcal J_0\le \varepsilon).
\]

Compare with actual orbit sampling over \(m\).

If the relaxed model finds many source-flat points but the actual orbit does not, that supports a prime-log nonrecurrence theorem.

## E. Interval search over \(m\)

For the one-parameter model, use:

\[
m\mapsto \mathcal J(m,\alpha^\ast(m)),
\]

where \(\alpha^\ast(m)\) minimizes \(|Z_\alpha(m)|\). Then search for near-zero valleys.

---

# 4. Success criteria

A candidate countermodel must satisfy all three criteria.

## Criterion 1 — Off-line center

\[
|Z_\alpha(m_0)|\le Q^{-C}.
\]

## Criterion 2 — Finite-jet source flatness

\[
\max_{0\le r\le R}
\left|
\Delta^r\partial_m^r q''_{\can}(m_0)
\right|
\le Q^{-C}.
\]

Use at least:

\[
R=6,8,10,12
\]

in practical experiments, and compare with the theoretical scale

\[
R(Q)\asymp \frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q}.
\]

## Criterion 3 — Interval flatness

After finding a jet-flat candidate, compute:

\[
E_I
=
|I|^{-1}
\int_I |q''_{\can}(m)|^2\,dm,
\qquad
I=[m_0-\Delta,m_0+\Delta].
\]

A candidate is genuine only if

\[
E_I\le Q^{-C'}
\]

and the value is stable under quadrature refinement and AFE/zero-side checks.

---

# 5. Verification of interval flatness

For each candidate:

1. Compute \(q''_{\can}\) at high-order quadrature nodes on \(I\).
2. Estimate

\[
E_I=|I|^{-1}\int_I |q''_{\can}|^2.
\]

3. Double quadrature nodes.
4. Increase AFE truncation/smoothing accuracy.
5. If zero data are available, cross-check against zero-side representation.
6. Compute finite jets independently by analytic differentiation and numerical interpolation.

Reject a candidate if smallness is not stable.

---

# 6. Expected interpretations

## Case A — Relaxed phases flatten, actual orbit does not

Interpretation:

\[
\text{coefficient structure alone does not prevent flatness,}
\]

but the actual one-parameter prime-log orbit may have nonrecurrence. This supports the missing theorem:

\[
\text{No simultaneous off-line-zero/source-flat finite-jet recurrence.}
\]

## Case B — Fixed-prime orbit flattens without \(Z_\alpha\), but not with \(Z_\alpha\)

Interpretation: the off-line center condition may provide real arithmetic leverage.

Then focus theorem work on:

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\Rightarrow
\max_r |S_r(m_0)|\ge Q^{-B}.
\]

## Case C — Full AFE admits candidates, but interval flatness fails

Interpretation: finite jets were not deep enough. Increase \(R\), or use \(L^2\)-direct objective.

## Case D — Full AFE admits stable interval-flat candidates

Interpretation: Gate 1 is numerically threatened. The rank-two route likely requires a source-robust row or global trace pivot.

## Case E — Actual zero-side data stays healthy while surrogates flatten

Interpretation: actual zero-prime compatibility may be protecting Gate 1. This is the best evidence for continuing the route.

---

# 7. Concrete staged plan

1. **Phase-relaxed model:** solve \(\mathcal J_0\) for many \(R\). Confirm whether solutions exist.
2. **One-parameter main-sum model:** search \(m\)-intervals for \(S_0=\cdots=S_R\) flatness.
3. **Add \(Z_\alpha\):** search \((m,\alpha)\) for joint bad points.
4. **Add dual/\(\chi\):** check whether the functional equation destroys candidates.
5. **Add gamma/background:** verify candidates remain.
6. **Validate interval \(E_I\):** convert jet-flat candidates to actual interval flatness.
7. **Cross-check against zero-side data:** if possible.

---

# 8. Final deliverable target

The search should produce one of three outcomes:

\[
\boxed{
\text{No countermodels beyond relaxed phases; Gate 1 remains plausible.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Realistic surrogates produce source-flat candidates; Gate 1 is threatened.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Full AFE/zero-side actual data produce robust source-flat intervals; rank-two route likely non-closing.}
}
\]

The most important output is not a single minimum of \(\mathcal J\), but a comparison table across surrogate levels showing exactly where source-flatness disappears, if it disappears.

## Agent 4 / D — AFE cross-check and fixed-prime surrogate search

### Objective

Design the AFE-side computation and surrogate search for Gate 1:

\[
E_I=|I|^{-1}\int_I |q''_{\can}(m)|^2\,dm.
\]

This branch has two roles:

1. Cross-check actual zero-side computations of \(q''_{\can}\).
2. Search for source-flat behavior in increasingly realistic prime/AFE surrogates.

The attached instruction puts this work downstream of the negative controls and actual zero-side scan, with emphasis on testing whether source-flat intervals survive as the model becomes more actual-zeta-like. 

---

# 1. AFE-side formula for \(q''_{\can}\)

Use the canonical representation

\[
q''_{\can}(m)=B_2(m)+P_2(m)+D_2(m)+E_2(m),
\]

where

\[
P_2(m)=\Re\sum_{n\le X} a_n e^{-im\log n}.
\]

At the schematic level, if the undifferentiated AFE main term has coefficients

\[
A_n(m)\,n^{-im},
\]

then two \(m\)-derivatives contribute terms involving

\[
(-i\log n)^2A_n(m)n^{-im},
\]

plus derivative terms from any \(m\)-dependent amplitude or smoothing. Thus \(a_n\) should include:

\[
(\log n)^2 n^{-1/2}W(n/T)
\]

up to the exact sign, smoothing convention, and completed-phase normalization.

The dual term \(D_2\) must include derivatives of:

\[
\chi(s),
\qquad
\theta(m),
\qquad
W^\ast(n/T),
\]

depending on the exact AFE form. In particular, do **not** treat the dual term as merely another independent Dirichlet polynomial with fixed coefficients; its \(m\)-dependent prefactor can contribute to \(q''_{\can}\).

The error \(E_2\) must be controlled at the scale being tested. For cross-checking a suspicious interval, require:

\[
|I|^{-1}\int_I |E_2(m)|^2\,dm
\ll E_I.
\]

If this is unavailable, label the AFE comparison as diagnostic only.

---

# 2. AFE cross-check metric

For any interval \(I\), compare the zero-side and AFE-side values by

\[
\operatorname{Err}_I
=
|I|^{-1}\int_I
\left|
q''_{\can,\zero}(m)-q''_{\can,\AFE}(m)
\right|^2\,dm.
\]

Acceptance condition:

\[
\operatorname{Err}_I\ll E_I.
\]

For suspicious intervals, use a stronger relative check:

\[
\frac{\operatorname{Err}_I}{E_I}\le 10^{-2}
\]

as an initial numerical target. If \(E_I\) is extremely small, require absolute stability under:

- AFE truncation change;
- smoothing change;
- higher precision;
- quadrature refinement;
- zero-side tail cutoff enlargement.

A candidate source-flat interval is not credible unless both representations agree to a scale smaller than the observed flatness.

---

# 3. Fixed-prime surrogate objective

Define scaled jets:

\[
S_r(m_0)
=
\Delta^r\partial_m^r q''_{\can}(m_0),
\qquad
0\le r\le R.
\]

For a fixed-prime surrogate, minimize

\[
\mathcal J_{\mathrm{src}}(m_0)
=
\sum_{r=0}^R |S_r(m_0)|^2.
\]

The first-stage objective ignores the off-line zero condition and asks only whether the prime/AFE model naturally produces source-flat finite jets.

After a low-\(\mathcal J_{\mathrm{src}}\) point is found, verify interval flatness:

\[
E_I
=
|I|^{-1}\int_I |q''_{\can}(m)|^2\,dm.
\]

A low jet score without low interval energy means \(R\) is too small or the candidate is not genuinely flat.

---

# 4. Staged surrogate hierarchy

## Level 1 — AFE main term only

Use

\[
q''_{\main}(m)=P_2(m).
\]

Objective:

\[
\mathcal J_1(m_0)
=
\sum_{r=0}^{R}
\left|
\Delta^r\partial_m^r P_2(m_0)
\right|^2.
\]

Purpose: determine whether fixed prime-log phases can produce source-flat jets in the simplest actual-amplitude model.

Expected result: flat candidates may occur. If they do not occur even here, Gate 1 is numerically stronger than expected.

---

## Level 2 — Main + dual term

Use

\[
q''_{\main+\dual}(m)=P_2(m)+D_2(m).
\]

Objective:

\[
\mathcal J_2(m_0)
=
\sum_{r=0}^{R}
\left|
\Delta^r\partial_m^r(P_2+D_2)(m_0)
\right|^2.
\]

Purpose: test whether the functional equation destroys main-sum source-flatness.

If candidates survive Level 2, the \(\chi\)-factor alone is not providing the needed rigidity.

---

## Level 3 — Main + dual + gamma/background

Use

\[
q''_{\AFE,0}(m)=B_2(m)+P_2(m)+D_2(m).
\]

Objective:

\[
\mathcal J_3(m_0)
=
\sum_{r=0}^{R}
\left|
\Delta^r\partial_m^r(B_2+P_2+D_2)(m_0)
\right|^2.
\]

Purpose: test whether deterministic background terms merely shift the flatness target or truly obstruct it.

Expected: background usually shifts the target. It is unlikely to create coercivity by itself.

---

## Level 4 — Add off-line center condition

Now include

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0.
\]

Minimize

\[
\mathcal J_4(m_0,\alpha)
=
|Z_\alpha(m_0)|^2
+
\sum_{r=0}^{R}
\left|
\Delta^r\partial_m^r(B_2+P_2+D_2)(m_0)
\right|^2.
\]

Search over:

\[
m_0\in[T,T+H],
\qquad
\alpha\in[\alpha_{\min},\alpha_{\max}].
\]

Purpose: test the real missing theorem:

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\Rightarrow
\max_{0\le r\le R}
|\Delta^r\partial_m^r q''_{\can}(m_0)|
\ge Q^{-B}.
\]

---

## Level 5 — Full AFE error validation

For any Level 4 candidate, verify that the differentiated AFE error satisfies:

\[
|I|^{-1}\int_I |E_2(m)|^2\,dm
\ll
|I|^{-1}\int_I |B_2+P_2+D_2|^2\,dm.
\]

If not, the candidate cannot be classified.

---

# 5. Search methods

## A. Direct interval scan over \(m\)

Compute \(\mathcal J_k(m)\) on a grid and identify local minima. Then refine using Newton, Levenberg–Marquardt, or quasi-Newton minimization.

Use this for Levels 1–3.

## B. Joint optimization over \((m,\alpha)\)

For Level 4, minimize

\[
\mathcal J_4(m,\alpha).
\]

Use multiple initial seeds:

- centers from low \(\mathcal J_3(m)\);
- Gram points;
- zero ordinates;
- random points;
- synthetic off-line centers.

## C. Log-scaled objective

Because one term can dominate, also minimize

\[
\widetilde{\mathcal J}_4(m,\alpha)
=
\log(|Z_\alpha(m)|^2+\varepsilon)
+
\sum_{r=0}^R
\log(|S_r(m)|^2+\varepsilon).
\]

This prevents the optimizer from ignoring some jet equations.

## D. Phase-relaxed control

As a diagnostic, replace

\[
e^{-im\log p}
\]

with independent phases

\[
z_p\in S^1.
\]

If phase-relaxed solutions are abundant but one-parameter solutions are absent, the actual prime-log orbit is the likely protective mechanism.

---

# 6. Success criteria for a surrogate threat

A surrogate candidate threatens Gate 1 only if all three conditions hold.

## 1. Jet flatness

\[
\max_{0\le r\le R}
|\Delta^r\partial_m^r q''_{\can}(m_0)|
\le Q^{-C}.
\]

## 2. Interval flatness

\[
E_I
=
|I|^{-1}\int_I |q''_{\can}(m)|^2\,dm
\le Q^{-C'}.
\]

## 3. Model stability

The candidate survives when moving from:

\[
\text{main only}
\to
\text{main + dual}
\to
\text{main + dual + background}
\to
\text{off-line center}
\to
\text{AFE error validation}.
\]

A candidate found only in Level 1 is not a serious threat. A candidate surviving Level 4 or Level 5 is serious.

---

# 7. Interpretation by level

| Result | Interpretation |
|---|---|
| Level 1 flat, Level 2 killed | Dual/\(\chi\)-term may be protective |
| Level 2 flat, Level 3 killed | Background shifts matter more than expected |
| Level 3 flat, Level 4 killed | Off-line center condition may provide rigidity |
| Level 4 flat, Level 5 unstable | AFE error too large to classify |
| Level 4/5 stable flat candidate | Gate 1 seriously threatened |
| Phase-relaxed flat, one-parameter not flat | Nonrecurrence of prime-log orbit is plausible |
| One-parameter flat without \(Z_\alpha\), not with \(Z_\alpha\) | Center condition is likely essential |

---

# 8. Recommended table schema

For each candidate:

| Field | Description |
|---|---|
| `level` | surrogate level 1–5 |
| `T` | height |
| `Q` | local scale |
| `m0` | center |
| `alpha` | off-line displacement if used |
| `Delta` | interval half-width |
| `R` | jet depth |
| `J_max` | \(\max_{r\le R}|S_r|\) |
| `J_l2` | \(\sum_{r\le R}|S_r|^2\) |
| `Z_abs` | \(|Z_\alpha(m_0)|\) |
| `E_I` | interval source energy |
| `B_eff` | \(-\log E_I/\log Q\) |
| `AFE_error` | interval AFE error |
| `status` | healthy / candidate / rejected / serious |
| `rejection_reason` | instability, AFE error, insufficient \(R\), etc. |

---

# 9. Final staged plan

1. Run Level 1 to see whether fixed actual amplitudes flatten at all.
2. Add dual/\(\chi\) and record whether candidates persist.
3. Add background and test whether it merely shifts targets.
4. Add \(Z_\alpha(m_0)=0\) and optimize over \((m,\alpha)\).
5. Validate interval energy \(E_I\).
6. Cross-check serious candidates against zero-side data where possible.

The key output should be a comparison table showing exactly where source-flat candidates disappear, if they disappear.

That table directly informs the missing theorem:

\[
\boxed{
\text{No simultaneous off-line-zero/source-flat finite-jet recurrence.}
}
\]
