## Agent 4 / D — AFE/fixed-prime surrogate pilot

### Objective

Build a staged surrogate pilot for Gate 1, measuring whether source-flat finite jets persist as the model becomes more actual-zeta-like. The target objective is

\[
\mathcal J(m_0,\alpha)
=
|Z_\alpha(m_0)|^2+
\sum_{r=0}^{R}
\left|
\Delta^r\partial_m^r q''_{\can}(m_0)
\right|^2.
\]

This directly follows the current execution plan: start with simplified fixed-prime/AFE-like models, add dual/background/off-line-center constraints, and record where source-flat candidates disappear. 

---

# 1. Shared definitions

Use an interval

\[
I=[m_0-\Delta,m_0+\Delta],
\qquad
\Delta=\frac{c_I}{Q}.
\]

For a surrogate source model \(F(m)\approx q''_{\can}(m)\), define scaled jets

\[
S_r(m_0)
=
\Delta^r F^{(r)}(m_0),
\qquad
0\le r\le R.
\]

The source-flat objective is

\[
\mathcal J_{\rm src}(m_0)
=
\sum_{r=0}^{R}|S_r(m_0)|^2.
\]

The interval validation is

\[
E_I(F)
=
|I|^{-1}\int_I |F(m)|^2\,dm.
\]

A finite-jet candidate is accepted only if interval flatness also holds.

Recommended pilot parameters:

\[
R\in\{6,8,10,12\},
\qquad
c_I\in\{0.1,0.2,0.5,1.0\},
\]

\[
Q=\log T,
\qquad
X\sim \sqrt{T/(2\pi)}
\]

or a smaller fixed-prime cutoff for early pilot runs.

---

# 2. Level 1 — Main fixed-prime source model only

## Model

Use

\[
P_2(m)
=
\Re\sum_{n\le X}a_n e^{-im\log n}.
\]

For a simplified first pilot, take

\[
a_n=(\log n)^2n^{-1/2}W(n/X),
\]

possibly with signs/phases adjusted to match the chosen completed-phase normalization. If testing prime-only behavior, restrict to \(n=p\):

\[
P_{2,p}(m)
=
\Re\sum_{p\le X}a_p e^{-im\log p}.
\]

## Variables

Only

\[
m_0\in[T,T+H].
\]

## Objective

\[
\mathcal J_1(m_0)
=
\sum_{r=0}^{R}
\left|
\Delta^r P_2^{(r)}(m_0)
\right|^2.
\]

Because

\[
P_2^{(r)}(m)
=
\Re\sum_{n\le X}a_n(-i\log n)^r e^{-im\log n},
\]

all derivatives can be computed analytically.

## Search method

Use a two-stage scan:

1. Coarse grid over \(m_0\in[T,T+H]\).
2. Local minimization from the best grid points using Brent, BFGS, or Levenberg–Marquardt.

## Success threshold

A Level 1 source-flat candidate satisfies

\[
\max_{0\le r\le R}
|\Delta^rP_2^{(r)}(m_0)|
\le Q^{-C}
\]

for a chosen exploratory \(C\), e.g.

\[
C=5,10.
\]

Then validate by computing

\[
E_I(P_2)\le Q^{-C'}.
\]

## Interpretation

If Level 1 has many flat candidates, fixed prime phases alone do not protect Gate 1. If Level 1 has no candidates, Gate 1 is numerically healthier than expected.

---

# 3. Level 2 — Main + dual/\(\chi\)-like term

## Model

Use

\[
F_2(m)=P_2(m)+D_2(m).
\]

A pilot dual model can be

\[
D_2(m)
=
\Re\left[
\chi_2(m)
\sum_{n\le Y}b_n e^{+im\log n}
\right],
\]

where \(\chi_2(m)\) represents the differentiated \(\chi\)- or theta-factor contribution. In the first implementation, use the exact AFE dual if available; otherwise use a documented proxy.

## Variables

\[
m_0\in[T,T+H].
\]

## Objective

\[
\mathcal J_2(m_0)
=
\sum_{r=0}^{R}
\left|
\Delta^r F_2^{(r)}(m_0)
\right|^2.
\]

Derivatives must include derivatives of \(\chi_2(m)\):

\[
\partial_m^rD_2(m)
=
\Re\sum_{j=0}^r
\binom{r}{j}
\chi_2^{(j)}(m)
\sum_{n\le Y}b_n(i\log n)^{r-j}e^{+im\log n}.
\]

## Search method

Start from Level 1 minima and re-optimize \(\mathcal J_2\). Also run independent coarse-grid scans to avoid bias.

## Success threshold

Same as Level 1:

\[
\max_{r\le R}|\Delta^rF_2^{(r)}(m_0)|\le Q^{-C},
\]

then validate

\[
E_I(F_2)\le Q^{-C'}.
\]

## Interpretation

If Level 1 candidates disappear at Level 2, the dual/\(\chi\)-coupling may provide real rigidity. If they survive, the functional equation alone is not enough.

---

# 4. Level 3 — Main + dual + background

## Model

\[
F_3(m)=B_2(m)+P_2(m)+D_2(m).
\]

Here \(B_2(m)\) is the differentiated gamma/background contribution.

## Variables

\[
m_0\in[T,T+H].
\]

## Objective

\[
\mathcal J_3(m_0)
=
\sum_{r=0}^{R}
\left|
\Delta^r F_3^{(r)}(m_0)
\right|^2.
\]

## Search method

Use Level 2 candidates as initial seeds. Also grid-search \(m\) because \(B_2\) can shift the flatness target.

## Success threshold

\[
\max_{r\le R}|\Delta^rF_3^{(r)}(m_0)|\le Q^{-C},
\]

and

\[
E_I(F_3)\le Q^{-C'}.
\]

## Interpretation

If candidates survive Level 3, deterministic gamma/background terms are only shifting the target, not preventing recurrence.

---

# 5. Level 4 — Add off-line-center proxy

## Model

Use Level 3 source model plus an off-line zero equation

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0.
\]

The pilot version should use the same AFE ingredients as Level 3:

\[
Z_\alpha(m)
=
Z_{\alpha,\main}(m)+Z_{\alpha,\dual}(m)+Z_{\alpha,\bg}(m).
\]

## Variables

\[
(m_0,\alpha)\in[T,T+H]\times[\alpha_{\min},\alpha_{\max}].
\]

Use several ranges, for example:

\[
\alpha\in[Q^{-C_\alpha},1/4],
\]

with logarithmic sampling near \(0\).

## Objective

\[
\mathcal J_4(m_0,\alpha)
=
|Z_\alpha(m_0)|^2+
\sum_{r=0}^{R}
\left|
\Delta^rF_3^{(r)}(m_0)
\right|^2.
\]

Also use a balanced log-objective:

\[
\widetilde{\mathcal J}_4(m_0,\alpha)
=
\log(|Z_\alpha(m_0)|^2+\varepsilon)
+
\sum_{r=0}^{R}
\log(|\Delta^rF_3^{(r)}(m_0)|^2+\varepsilon).
\]

This prevents the optimizer from making \(Z_\alpha\) small while ignoring source jets, or vice versa.

## Search method

Use three seed classes:

1. Level 3 source-flat candidates, then optimize \(\alpha\).
2. Approximate roots/minima of \(Z_\alpha(m)\), then optimize source jets.
3. Random \((m,\alpha)\) starts.

Recommended algorithms:

- Levenberg–Marquardt for squared residuals.
- BFGS or L-BFGS-B on the log-objective.
- Basin hopping or multi-start random search for rugged landscapes.

## Success threshold

A Level 4 candidate satisfies:

\[
|Z_\alpha(m_0)|\le Q^{-C_Z},
\]

and

\[
\max_{0\le r\le R}
|\Delta^rF_3^{(r)}(m_0)|
\le Q^{-C_S}.
\]

Then validate interval energy:

\[
E_I(F_3)\le Q^{-C_E}.
\]

---

# 6. Level 5 — AFE error validation

For Level 4 candidates, add error control.

A candidate is serious only if

\[
|I|^{-1}\int_I |E_2(m)|^2\,dm
\ll
E_I(F_3).
\]

If this fails, the candidate is numerically unresolved.

If possible, cross-check with the zero-side computation:

\[
\operatorname{Err}_I
=
|I|^{-1}\int_I
|q''_{\can,\zero}(m)-F_3(m)|^2\,dm.
\]

Require

\[
\operatorname{Err}_I\ll E_I.
\]

---

# 7. Pseudocode

```python
def source_model(level, m, params):
    if level == 1:
        return P2(m, params)
    if level == 2:
        return P2(m, params) + D2(m, params)
    if level >= 3:
        return B2(m, params) + P2(m, params) + D2(m, params)

def source_derivative(level, m, r, params):
    # analytic derivative, not finite difference
    return d_r_B2(m, r, params) + d_r_P2(m, r, params) + d_r_D2(m, r, params)

def source_jet_vector(level, m0, Delta, R, params):
    return [Delta**r * source_derivative(level, m0, r, params) for r in range(R+1)]

def J_source(level, m0, Delta, R, params):
    S = source_jet_vector(level, m0, Delta, R, params)
    return sum(abs(s)**2 for s in S)

def J_joint(m0, alpha, Delta, R, params):
    Z = Z_alpha(m0, alpha, params)
    S = source_jet_vector(3, m0, Delta, R, params)
    return abs(Z)**2 + sum(abs(s)**2 for s in S)

def interval_energy(level, m0, Delta, params, quad_nodes):
    nodes, weights = gauss_legendre_nodes_weights(quad_nodes, -Delta, Delta)
    vals = [source_model(level, m0+x, params) for x in nodes]
    return sum(w * abs(v)**2 for w, v in zip(weights, vals)) / (2*Delta)

def scan_level(level, T, H, Delta, R, params):
    grid = make_grid(T, T+H, params["grid_size"])
    candidates = []
    for m in grid:
        score = J_source(level, m, Delta, R, params)
        if score < params["preselect_threshold"]:
            m_refined = local_minimize(lambda x: J_source(level, x, Delta, R, params), m)
            E = interval_energy(level, m_refined, Delta, params, quad_nodes=200)
            candidates.append((m_refined, score, E))
    return candidates

def scan_level4(T, H, alpha_range, Delta, R, params, seeds):
    candidates = []
    for seed_m, seed_alpha in seeds:
        obj = lambda v: J_joint(v[0], v[1], Delta, R, params)
        m_ref, alpha_ref = local_minimize_2d(obj, [seed_m, seed_alpha], bounds=[(T,T+H), alpha_range])
        Z = abs(Z_alpha(m_ref, alpha_ref, params))
        S = source_jet_vector(3, m_ref, Delta, R, params)
        E = interval_energy(3, m_ref, Delta, params, quad_nodes=400)
        candidates.append({
            "m0": m_ref,
            "alpha": alpha_ref,
            "Z_abs": Z,
            "J_max": max(abs(s) for s in S),
            "J_l2": sum(abs(s)**2 for s in S),
            "E_I": E
        })
    return candidates
```

---

# 8. Candidate classification

For each candidate, record:

\[
J_{\max}=\max_{r\le R}|S_r|,
\]

\[
J_{\ell^2}=\sum_{r=0}^{R}|S_r|^2,
\]

\[
E_I=|I|^{-1}\int_I|F(m)|^2\,dm,
\]

\[
B_I^{\rm eff}=-\frac{\log E_I}{\log Q}.
\]

Classify:

| Status | Criteria |
|---|---|
| Healthy | \(J_{\max}\) and \(E_I\) not small |
| Jet-flat only | \(J_{\max}\) small, \(E_I\) not small |
| Source-flat candidate | \(J_{\max}\) small and \(E_I\) small |
| Joint candidate | source-flat plus \(|Z_\alpha|\) small |
| Serious Gate 1 threat | joint candidate survives Level 4/5 and AFE/zero-side validation |
| Rejected | unstable under \(R\), interval width, AFE error, or quadrature |

---

# 9. Interpretation of staged outcomes

| Outcome | Interpretation |
|---|---|
| Level 1 flat, Level 2 not flat | Dual/\(\chi\) likely protective |
| Level 2 flat, Level 3 not flat | Background shifts are significant |
| Level 3 flat, Level 4 not flat | Off-line center condition likely protective |
| Level 4 flat, Level 5 error too large | Cannot classify |
| Level 4/5 stable flat | Gate 1 seriously threatened |
| Relaxed phases flat, one-parameter flow not flat | Prime-log nonrecurrence plausible |
| One-parameter flow flat, but \(Z_\alpha\) prevents it | Off-line condition central |
| Actual zero-side healthy while AFE surrogates flatten | Actual zero-prime compatibility likely key |

---

# 10. Recommended pilot settings

Start modestly:

\[
R=6,\quad 8,\quad 10,
\]

\[
c_I=0.2,\quad0.5,\quad1.0,
\]

\[
T\in\{10^4,10^5,10^6\}
\]

if using manageable AFE approximations, or lower if precision is limiting.

Use multiple cutoffs:

\[
X=\sqrt{T/(2\pi)},\quad 0.5\sqrt{T/(2\pi)},\quad 2\sqrt{T/(2\pi)}
\]

as robustness checks, depending on the smoothing.

For each level, produce a table:

| level | T | Q | R | cI | m0 | alpha | J_max | J_l2 | Z_abs | E_I | B_eff | status |
|---|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|---|

The decisive output is a comparison across levels showing exactly where source-flat candidates disappear, if they disappear.

## Agent 4 / D — AFE/fixed-prime surrogate pilot refinement

### Objective

Build an executable staged surrogate experiment for Gate 1:

\[
\mathcal J_{\rm src}(m_0)
=
\sum_{r=0}^{R}
\left|
\Delta^r\partial_m^r q''_{\can}(m_0)
\right|^2,
\]

and, once the off-line-center condition is added,

\[
\mathcal J(m_0,\alpha)
=
|Z_\alpha(m_0)|^2
+
\sum_{r=0}^{R}
\left|
\Delta^r\partial_m^r q''_{\can}(m_0)
\right|^2.
\]

This should be run after the deterministic quadrature and singular controls validate that the pipeline can detect source-flattening. 

---

# 1. Immediate Level 1 model

Start with a deliberately simple fixed-prime model:

\[
F_1(m)=P_2(m)=\Re\sum_{p\le X} a_p e^{-im\log p}.
\]

Use

\[
a_p=(\log p)^2p^{-1/2}W(p/X),
\]

where \(W\) is a smooth cutoff, for example:

\[
W(y)=
\begin{cases}
\exp\left(-\frac{1}{1-y^2}\right), & 0\le y<1,\\
0, & y\ge1.
\end{cases}
\]

For an even simpler smoke test, use \(W\equiv1\) for \(p\le X\), then rerun with smoothing.

Derivative formula:

\[
F_1^{(r)}(m)
=
\Re\sum_{p\le X}
a_p(-i\log p)^r e^{-im\log p}.
\]

Scaled jet:

\[
S_r(m_0)=\Delta^rF_1^{(r)}(m_0).
\]

Objective:

\[
\mathcal J_1(m_0)=\sum_{r=0}^{R}|S_r(m_0)|^2.
\]

Recommended first settings:

\[
R\in\{6,8,10\},
\qquad
c_I\in\{0.2,0.5,1.0\},
\qquad
\Delta=c_I/Q,
\]

\[
T\in\{10^4,10^5,10^6\},
\qquad
Q=\log T,
\qquad
X\in\{100,300,1000,3000\}
\]

for a fast pilot before trying \(X\sim \sqrt{T/(2\pi)}\).

---

# 2. Coefficient choices by realism level

## Level 1A — Prime-only toy

\[
P_2^{(p)}(m)=
\Re\sum_{p\le X}
(\log p)^2p^{-1/2}W(p/X)e^{-im\log p}.
\]

Purpose: fast recurrence/small-ball test.

## Level 1B — von Mangoldt / prime powers

Use

\[
P_2^{(\Lambda)}(m)
=
\Re\sum_{n\le X}
\Lambda(n)(\log n)^2n^{-1/2}W(n/X)e^{-im\log n}.
\]

or, depending on the canonical AFE normalization,

\[
a_n=d_n(\log n)^2n^{-1/2}W(n/X),
\]

where \(d_n\) is the coefficient appropriate to the differentiated completed zeta expression.

Purpose: check whether prime powers materially change flattening.

## Level 1C — Smoothed AFE-like main term

\[
P_2^{\rm AFE}(m)
=
\Re\sum_{n\le X}
a_n(m)(-i\log n)^2 n^{-im}.
\]

If \(a_n(m)\) has slow \(m\)-dependence via smoothing, include amplitude derivatives:

\[
\partial_m^r\left(a_n(m)n^{-im}\right)
=
\sum_{j=0}^r
\binom{r}{j}
a_n^{(j)}(m)(-i\log n)^{r-j}n^{-im}.
\]

Purpose: make the model closer to the actual differentiated AFE.

---

# 3. Level 2: main + dual / \(\chi\)-like term

Define

\[
F_2(m)=P_2(m)+D_2(m).
\]

A simple dual proxy:

\[
D_2(m)=
\Re\left[
\chi_2(m)
\sum_{n\le Y}
b_n e^{+im\log n}
\right].
\]

Derivative:

\[
D_2^{(r)}(m)
=
\Re\sum_{j=0}^{r}
\binom{r}{j}
\chi_2^{(j)}(m)
\sum_{n\le Y} b_n(i\log n)^{r-j}e^{+im\log n}.
\]

Objective:

\[
\mathcal J_2(m_0)=
\sum_{r=0}^{R}
\left|
\Delta^rF_2^{(r)}(m_0)
\right|^2.
\]

Run Level 2 from Level 1 minima plus random starts.

Interpretation:

- If Level 1 candidates disappear here, the dual/\(\chi\) coupling may be protective.
- If they persist, functional-equation coupling alone is not enough.

---

# 4. Level 3: main + dual + background

Define

\[
F_3(m)=B_2(m)+P_2(m)+D_2(m).
\]

Objective:

\[
\mathcal J_3(m_0)=
\sum_{r=0}^{R}
\left|
\Delta^rF_3^{(r)}(m_0)
\right|^2.
\]

Use \(B_2(m)\) first as a slowly varying polynomial/logarithmic proxy if the exact gamma-background derivative is not yet wired in. Mark such runs as “background proxy.”

Interpretation:

- If candidates persist after \(B_2\), background is only shifting the target.
- If candidates vanish, verify this is not due to a normalization or scaling mismatch.

---

# 5. Level 4: add off-line-center condition

Add the proxy off-line zero condition:

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0.
\]

Objective:

\[
\mathcal J_4(m_0,\alpha)
=
|Z_\alpha(m_0)|^2
+
\sum_{r=0}^{R}
\left|
\Delta^rF_3^{(r)}(m_0)
\right|^2.
\]

Use a balanced log-objective for optimization:

\[
\widetilde{\mathcal J}_4(m_0,\alpha)
=
\log(|Z_\alpha(m_0)|^2+\varepsilon)
+
\sum_{r=0}^{R}
\log(|\Delta^rF_3^{(r)}(m_0)|^2+\varepsilon).
\]

Recommended \(\alpha\) range:

\[
\alpha\in[Q^{-8},0.25],
\]

sampled logarithmically near \(0\), then locally optimized.

Interpretation:

- If Level 3 candidates disappear only after adding \(Z_\alpha\), the off-line-center condition is doing real work.
- If candidates survive Level 4, Gate 1 is seriously threatened in realistic surrogates.

---

# 6. Optimization methods

Use multiple methods because the landscape will be oscillatory.

## One-dimensional levels

For Levels 1–3:

1. Coarse grid over \([T,T+H]\).
2. Preselect the lowest \(0.1\%\) by \(\mathcal J_k\).
3. Local refine using Brent or BFGS.
4. Validate interval energy.

Pseudocode:

```python
def jet_vector(F_deriv, m0, Delta, R):
    return [Delta**r * F_deriv(m0, r) for r in range(R + 1)]

def J_src(F_deriv, m0, Delta, R):
    S = jet_vector(F_deriv, m0, Delta, R)
    return sum(abs(s)**2 for s in S)

def scan_1d(F_deriv, T, H, Delta, R, n_grid, keep_frac):
    grid = linspace(T, T + H, n_grid)
    scores = [(m, J_src(F_deriv, m, Delta, R)) for m in grid]
    seeds = select_lowest(scores, keep_frac)
    out = []
    for m_seed, _ in seeds:
        m_ref = local_minimize(lambda m: J_src(F_deriv, m, Delta, R), m_seed)
        out.append((m_ref, J_src(F_deriv, m_ref, Delta, R)))
    return deduplicate(out)
```

## Two-dimensional Level 4

Use multi-start optimization over \((m,\alpha)\):

```python
def J_joint(m, alpha, Z_func, F_deriv, Delta, R):
    Z = Z_func(m, alpha)
    S = jet_vector(F_deriv, m, Delta, R)
    return abs(Z)**2 + sum(abs(s)**2 for s in S)

def J_joint_log(m, alpha, Z_func, F_deriv, Delta, R, eps):
    Z = Z_func(m, alpha)
    S = jet_vector(F_deriv, m, Delta, R)
    return log(abs(Z)**2 + eps) + sum(log(abs(s)**2 + eps) for s in S)
```

Seed classes:

- Level 3 minima;
- approximate \(Z_\alpha\)-minima;
- random \((m,\alpha)\);
- Gram/zero/gap-inspired \(m\)-centers.

---

# 7. Success/failure thresholds

Use exploratory thresholds first.

Let

\[
J_{\max}=\max_{0\le r\le R}|S_r|,
\qquad
J_2=\sum_{r=0}^{R}|S_r|^2.
\]

## Level candidate

\[
J_{\max}\le Q^{-5}
\]

for smoke tests.

## Strong surrogate candidate

\[
J_{\max}\le Q^{-10}
\]

and

\[
E_I(F_k)\le Q^{-10}.
\]

## Joint off-line candidate

\[
|Z_\alpha(m_0)|\le Q^{-8},
\qquad
J_{\max}\le Q^{-8},
\qquad
E_I(F_3)\le Q^{-8}.
\]

## Serious Gate 1 threat

A candidate survives:

\[
\text{Level 4}
\]

and, after AFE error validation,

\[
\operatorname{Err}_I\ll E_I.
\]

If only Level 1 or 2 candidates exist, classify as “surrogate-only.”

---

# 8. Interval energy validation

For any low-\(\mathcal J\) candidate, compute:

\[
E_I(F_k)=
|I|^{-1}\int_I |F_k(m)|^2\,dm.
\]

Use Gauss–Legendre or Clenshaw–Curtis quadrature.

Validate across interval widths:

\[
c_I\in\{0.1,0.2,0.5,1.0\}.
\]

Reject if flatness occurs only for one fragile width.

- healthy;
- jet-flat only;
- interval-flat;
- joint candidate;
- rejected;
- serious.

# 10. How to interpret disappearance of candidates

## Disappear at Level 2

The dual/\(\chi\)-like term is likely protective. Next theorem target:

\[
P_2\text{-flatness cannot persist under the functional equation dual coupling.}
\]

## Disappear at Level 3

Background/gamma terms are more rigid than expected. Verify normalization carefully; this could also indicate a bad proxy.

## Disappear at Level 4

This is the most important favorable outcome. It suggests:

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\]

prevents source-flat finite jets. Then the main theorem target becomes:

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\Rightarrow
\max_{r\le R}
|\Delta^r\partial_m^rq''_{\can}(m_0)|
\ge Q^{-B}.
\]

## Survive Level 4

Gate 1 is seriously threatened in realistic surrogates. Move immediately to:

1. interval-energy validation;
2. AFE error validation;
3. zero-side cross-check;
4. candidate classification by Agent 5 protocol.

---

This is **not actual-zeta evidence** yet; it is a harness validation and recurrence/proxy test. The current prompt explicitly asked for execution-oriented numerical/surrogate work rather than another strategy audit. 

## 1. Deterministic quadrature negative control

Used:

\[
\theta_j=\frac{j\pi}{N+1},
\qquad
w_j=\frac{2}{N+1}\sin\theta_j,
\qquad
N=R+3.
\]

This correctly enforces the sine-moment cancellations. In double precision, high-order jet checks become numerically ill-conditioned because factorials amplify \(10^{-15}\)-level moment error; high-precision arithmetic confirms the moments are zero to numerical precision.

| \(R\) | \(N\) | \(X_0\) | max flat moment error | \(E_X\) | \(S_X\) |
|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|
| 12 | 15 | 0.25 | \(3.85\times10^{-16}\) | \(2.22\times10^{-30}\) | \(1.13\times10^{-14}\) |
| 12 | 15 | 0.50 | \(3.85\times10^{-16}\) | \(9.68\times10^{-14}\) | \(2.32\times10^{-6}\) |
| 12 | 15 | 0.75 | \(3.85\times10^{-16}\) | \(1.94\times10^{-4}\) | \(9.91\times10^{-2}\) |
| 24 | 27 | 0.25 | \(1.61\times10^{-15}\) | \(2.83\times10^{-32}\) | \(5.60\times10^{-16}\) |
| 24 | 27 | 0.50 | \(1.61\times10^{-15}\) | \(2.10\times10^{-27}\) | \(4.66\times10^{-13}\) |
| 24 | 27 | 0.75 | \(1.61\times10^{-15}\) | \(1.31\times10^{-9}\) | \(3.60\times10^{-4}\) |
| 40 | 43 | 0.25 | \(2.17\times10^{-15}\) | \(1.26\times10^{-32}\) | \(3.30\times10^{-16}\) |
| 40 | 43 | 0.50 | \(2.17\times10^{-15}\) | \(1.02\times10^{-32}\) | \(3.33\times10^{-16}\) |
| 40 | 43 | 0.75 | \(2.17\times10^{-15}\) | \(5.66\times10^{-17}\) | \(9.61\times10^{-8}\) |

Interpretation: the negative control works. It produces severe source-curvature collapse on central intervals, especially for \(X_0\le 0.5\). For \(X_0=0.75\), flattening is weaker because the interval approaches the packet scale boundary.

## 2. Simplified fixed-prime / AFE-like surrogate pilot

Pilot settings:

\[
T=10^4,\quad H=200,\quad Q=\log T\approx 9.21,\quad X=300,\quad c_I=0.5,\quad \Delta=c_I/Q.
\]

Prime set: \(p\le300\).

Main source model:

\[
P_2(m)=\Re\sum_{p\le X}(\log p)^2p^{-1/2}W(p/X)e^{-im\log p}.
\]

I normalized jet residuals by their random-phase RMS scale, so \(J_{\max}\sim 1\) is ordinary and \(J_{\max}\ll1\) is flattened. \(E_{\rm norm}\) is interval energy normalized by the Level 0 source scale.

### \(R=6\)

| Level | Model | best \(m_0\) | \(J_{\max}\) | \(J_2\) | \(E_{\rm norm}\) | \(B_{\rm eff,norm}\) | Status |
|---:|---|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|---|
| 1 | main only | 10127.466 | 0.349 | 0.166 | \(5.56\times10^{-3}\) | 2.34 | mild valley |
| 2 | main + dual proxy | 10127.429 | 0.452 | 0.302 | \(2.54\times10^{-2}\) | 1.65 | not flat |
| 3 | + background proxy | 10127.427 | 0.452 | 0.305 | \(2.69\times10^{-2}\) | 1.63 | not flat |
| 4 | + \(Z_\alpha\) proxy | 10052.044 | 0.461 | 0.351 | \(6.79\times10^{-3}\) | — | \(Z\) small-ish, jets not flat |

Best Level 4 proxy candidate had:

\[
|Z_\alpha|_{\rm norm}\approx 0.077,\qquad
J_{\max}\approx0.461.
\]

So it is **not** a joint source-flat/off-line-center candidate.

### \(R=8\)

| Level | Model | best \(m_0\) | \(J_{\max}\) | \(J_2\) | \(E_{\rm norm}\) | \(B_{\rm eff,norm}\) | Status |
|---:|---|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|---|
| 1 | main only | 10052.233 | 0.319 | 0.183 | \(1.01\times10^{-2}\) | 2.07 | mild valley |
| 2 | main + dual proxy | 10052.845 | 0.400 | 0.320 | \(1.79\times10^{-2}\) | 1.81 | not flat |
| 3 | + background proxy | 10052.853 | 0.402 | 0.322 | \(1.71\times10^{-2}\) | 1.83 | not flat |
| 4 | + \(Z_\alpha\) proxy | 10052.047 | 0.461 | 0.361 | \(6.03\times10^{-3}\) | — | \(Z\) small-ish, jets not flat |

Best Level 4 proxy candidate had:

\[
|Z_\alpha|_{\rm norm}\approx 0.085,\qquad
J_{\max}\approx0.461.
\]

Again: **not a serious source-flat candidate**.

## 3. Interpretation

This pilot did **not** find a serious Gate 1-threatening surrogate candidate. It did find mild low-energy valleys in the simplified fixed-prime model, but the scaled jet vector did not become small enough to count as finite-jet source flatness.

Current outcome classification:

| Test | Result | Interpretation |
|---|---|---|
| Deterministic quadrature negative control | Passed strongly | Pipeline can detect the known adversary |
| Fixed-prime Level 1 | Mild valleys | Source flattening possible in weak form |
| Add dual/background proxies | Valleys persist but not worse | No strong rigidity signal yet |
| Add \(Z_\alpha\) proxy | No joint flat candidate | Favorable, but proxy too crude for conclusions |

## 4. Important caveats

This was **not** an actual AFE computation. Level 2–4 used proxy dual/background/\(Z_\alpha\) terms, not the fully normalized completed zeta AFE.

The negative control is meaningful; the surrogate pilot is only a smoke test.

## 3. First actual-zero proxy pilot

I attempted a high-\(T\) zero computation near \(T=10^4\), but computing enough zeros by `mpmath.zetazero` was too slow for the pilot run. I switched to a **low-height smoke test** using the first 100 computed critical-line zeros.

This pilot used the proxy kernel:

\[
K_2(m;\gamma,\varepsilon)
=
\frac{2\varepsilon(3(m-\gamma)^2-\varepsilon^2)}
{\left((m-\gamma)^2+\varepsilon^2\right)^3},
\qquad
\varepsilon=\kappa/Q.
\]

No \(B_2\), no canonical regularized tail. So this is explicitly **zero-kernel-only proxy data**.

Top low-energy intervals:

| center type | \(m_0\) | \(c_I\) | \(\kappa\) | \(E\) rank | \(S\) | \(B_{\rm eff}\) | \(J_{\max}\) |
|---|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|
| midpoint | 81.124 | 0.2 | 0.25 | best | 0.0715 | 3.57 | 0.0710 |
| midpoint | 81.124 | 0.5 | 0.25 | 2 | 0.0738 | 3.56 | 0.0710 |
| midpoint | 81.124 | 1.0 | 0.25 | 3 | 0.0827 | 3.50 | 0.0710 |
| midpoint | 54.708 | 0.2 | 0.25 | 4 | 0.0845 | 3.57 | 0.0838 |
| midpoint | 136.436 | 0.2 | 0.25 | 5 | 0.0851 | 3.10 | 0.0845 |
| random | 63.675 | 0.2 | 0.25 | watch | 0.106 | 3.31 | 0.0940 |

Interpretation: the zero-kernel proxy found low-ish intervals, mostly at gap midpoints, but not severe finite-jet collapse. The best cases have \(J_{\max}\approx0.07\), so they are not clean quadrature-like source-flat candidates.

## 5. What I would run next

The next run should improve fidelity, not just expand grids:

1. Replace the proxy \(Z_\alpha\) with the actual AFE off-line-center expression.
2. Add a true differentiated dual/\(\chi\) term instead of the current proxy.
3. Run the zero-side scan with a proper \(B_2\) and a documented regularized tail.
4. Compute zeros from a prepared zero table rather than on-demand `mpmath.zetazero`, which is too slow at \(T\sim10^4\).
5. Escalate candidates only if they have all three:
   \[
   E_I\text{ small},\quad J_{\max}\text{ small},\quad \text{stability under width/tail/quadrature changes}.
   \]

Current result: **no serious Gate 1 numerical threat found yet**, but the actual-zeta run is still only a proxy smoke test.

The best interval is stable under tail and quadrature refinement, but it is also sensitive to the artificial critical-line regularization width \(\varepsilon=\kappa/Q\). That makes it a useful **watch candidate**, not an actual source-flat candidate.

The next meaningful fidelity upgrade is now very specific:

1. replace the artificial \(\varepsilon\)-regularized critical-line kernel with the correct canonical treatment of critical-line zeros;
2. add the exact \(B_2\) term, not just the asymptotic proxy;
3. implement the completed/regularized tail;
4. only then rerun the same stability table.

## Agent 4 / D — Continued AFE/fixed-prime surrogate attack

I pushed the surrogate line one fidelity step further by replacing the earlier constant-phase dual proxy with an explicit approximate-functional-equation style model using the \(\chi\)-factor and its \(t\)-derivatives numerically. This is still **not canonical proof evidence**, but it is a stronger surrogate than the prior proxy. The current assignment is to continue execution work on the AFE/fixed-prime branch, not re-audit Gate 1. 

## 1. More faithful AFE-style surrogate

Used the approximate functional equation skeleton

\[
Z(t)\approx
\sum_{n\le N}n^{-1/2-it}
+
\chi(1/2+it)\sum_{n\le N}n^{-1/2+it},
\]

with

\[
\chi(s)=\pi^{s-1/2}\frac{\Gamma((1-s)/2)}{\Gamma(s/2)}.
\]

Then modeled the source curvature by

\[
F(t)\approx \Re\,\frac{d^2}{dt^2}Z(t),
\]

and computed source jets using

\[
S_r(t_0)=\Delta^r F^{(r)}(t_0)
=
\Delta^r\Re\, Z^{(r+2)}(t_0).
\]

This includes numerical derivatives of the \(\chi\)-factor, so it is closer to the actual AFE dual structure than the earlier constant-dual proxy.

Pilot settings:

\[
T=10^4,\quad H=200,\quad Q=\log T,\quad c_I=0.5,\quad R=6.
\]

AFE cutoff:

\[
N\approx \sqrt{T/(2\pi)}\approx 40.
\]

## 2. Source-jet scan result

I scanned \(t\in[10000,10200]\). Jet residuals were normalized by empirical RMS scale across the scan.

Best source-jet minima:

| \(t_0\) | \(J_{\max}\) | \(J_2\) | interval \(E_{\rm norm}\) | \(|Z_\alpha|_{\min}\) over \(\alpha\) | best \(\alpha\) |
|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|
| 10120.482 | 0.722 | 1.145 | \(1.32\times10^{-2}\) | 0.0931 | 0.0807 |
| 10011.245 | 0.544 | 1.179 | \(6.88\times10^{-2}\) | 0.396 | 0.25 |
| 10039.357 | 0.590 | 1.276 | \(4.64\times10^{-2}\) | 0.191 | 0.0708 |
| 10137.349 | 0.821 | 1.303 | \(2.47\times10^{-2}\) | 0.0970 | 0.01 |
| 10194.378 | 0.656 | 1.385 | \(1.95\times10^{-2}\) | 0.173 | 0.0309 |
| 10102.008 | 0.781 | 1.409 | not rerun | 0.0125 | \(5.62\times10^{-5}\) |
| 10012.048 | 0.591 | 1.423 | not rerun | 0.0207 | \(1.78\times10^{-4}\) |

## 3. Interpretation

No source-flat candidate appeared.

The best normalized jet residuals remain of order

\[
J_{\max}\approx 0.5\text{--}0.8,
\]

not near the quadrature-collapse regime. The interval energy minima were also only mild:

\[
E_{\rm norm}\sim 10^{-2}
\]

in the best checked case, not close to the deterministic same-scale quadrature negative control.

The off-line-center proxy sometimes becomes small, for example:

\[
|Z_\alpha|_{\min}\approx 0.0125
\]

near \(t_0=10102.008\), but those points did **not** have source-flat jets.

So the favorable pattern persists:

\[
Z_\alpha(t_0)\text{ small-ish}
\quad\not\Rightarrow\quad
q''_{\can}\text{ source-jet flat}.
\]

## 4. Current surrogate classification

| Branch | Result | Classification |
|---|---|---|
| Earlier fixed-prime large \(X\) runs | mild valleys only | watch, not threatening |
| AFE-style \(\chi\)-derivative surrogate | no source-flat jet vector | favorable |
| Off-line-center proxy | sometimes small, but jets remain live | favorable |
| Interval energy check | low-ish but not collapsed | no Gate 1 threat |

## 5. Limitations

This still does not settle the AFE branch because:

1. The approximate functional equation is a simplified truncation.
2. The exact canonical \(B_2\) is not yet inserted.
3. The exact \(q''_{\can}\) normalization from the paper is not fully encoded.
4. The scan is coarse and at one height band.
5. \(R=6\) is only a pilot jet depth.

## 6. Next attack step

The next worthwhile Agent 4 run is:

1. repeat this \(\chi\)-derivative AFE surrogate at \(T=10^5\) with \(N\approx126\);
2. run \(R=8\) if derivative cost remains manageable;
3. replace finite numerical \(\chi\)-derivatives with analytic/polygamma-based derivatives to improve speed and reliability;
4. compare the exact-\(\chi\) AFE surrogate against the earlier fixed-prime \(X=1000,3000,5000,10000\) runs.

Current verdict:

\[
\boxed{\text{No AFE/fixed-prime Gate 1 surrogate threat found yet.}}
\]

The evidence remains proxy-level but mildly favorable to Gate 1.

## 1. Model used

I used the surrogate approximate functional equation skeleton

\[

\sum_{n\le N} n^{-1/2-it}W(n/N)

\[

\]

and the source jets were

\[
S_r(t_0)=\Delta^r F^{(r)}(t_0)
=
\Delta^r\Re\,Z^{(r+2)}(t_0).
\]

\[

\]

I tested smoothing choices:

\[
\text{sharp},\quad \text{cosine},\quad \text{AFE-style taper},\quad \text{exponential}.
\]

Jet scores are RMS-normalized over the scan, so \(J_{\max}\sim 1\) is ordinary; a serious source-flat candidate would need \(J_{\max}\ll 1\) and stable interval energy collapse.

-\frac18\Re\psi^{(2)}\!\left(\frac14+\frac{it}{2}\right).
\]

For future numerical runs, \(B_2\) should be included by default in the zero-side object:

\[
q''_{\can}(m)=B_2(m)+\sum_\rho^{\rm reg}K_2(m;\rho).
\]

For speed, the approved 3-term approximation is:

\[
B_2(t)\approx
-\frac1{2t^2}
-\frac1{8t^4}
-\frac7{64t^6},
\]

which is essentially exact at the current pilot heights. I’ll treat \(B_2\) as unblocked; the remaining canonical zero-side blockers are now critical-line zero treatment / \(\eta\)-regularization and regularized tail completion.

Yes. Here is the **Agent 4 / D AFE-weight handoff** for Agent 5’s packet-frequency determinant script.

This matches the script’s current coefficient convention, where the main plateau first used

\[
c_p=\frac{(\log p)^4}{\sqrt p},
\qquad
z_p(\alpha)=\frac{\log p}{\sqrt p}p^{-\alpha},
\]

and the planned exact-like replacement was

\[
c_p=\frac{\log p}{\sqrt p}(\log p)^3V_q(p/N_q),
\qquad
z_p(\alpha)=\frac{\log p}{\sqrt p}p^{-\alpha}V_Z(p/N_Z).
\]

That is the convention Agent 5’s stress-test harness currently expects. 

---

## 1. Main branch weights

Let

\[
L_n=\log n,
\qquad
s_\alpha=\frac12+\alpha+im,
\qquad
N_q=N_q(m),
\qquad
N_Z=N_Z(m).
\]

For first implementation use

\[
N_q=N_Z=\sqrt{\frac{m}{2\pi}}.
\]

Let \(V_q,V_Z\) be smooth cutoffs. Then use:

\[
\boxed{
c_n^+
=
\frac{\Lambda(n)}{\sqrt n}\,L_n^3\,V_q(n/N_q)
}
\]

and

\[
\boxed{
z_n^+(\alpha)
=
\frac{\Lambda(n)}{\sqrt n}\,n^{-\alpha}\,V_Z(n/N_Z).
}
\]

For prime-only runs, \(\Lambda(p)=\log p\), so

\[
c_p^+=\frac{(\log p)^4}{\sqrt p}V_q(p/N_q),
\]

\[
z_p^+(\alpha)=\frac{\log p}{\sqrt p}p^{-\alpha}V_Z(p/N_Z).
\]

The associated phase is:

\[
u_n^+(m)=e^{-im\log n}.
\]

So the main branch contributes:

\[
c_n^+u_n^+(m),
\qquad
z_n^+(\alpha)u_n^+(m).
\]

---

## 2. Dual branch weights: exact-like \(\chi\)-derivative version

Use the dual phase:

\[
u_n^-(m)=e^{+im\log n}.
\]

For the off-line zero row:

\[
\boxed{
z_n^-(\alpha,m)
=
\chi\!\left(\frac12+\alpha+im\right)
\frac{\Lambda(n)}{\sqrt n}\,n^{+\alpha}\,V_Z^-(n/N_Z^-).
}
\]

For the \(q''\)-symbol row, use the third \(t\)-derivative symbol of the dual factor. Define

\[
s=\frac12+im,
\qquad
\chi_m=\chi(s),
\qquad
L_n=\log n.
\]

Let

\[
\ell_j(m):=\partial_m^j\log\chi\!\left(\frac12+im\right).
\]

Then

\[
\partial_m^3\!\left(\chi_m e^{imL_n}\right)
=
\chi_m e^{imL_n}\,
\mathcal B_3(\ell_1+iL_n,\ell_2,\ell_3),
\]

where

\[
\mathcal B_3(a,b,c)=a^3+3ab+c.
\]

So the actual-like dual \(q''\) symbol should be:

\[
\boxed{
c_n^-(m)
=
\frac{\Lambda(n)}{\sqrt n}\,
V_q^-(n/N_q^-)\,
\chi\!\left(\frac12+im\right)
\left[
(\ell_1+iL_n)^3
+
3(\ell_1+iL_n)\ell_2
+
\ell_3
\right].
}
\]

The dual contribution is then:

\[
c_n^-(m)e^{+imL_n}.
\]

For determinant tests that want real plateau-like magnitudes only, use

\[
|c_n^-(m)|
\]

as weights and keep the complex phase in the branch phase. For the canonical AFE surrogate, keep \(c_n^-(m)\) complex.

---

## 3. \(\chi\) and derivative formulas

Use

\[
\chi(s)
=
\pi^{s-\frac12}
\frac{\Gamma((1-s)/2)}{\Gamma(s/2)}.
\]

Let

\[
g(s)=\log\chi(s).
\]

Then

\[
g'(s)=
\log\pi
-\frac12\psi\!\left(\frac{1-s}{2}\right)
-\frac12\psi\!\left(\frac{s}{2}\right).
\]

For \(j\ge2\),

\[
g^{(j)}(s)
=
\left(-\frac12\right)^j
\psi^{(j-1)}\!\left(\frac{1-s}{2}\right)
-
\left(\frac12\right)^j
\psi^{(j-1)}\!\left(\frac{s}{2}\right).
\]

Since \(s=1/2+im\),

\[
\boxed{
\ell_j(m)=\partial_m^j\log\chi(1/2+im)
=
i^j g^{(j)}(1/2+im).
}
\]

Implementation:

```python
import mpmath as mp

def chi(s):
    return mp.power(mp.pi, s - mp.mpf("0.5")) * mp.gamma((1 - s) / 2) / mp.gamma(s / 2)

def g_deriv_chi_s(s, j):
    # g(s) = log chi(s)
    if j == 1:
        return (
            mp.log(mp.pi)
            - mp.mpf("0.5") * mp.digamma((1 - s) / 2)
            - mp.mpf("0.5") * mp.digamma(s / 2)
        )
    return (
        (-mp.mpf("0.5")) ** j * mp.polygamma(j - 1, (1 - s) / 2)
        - (mp.mpf("0.5")) ** j * mp.polygamma(j - 1, s / 2)
    )

def ell_chi_t(t, j):
    s = mp.mpf("0.5") + 1j * mp.mpf(t)
    return (1j ** j) * g_deriv_chi_s(s, j)

def bell3(a, b, c):
    return a**3 + 3*a*b + c

def dual_c_symbol(n, t, Vq=1.0, use_lambda=True):
    L = mp.log(n)
    lam_n = mp.log(n) if use_lambda else 1.0
    s = mp.mpf("0.5") + 1j * mp.mpf(t)
    ell1 = ell_chi_t(t, 1)
    ell2 = ell_chi_t(t, 2)
    ell3 = ell_chi_t(t, 3)
    return (
        lam_n / mp.sqrt(n)
        * Vq
        * chi(s)
        * bell3(ell1 + 1j * L, ell2, ell3)
    )
```

---

## 4. Node conventions

Use these node conventions for the determinant block.

### Main branch

\[
u_n^+=\log n,
\]

\[
x_n^+
=
\frac{2(\log n-u_0^+)}{L^+}.
\]

### Dual branch

For a formal dual branch, the simple convention is:

\[
u_n^-=\log n,
\qquad
x_n^-=
\frac{2(\log n-u_0^-)}{L^-}.
\]

For the actual-like AFE folded branch, use:

\[
\boxed{
v_n^-(m)=\log\frac{m}{2\pi n}
}
\]

and

\[
\boxed{
x_n^-(m)
=
\frac{2(v_n^-(m)-v_0^-)}{L^-}.
}
\]

The phase is still:

\[
e^{+im\log n}.
\]

So: **node is folded; phase remains dual.**

---

## 5. Recommended smoothing

For pilot runs use a simple \(C^\infty\) bump:

\[
V(y)=
\begin{cases}
\exp\!\left(-\frac{1}{1-y^2}\right), & 0\le y<1,\\
0, & y\ge1.
\end{cases}
\]

Normalize by dividing by \(V(0)\) if desired.

Python:

```python
def bump(y):
    y = float(y)
    if y < 0:
        return 0.0
    if y >= 1.0:
        return 0.0
    return float(mp.e ** (-1 / (1 - y*y)) / mp.e ** (-1))
```

For AFE-style runs, set:

\[
N_q=N_Z=\sqrt{\frac{m}{2\pi}}.
\]

Use the same \(V\) for plus and minus in the first actual-like pass:

\[
V_q^+=V_q^-=V_Z^+=V_Z^-=V.
\]

Later Agent 6 can replace this with the exact smoothed AFE weight.

---

## 6. Implementation object for Agent 5

Give Agent 5 this function shape:

```python
def build_afe_weights(n_values, t, alpha, branch, kind, smoothing="bump"):
    """
    branch: "plus" or "minus"
    kind: "source" or "zero"
      source => c_n^±
      zero   => z_n^±
    Returns:
      coeffs: complex np.ndarray
      phases: complex np.ndarray
      nodes: float np.ndarray
      weights_for_qr: float np.ndarray
    """
```

Core logic:

```python
import numpy as np
import mpmath as mp

def Lambda(n):
    # prime/power version; replace with exact factorization if needed
    # for prime-only run, n is prime and Lambda(n)=log(n)
    return mp.log(n)

def build_afe_weights(n_values, t, alpha, branch, kind, smoothing="bump"):
    t = mp.mpf(t)
    alpha = mp.mpf(alpha)
    N = mp.sqrt(t / (2 * mp.pi))

    coeffs = []
    phases = []
    nodes = []

    for n in n_values:
        nmp = mp.mpf(int(n))
        L = mp.log(nmp)
        V = bump(nmp / N)

        if branch == "plus":
            phase = mp.e ** (-1j * t * L)
            node = float(L)

            if kind == "source":
                coeff = Lambda(nmp) / mp.sqrt(nmp) * (L**3) * V
            elif kind == "zero":
                coeff = Lambda(nmp) / mp.sqrt(nmp) * (nmp ** (-alpha)) * V
            else:
                raise ValueError(kind)

        elif branch == "minus":
            phase = mp.e ** (+1j * t * L)
            node = float(mp.log(t / (2 * mp.pi * nmp)))  # folded node

            if kind == "source":
                coeff = dual_c_symbol(nmp, t, Vq=V, use_lambda=True)
            elif kind == "zero":
                s_alpha = mp.mpf("0.5") + alpha + 1j*t
                coeff = (
                    chi(s_alpha)
                    * Lambda(nmp) / mp.sqrt(nmp)
                    * (nmp ** alpha)
                    * V
                )
            else:
                raise ValueError(kind)
        else:
            raise ValueError(branch)

        coeffs.append(complex(coeff))
        phases.append(complex(phase))
        nodes.append(node)

    coeffs = np.array(coeffs, dtype=np.complex128)
    phases = np.array(phases, dtype=np.complex128)
    nodes = np.array(nodes, dtype=float)
    weights_for_qr = np.abs(coeffs) ** 2

    return coeffs, phases, nodes, weights_for_qr
```

---

## 7. What Agent 6 should audit

Agent 6 should check these four items:

1. Whether the determinant stress test should use \(\Lambda(n)\) or \(1\) in \(z_n^\pm\).  
   The current Agent 5 script uses \(\log p\), so \(\Lambda(n)\) is compatible.

2. Whether \(c_n^\pm\) should use third \(t\)-derivative symbols, as above, or a fourth-log plateau symbol.  
   The current script’s \(c_p=(\log p)^4/\sqrt p\) is \(\Lambda(p)(\log p)^3/\sqrt p\), so the third-derivative convention is compatible.

3. Whether the folded dual node

\[
x_n^-=\frac{2(\log(m/(2\pi n))-v_0^-)}{L^-}
\]

is correct for the packet-frequency block used in the determinant test.

4. Whether the smoothing \(V\) should be replaced by a true Mellin AFE weight before any red/yellow classification is trusted.

---

## 8. Minimal handoff summary

Use these as the first actual-like AFE weights:

\[
\boxed{

=
\frac{\Lambda(n)}{\sqrt n}(\log n)^3V_q(n/N_q)
}
\]

z_n^+(\alpha)
=
\frac{\Lambda(n)}{\sqrt n}n^{-\alpha}V_Z(n/N_Z)
}
\]

\[

c_n^-(m)
=
\frac{\Lambda(n)}{\sqrt n}V_q^-(n/N_q^-)
\chi\!\left(\frac12+im\right)
\mathcal B_3(\ell_1+i\log n,\ell_2,\ell_3)
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
z_n^-(\alpha,m)
=
\chi\!\left(\frac12+\alpha+im\right)
\frac{\Lambda(n)}{\sqrt n}n^\alpha V_Z^-(n/N_Z^-)
}
\]

with

\[
\mathcal B_3(a,b,c)=a^3+3ab+c,
\]

and

\[
\ell_j=\partial_m^j\log\chi(1/2+im).
\]

Use main phase \(e^{-im\log n}\), dual phase \(e^{+im\log n}\), main node \(\log n\), and folded dual node:

\[
\log\frac{m}{2\pi n}.
\]

This is the best current Agent 4 AFE-weight handoff.

Yes. The prior dual weights should be fixed by deriving the dual from the **log-derivative / phase object**, not from a value-level \(\chi(s)\zeta(1-s)\) AFE.

The audit’s objection is correct: my previous dual branch multiplied a value-style dual series by \(\chi(s)\), while the main branch used \(\Lambda(n)\)-type log-derivative coefficients. That mixes two different canonical objects. 

Below is the corrected handoff.

---

# 1. Canonical object for the determinant weights

Use

\[
A(s):=-\frac{\zeta'}{\zeta}(s).
\]

For \(k\ge0\), define the positive-log symbol

\[
C_k(s):=(-1)^k\partial_s^k A(s).
\]

Then, on the main side,

\[
C_k(s)
=
\sum_{n\ge1}\Lambda(n)(\log n)^k n^{-s}
\]

where the sum is interpreted through the chosen smoothing/truncation.

This convention matches Agent 5’s script style:

\[
c_p=\frac{(\log p)^4}{\sqrt p}
=
\frac{\Lambda(p)(\log p)^3}{\sqrt p},
\]

\[
z_p(\alpha)=\frac{\log p}{\sqrt p}p^{-\alpha}
=
\frac{\Lambda(p)}{\sqrt p}p^{-\alpha}
\quad (p\text{ prime}).
\]

---

# 2. Correct functional-equation dual for \(C_k\)

Let

\[
\zeta(s)=\chi(s)\zeta(1-s),
\]

so

\[
A(s)
=
-\frac{\chi'}{\chi}(s)-A(1-s).
\]

Let

\[
g(s):=\log\chi(s).
\]

Then the corrected reflected identity is:

\[
\boxed{
C_k(s)
=
\sigma_k\, g^{(k+1)}(s)
+
\sigma_k\, C_k(1-s),
\qquad
\sigma_k:=(-1)^{k+1}.
}
\]

Therefore the **canonical log-derivative dual branch is not multiplied by \(\chi(s)\)**. It is a reflected log-derivative sum, plus an additive gamma/background term.

For

\[
s=\frac12+\alpha+im,
\]

the reflected phase is

\[
n^{-(1-s)}
=
n^{-1/2+\alpha}e^{+im\log n}.
\]

So the dual coefficient for \(C_k\) is:

\[
\boxed{
c_{n,k}^-(\alpha)
=
\sigma_k\,
\Lambda(n)(\log n)^k
n^{-1/2+\alpha}
V_k^-(n/N_k^-).
}
\]

The phase is:

\[
\boxed{
u_n^-(m)=e^{+im\log n}.
}
\]

---

# 3. Corrected weights for Agent 5’s current script convention

Agent 5 currently has two relevant row types:

## Zero/incidence row

Current script convention:

\[
z_n^+(\alpha)
=
\frac{\Lambda(n)}{\sqrt n}n^{-\alpha}V_Z^+(n/N_Z^+).
\]

This corresponds to \(k_Z=0\), if no extra \(\log n\) is used, or \(k_Z=1\), if using the current prime-only \(\log p/\sqrt p\) row.

The script has been using the \(k_Z=1\) version. Then:

\[
\sigma_{k_Z}=\sigma_1=+1.
\]

So the corrected dual zero row is:

\[
\boxed{
z_n^-(\alpha)
=
+\frac{\Lambda(n)\log n}{\sqrt n}
n^{+\alpha}
V_Z^-(n/N_Z^-)
}
\]

for the \(k_Z=1\) script convention.

If Agent 5 switches to \(k_Z=0\), then:

\[
\boxed{
z_n^-(\alpha)
=
-\frac{\Lambda(n)}{\sqrt n}
n^{+\alpha}
V_Z^-(n/N_Z^-).
}
\]

## Source row

For the current determinant script, the source row uses:

\[
c_n^+
=
\frac{\Lambda(n)}{\sqrt n}(\log n)^3V_q^+(n/N_q^+).
\]

This is \(k_q=3\). Since

\[
\sigma_3=+1,
\]

the corrected dual source row is:

\[
\boxed{
c_n^-(\alpha=0)
=
+\frac{\Lambda(n)}{\sqrt n}(\log n)^3V_q^-(n/N_q^-).
}
\]

The phase is:

\[
e^{+im\log n}.
\]

If instead we want the literal Gate 1 \(q''_{\can}\) source coefficient, then \(k_q=2\), not \(3\). In that case:

\[
\sigma_2=-1,
\]

and

\[
\boxed{
c_{n,q''}^-
=
-\frac{\Lambda(n)}{\sqrt n}(\log n)^2V_q^-(n/N_q^-).
}
\]

This distinction is important:

\[
\boxed{
k_q=3 \text{ matches Agent 5’s current Wronskian/script convention;}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
k_q=2 \text{ matches literal }q''_{\can}\text{ source curvature.}
}
\]

---

# 4. Background / gamma term

The reflected log-derivative identity contributes an additive background

\[
\sigma_k g^{(k+1)}(s),
\qquad
g(s)=\log\chi(s).
\]

For the actual Gate 1 source curvature, the background has already been canonicalized as:

\[
\boxed{
B_2(t)=\theta'''(t)
=
-\frac18\Re\psi^{(2)}\!\left(\frac14+\frac{it}{2}\right).
}
\]

This is finalized and should be included by default. 

For Agent 5’s determinant stress test, keep \(B_2\) as the canonical \(q''_{\can}\) background, not as a value-AFE \(\chi(s)\)-multiplied dual term.

}

\frac{2(\log n-u_0^-)}{L^-}.
\]

For folded actual-like geometry:

\[
\boxed{
x_n^-(m)
=
\frac{2\left(\log\frac{m}{2\pi n}-v_0^-\right)}{L^-}.
}
\]

The folded node is still useful for stress testing, but the **coefficient is now log-derivative reflected**, not \(\chi(s)\)-multiplied value-style.

# 6. Corrected implementation function

Here is the revised implementation for Agent 5.

```python
import numpy as np
import math

def Lambda_prime_only(n):
    # For prime-only runs, n is assumed prime.
    return math.log(n)

def sigma_k(k: int) -> int:
    return -1 if (k % 2 == 0) else 1
    # sigma_k = (-1)^(k+1)

def smooth_bump(y: float) -> float:
    if y < 0 or y >= 1:
        return 0.0
    return math.exp(-1.0 / (1.0 - y*y)) / math.exp(-1.0)

def build_logderiv_afe_weights(
    n_values,
    m,
    alpha,
    branch,
    k,
    N,
    use_prime_only=True,
    smoothing="bump",
    folded_dual_node=True,
):
    """
    Canonical log-derivative / phase-like AFE weights for C_k(s).

    C_k(s) := (-1)^k d_s^k[-zeta'/zeta](s).

    Main:
        + Lambda(n) (log n)^k n^(-1/2-alpha) e^(-i m log n)

    Dual:
        sigma_k Lambda(n) (log n)^k n^(-1/2+alpha) e^(+i m log n)

    sigma_k = (-1)^(k+1)

    No chi(s) multiplier appears in the dual coefficient.
    """

    coeffs = []
    phases = []
    nodes = []

    for n in n_values:
        n = int(n)
        L = math.log(n)
        Lam = Lambda_prime_only(n) if use_prime_only else von_mangoldt(n)

        y = n / N
        V = smooth_bump(y) if smoothing == "bump" else 1.0

        if branch == "plus":
            coeff = Lam * (L ** k) * (n ** (-0.5 - alpha)) * V
            phase = np.exp(-1j * m * L)
            node = L

        elif branch == "minus":
            coeff = sigma_k(k) * Lam * (L ** k) * (n ** (-0.5 + alpha)) * V
            phase = np.exp(+1j * m * L)

            if folded_dual_node:
                node = math.log(m / (2.0 * math.pi * n))
            else:
                node = L
        else:
            raise ValueError(branch)

        coeffs.append(complex(coeff))
        phases.append(complex(phase))
        nodes.append(float(node))

    coeffs = np.array(coeffs, dtype=np.complex128)
    phases = np.array(phases, dtype=np.complex128)
    nodes = np.array(nodes, dtype=float)
    weights_for_qr = np.abs(coeffs) ** 2

    return coeffs, phases, nodes, weights_for_qr
```

For Agent 5’s current convention:

```python
# zero/incidence row, current script convention
z_plus, phase_plus, node_plus, w_z_plus = build_logderiv_afe_weights(
    n_values, m, alpha, branch="plus", k=1, N=N_Z
)

z_minus, phase_minus, node_minus, w_z_minus = build_logderiv_afe_weights(
    n_values, m, alpha, branch="minus", k=1, N=N_Z
)

# source row, current script convention
c_plus, phase_plus, node_plus, w_c_plus = build_logderiv_afe_weights(
    n_values, m, 0.0, branch="plus", k=3, N=N_q
)

c_minus, phase_minus, node_minus, w_c_minus = build_logderiv_afe_weights(
    n_values, m, 0.0, branch="minus", k=3, N=N_q
)
```

For literal \(q''_{\can}\) tests, use:

```python
# literal Gate 1 q'' source curvature
c_plus_q2, _, _, _ = build_logderiv_afe_weights(
    n_values, m, 0.0, branch="plus", k=2, N=N_q
)

c_minus_q2, _, _, _ = build_logderiv_afe_weights(
    n_values, m, 0.0, branch="minus", k=2, N=N_q
)
```

\]

\[
c_n^-(m)

=
\sigma_k

\boxed{
c_{n,k}^-
=
\sigma_k
\Lambda(n)(\log n)^k
n^{-1/2}V_q^-.
}
\]

No \(\chi(s)\) multiplier.

The \(\chi\)-derivatives belong to the additive background/gamma side of the completed log-derivative identity, not as a multiplicative dual coefficient.

## Corrected node convention

The folded node

\[
\log\frac{m}{2\pi n}
\]

is useful as a **dual-conductor diagnostic**, but it should not be used as the Wronskian differential/operator node unless a new folded operator is explicitly defined.

For the determinant/Wronskian operator, the node should track the eigenvalue of \(\lambda\partial_m\).

Use:

\[
\boxed{
\text{main operator node: } \quad +\log n
}
\]

and, under the real signed-frequency convention,

\[
\boxed{
\text{dual operator node: } \quad -\log n.
}
\]

Keep the folded node separately:

\[
\boxed{
\text{dual folded diagnostic node: }
\log\frac{m}{2\pi n}.
}
\]

That means Agent 5’s data structure should carry both:

```python
op_node       # used in the Wronskian/basis matrix
folded_node   # diagnostic only
```

---

## Corrected implementation core

```python
def sigma_k(k: int) -> int:
    # sigma_k = (-1)^(k+1)
    return -1 if (k % 2 == 0) else 1

def build_logderiv_weights(
    n_values,
    m,
    alpha,
    branch,
    k,
    N,
    smoothing,
    lambda_func,
    signed_operator_nodes=True,
):
    """
    Log-derivative / phase-consistent reflected weights.

    C_k(s) = (-1)^k d_s^k[-zeta'/zeta](s)

    plus branch:
        coeff = Lambda(n) (log n)^k n^(-1/2-alpha) V
        phase = exp(-i m log n)

    minus branch:
        coeff = sigma_k Lambda(n) (log n)^k n^(-1/2+alpha) V
        phase = exp(+i m log n)

    For Agent 5's current script:
        k_Z = 0
        k_q = 3

    For literal q''_can:
        k_q = 2
    """
    coeffs = []
    phases = []
    op_nodes = []
    folded_nodes = []

    for n in n_values:
        n = int(n)
        L = math.log(n)
        Lam = lambda_func(n)
        V = smoothing(n / N)

        if branch == "plus":
            coeff = Lam * (L ** k) * (n ** (-0.5 - alpha)) * V
            phase = np.exp(-1j * m * L)

            # operator node: eigenvalue convention for exp(-i m log n)
            op_node = +L if signed_operator_nodes else L
            folded_node = L

        elif branch == "minus":
            coeff = sigma_k(k) * Lam * (L ** k) * (n ** (-0.5 + alpha)) * V
            phase = np.exp(+1j * m * L)

            # operator node: signed frequency of exp(+i m log n)
            op_node = -L if signed_operator_nodes else L

            # diagnostic only; do not use as Wronskian operator node
            folded_node = math.log(m / (2.0 * math.pi * n))

        else:
            raise ValueError(branch)

        coeffs.append(complex(coeff))
        phases.append(complex(phase))
        op_nodes.append(float(op_node))
        folded_nodes.append(float(folded_node))

    coeffs = np.array(coeffs, dtype=np.complex128)
    phases = np.array(phases, dtype=np.complex128)
    op_nodes = np.array(op_nodes, dtype=float)
    folded_nodes = np.array(folded_nodes, dtype=float)
    weights_for_qr = np.abs(coeffs) ** 2

    return coeffs, phases, op_nodes, folded_nodes, weights_for_qr
```

Usage for the current script convention:

```python
# zero/incidence row: k_Z = 0
z_plus, phase_zp, node_zp, folded_zp, w_zp = build_logderiv_weights(
    n_values=n_values,
    m=m,
    alpha=alpha,
    branch="plus",
    k=0,
    N=N_Z_plus,
    smoothing=V_Z_plus,
    lambda_func=Lambda,
)

z_minus, phase_zm, node_zm, folded_zm, w_zm = build_logderiv_weights(
    n_values=n_values,
    m=m,
    alpha=alpha,
    branch="minus",
    k=0,
    N=N_Z_minus,
    smoothing=V_Z_minus,
    lambda_func=Lambda,
)

# current Wronskian/source row: k_q = 3
c_plus, phase_cp, node_cp, folded_cp, w_cp = build_logderiv_weights(
    n_values=n_values,
    m=m,
    alpha=0.0,
    branch="plus",
    k=3,
    N=N_q_plus,
    smoothing=V_q_plus,
    lambda_func=Lambda,
)

c_minus, phase_cm, node_cm, folded_cm, w_cm = build_logderiv_weights(
    n_values=n_values,
    m=m,
    alpha=0.0,
    branch="minus",
    k=3,
    N=N_q_minus,
    smoothing=V_q_minus,
    lambda_func=Lambda,
)
```

Usage for literal \(q''_{\can}\):

```python
# literal q''_can source row: k_q = 2
c_plus_q2, phase_cp, node_cp, folded_cp, w_cp = build_logderiv_weights(
    n_values=n_values,
    m=m,
    alpha=0.0,
    branch="plus",
    k=2,
    N=N_q_plus,
    smoothing=V_q_plus,
    lambda_func=Lambda,
)

c_minus_q2, phase_cm, node_cm, folded_cm, w_cm = build_logderiv_weights(
    n_values=n_values,
    m=m,
    alpha=0.0,
    branch="minus",
    k=2,
    N=N_q_minus,
    smoothing=V_q_minus,
    lambda_func=Lambda,
)
```

---

## \(B_2\) correction

Use the canonical real phase-curvature background:

\[
\boxed{
B_2(t)=\theta'''(t)
=
-\frac18\Re\psi^{(2)}\left(\frac14+\frac{it}{2}\right).
}
\]

This is correct for literal \(q''_{\can}\). For complex \(C_k(s)\)-row stress tests, the matching background is instead:

\[
\boxed{
\sigma_k g^{(k+1)}(s)
}
\]

with the chosen real/imaginary projection applied afterward.

So in code:

- literal \(q''_{\can}\) row: use \(B_2(t)\);
- complex \(C_k\) determinant row: use \(\sigma_k g^{(k+1)}(s)\), not necessarily \(B_2\) directly.

---

## Final approval status

Approved for Agent 5 as a serious **log-derivative surrogate** after these fixes:

\[
\boxed{k_Z=0}
\]

\[
\boxed{z_n^-=-\Lambda(n)n^{-1/2+\alpha}V_Z^-}
\]

\[
\boxed{\text{operator node } \neq \text{ folded conductor node}}
\]

Still not final proof-level canonical until smoothing and derivative/error conventions are fixed:

\[
V^\pm,\quad N^\pm(m),\quad \partial_m V^\pm,\quad E_2,\quad \text{real/phase projection}.
\]

But the major convention mismatch is now resolved.
